the blow-up alternative requires this quantity to be unbounded.  Hence
\(\tau(D)=T\).

It remains to prove continuity with constants that are uniform on \(K\).
Compactness of \(K\) gives a finite noise bound
\[
  M_{K,T}:=
  \sup_{D\in K}\sum_{j=1}^3
  \|\mathbb X_j\|_{C([0,T];\mathcal C^{-\kappa})}
  <\infty .
\]
Inspecting the contraction estimate in
Theorem~\ref{thm:spde-dpd-besov-local-fixed-point}, one obtains a time
\(\delta>0\) and a constant \(L<\infty\), depending only on
\(B_{K,T}\), \(M_{K,T}\), \(T\), and the fixed exponents, with the following
property.  If two solutions are known on a time interval beginning at
\(t_0\) and both remainders have \(\mathcal C^\alpha\)-norm at most
\(B_{K,T}\), then on
\([t_0,t_0+\delta]\cap[0,T]\)
\[
  \|Y_D-Y_{\widetilde D}\|_
  {C([t_0,t_0+\delta]\cap[0,T];\mathcal C^\alpha)}
  \leq
  L\Big(
    \|Y_D(t_0)-Y_{\widetilde D}(t_0)\|_{\mathcal C^\alpha}
    + d_{\mathfrak D_T}(D,\widetilde D)
  \Big),
\]
where \(d_{\mathfrak D_T}\) is any metric inducing the product topology on
bounded subsets of \(\mathfrak D_T\).  The same \(\delta\) works at every
\(t_0\) because the heat-kernel estimates depend only on the length of the
interval, while the nonlinear estimates depend only on the preceding
uniform bounds.

Choose an integer \(m\) with \(m\delta\geq T\).  Iterating the last estimate
over the grid \(0,\delta,2\delta,\ldots,m\delta\) gives, for \(D\) and
\(\widetilde D\) sufficiently close in \(K\),
\[
  \|Y_D-Y_{\widetilde D}\|_{C([0,T];\mathcal C^\alpha)}
  \leq C_{K,T}\,d_{\mathfrak D_T}(D,\widetilde D)
\]
with finite \(C_{K,T}\).  Thus \(\mathcal S_T\) is continuous at each point
of \(K\), and compactness of \(K\) upgrades pointwise continuity to uniform
continuity.  The convergence statement is the preceding uniform-continuity
claim applied to the compact set containing the tail of the sequence and
its limit.
\end{proof}

This criterion separates a soft continuation argument from the genuinely
hard stochastic estimate.  Once the local Besov theory is known, global
cutoff convergence on compact enhanced-noise sets is reduced to proving a
rough energy-to-Besov a priori bound.  The latter is precisely where the
Wick-renormalized coercivity of the two-dimensional equation must enter.

\begin{proposition}[Local rough-forcing bootstrap for the energy-to-Besov step]
\label{prop:spde-dpd-rough-forcing-bootstrap}
Keep the notation and exponents of
Theorem~\ref{thm:spde-dpd-besov-local-fixed-point}, and put
\[
  \theta=\frac{\alpha+\kappa}{2}\in(0,1),
  \qquad A=\Delta-m^2 .
\]
Let \(C_0\) and \(C_1\) be constants such that, for all
\(0\leq t\leq1\) and all intervals \(I\) of length at most \(1\),
\begin{equation}
  \|e^{tA}f\|_{\mathcal C^\alpha}
  \leq C_0\|f\|_{\mathcal C^\alpha},
  \qquad
  \left\|\int_{t_0}^t e^{(t-s)A}F(s)\,\dd s
  \right\|_{C(I;\mathcal C^\alpha)}
  \leq
  C_1 |I|^{1-\theta}\|F\|_{C(I;\mathcal C^{-\kappa})}.
  \label{eq:spde-rough-forcing-bootstrap-semigroup}
\end{equation}
Let \(Y\in C([0,T];\mathcal C^\alpha)\) solve the Besov mild equation
\eqref{eq:spde-dpd-besov-mild-equation} on \([0,T]\).  Choose a partition
\[
  0=t_0<t_1<\cdots<t_M=T,
  \qquad I_\ell=[t_\ell,t_{\ell+1}],
  \qquad |I_\ell|\leq\delta\leq1 .
\]
Assume that on every \(I_\ell\) the renormalized DPD nonlinearity satisfies
a local rough-forcing estimate
\begin{equation}
  \|\mathcal N_{\mathcal C}(Y,\mathbb X)\|_{C(I_\ell;\mathcal C^{-\kappa})}
  \leq A_\ell+\varepsilon
  \|Y\|_{C(I_\ell;\mathcal C^\alpha)}
  \label{eq:spde-local-rough-forcing-estimate}
\end{equation}
with \(A_\ell\geq0\) and
\begin{equation}
  |\lambda|C_1\delta^{1-\theta}\varepsilon\leq \frac12 .
  \label{eq:spde-rough-forcing-absorption-condition}
\end{equation}
Then, writing
\[
  D_0=
  2C_0\|Y(0)\|_{\mathcal C^\alpha}
  +2|\lambda|C_1\delta^{1-\theta}A_0,
\]
and recursively
\[
  D_\ell=
  2C_0D_{\ell-1}
  +2|\lambda|C_1\delta^{1-\theta}A_\ell,
  \qquad 1\leq \ell\leq M-1,
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
  \|Y\|_{C(I_\ell;\mathcal C^\alpha)}\leq D_\ell,
  \qquad 0\leq\ell\leq M-1.
  \label{eq:spde-rough-forcing-bootstrap-recursive-bound}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
  \|Y\|_{C([0,T];\mathcal C^\alpha)}
  \leq
  (2C_0)^M\|Y(0)\|_{\mathcal C^\alpha}
  +
  2|\lambda|C_1\delta^{1-\theta}
  \sum_{j=0}^{M-1}(2C_0)^{M-1-j}A_j .
  \label{eq:spde-rough-forcing-bootstrap-explicit-bound}
\end{equation}
In particular, if the numbers \(A_\ell\) are bounded uniformly on a compact
set of enhanced noises and initial conditions, and if the same
\(\delta,\varepsilon\) satisfy
\eqref{eq:spde-rough-forcing-absorption-condition} throughout that compact
set, then the rough energy-to-Besov hypothesis in
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-dpd-global-compact-continuity-criterion} follows.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For \(t\in I_\ell\), the mild equation restarted at time \(t_\ell\) is
\begin{equation}
  Y(t)
  =
  e^{(t-t_\ell)A}Y(t_\ell)
  -
  \lambda
  \int_{t_\ell}^t
  e^{(t-s)A}
  \mathcal N_{\mathcal C}(Y(s),\mathbb X(s))\,\dd s .
  \label{eq:spde-rough-forcing-restarted-mild}
\end{equation}
Taking the \(C(I_\ell;\mathcal C^\alpha)\) norm and using
\eqref{eq:spde-rough-forcing-bootstrap-semigroup} gives
\[
  R_\ell
  \leq
  C_0\|Y(t_\ell)\|_{\mathcal C^\alpha}
  +|\lambda|C_1\delta^{1-\theta}
  \|\mathcal N_{\mathcal C}(Y,\mathbb X)\|_
    {C(I_\ell;\mathcal C^{-\kappa})},
  \qquad
  R_\ell:=\|Y\|_{C(I_\ell;\mathcal C^\alpha)} .
\]
Insert the rough-forcing estimate
\eqref{eq:spde-local-rough-forcing-estimate}.  The absorption condition
\eqref{eq:spde-rough-forcing-absorption-condition} implies
\begin{equation}
  R_\ell
  \leq
  2C_0\|Y(t_\ell)\|_{\mathcal C^\alpha}
  +2|\lambda|C_1\delta^{1-\theta}A_\ell .
  \label{eq:spde-rough-forcing-single-step}
\end{equation}
For \(\ell=0\) this is exactly \(R_0\leq D_0\).  If \(\ell\geq1\), then
\(\|Y(t_\ell)\|_{\mathcal C^\alpha}\leq R_{\ell-1}\).  Induction using
\eqref{eq:spde-rough-forcing-single-step} proves
\eqref{eq:spde-rough-forcing-bootstrap-recursive-bound}.  Iterating the
recursion for \(D_\ell\) gives the explicit bound
\eqref{eq:spde-rough-forcing-bootstrap-explicit-bound}.  The compact-set
consequence follows by taking the supremum of the right hand side over the
compact family.
\end{proof}

The preceding proposition makes the remaining analytic obligation precise.
The phrase ``rough energy-to-Besov bound'' means a proof of
\eqref{eq:spde-local-rough-forcing-estimate} with \(A_\ell\) controlled by
the coercive energy estimates, by the enhanced-noise norms, and by no
unabsorbed positive power of
\(\|Y\|_{C(I_\ell;\mathcal C^\alpha)}\).  Once such a local estimate is
proved, the conversion to the global Besov bound is the elementary
parabolic bootstrap above.

\begin{lemma}[Passing invariance through a cutoff limit]
\label{lem:spde-invariant-measure-limit}
Let \(E\) be a Polish space, let \(P_t^{(n)}\) and \(P_t\) be Markov
semigroups on bounded continuous functions on \(E\), and let
\(\mu_n\) be an invariant probability measure for \(P_t^{(n)}\).  Suppose
\(\mu_n\Rightarrow\mu\) weakly and that, for every bounded continuous
function \(f\) and every fixed \(t\geq0\),
\[
  P_t^{(n)}f\longrightarrow P_tf
  \quad\hbox{uniformly on compact subsets of }E .
\]
Assume also that \(\{\mu_n\}\) is tight and that the convergence above is
uniform on a compact set whose \(\mu_n\)-mass is arbitrarily close to one,
uniformly in \(n\).  Then \(\mu\) is invariant for \(P_t\):
\[
  \int_E P_tf\,\dd\mu=\int_E f\,\dd\mu .
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Fix \(f\in C_b(E)\), \(t\geq0\), and \(\eta>0\).  Choose a compact set
\(K\subset E\) such that \(\mu_n(K)\ge 1-\eta\) for all sufficiently large
\(n\) and such that the convergence \(P_t^{(n)}f\to P_tf\) is uniform on
this same \(K\).  The latter requirement is not implied by tightness alone;
it is the high-probability compact-set convergence hypothesis in the
statement.  Since Markov semigroups are contractions on bounded functions,
\[
  \|P_t^{(n)}f\|_\infty\le \|f\|_\infty,
  \qquad
  \|P_tf\|_\infty\le \|f\|_\infty .
\]
Therefore
\[
  \left|
    \int P_t^{(n)}f\,\dd\mu_n
    -
    \int P_tf\,\dd\mu_n
  \right|
  \leq
  \sup_{x\in K}|P_t^{(n)}f(x)-P_tf(x)|
  +2\|f\|_\infty\eta ,
\]
which tends to at most \(2\|f\|_\infty\eta\).  Letting \(\eta\downarrow0\)
gives
\[
  \int P_t^{(n)}f\,\dd\mu_n
  -
  \int P_tf\,\dd\mu_n
  \longrightarrow0 .
\]
The limiting semigroup is assumed to map \(C_b(E)\) to \(C_b(E)\), so weak
convergence of \(\mu_n\) gives
\[
  \int P_tf\,\dd\mu_n\longrightarrow \int P_tf\,\dd\mu .
\]
The cutoff invariance gives
\[
  \int P_t^{(n)}f\,\dd\mu_n=\int f\,\dd\mu_n,
\]
and weak convergence also gives
\[
  \int f\,\dd\mu_n\longrightarrow \int f\,\dd\mu .
\]
Combining the three limits yields
\[
  \int P_tf\,\dd\mu=\int f\,\dd\mu .
\]
Since \(f\) and \(t\) were arbitrary, \(\mu\) is invariant for the limiting
Markov semigroup.
\end{proof}

For singular SPDE, the hypotheses of
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-invariant-measure-limit} are not automatic.
They require tightness of the stationary cutoff laws in the chosen field
topology, convergence of the renormalized solution maps on high-probability
compact sets of enhanced noises and initial data, and continuity of the
limiting Markov semigroup on the same topology.  This is the exact
invariant-law step that sits between cutoff Langevin stationarity and a
Euclidean measure for QFT.

\begin{lemma}[Sobolev compactness criterion for cutoff-field tightness]
\label{lem:spde-sobolev-compactness-tightness}
Let \(0<\eta<\kappa\), \(p>0\), and let \(\{\nu_N\}\) be Borel probability
measures on \(H^{-\kappa}(\mathbb T^2)\).  Suppose that each \(\nu_N\) is
carried by \(H^{-\eta}(\mathbb T^2)\) and that
\begin{equation}
  \sup_N
  \int
  \|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^p\,\dd\nu_N(\phi)
  \leq C
  <\infty .
  \label{eq:spde-tightness-h-minus-eta-moment}
\end{equation}
Then \(\{\nu_N\}\) is tight as a family of probability measures on
\(H^{-\kappa}(\mathbb T^2)\).  More explicitly, for every \(R>0\) the set
\[
  K_R=\{\phi\in H^{-\eta}(\mathbb T^2):
          \|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}\leq R\}
\]
is compact in \(H^{-\kappa}(\mathbb T^2)\), and
\[
  \nu_N(K_R^c)\leq C R^{-p}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Write the Fourier coefficients of \(\phi\) as \(\widehat\phi(k)\),
\(k\in\mathbb Z^2\), and set
\(\langle k\rangle=(1+|k|^2)^{1/2}\).  The Sobolev norms are
\begin{equation}
  \|\phi\|_{H^{-\rho}}^2
  =
  \sum_{k\in\mathbb Z^2}
  \langle k\rangle^{-2\rho}|\widehat\phi(k)|^2 ,
  \qquad \rho\geq0 .
  \label{eq:spde-negative-sobolev-fourier-norm}
\end{equation}
Let \(P_M\) be the projection to Fourier modes \(|k|\leq M\), and write
\(\langle M\rangle=(1+M^2)^{1/2}\).  If \(\phi\in K_R\), then
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \|(1-P_M)\phi\|_{H^{-\kappa}}^2
  &=
  \sum_{|k|>M}
  \langle k\rangle^{-2(\kappa-\eta)}
  \langle k\rangle^{-2\eta}|\widehat\phi(k)|^2
\\
  &\leq
  \langle M\rangle^{-2(\kappa-\eta)}
  \|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^2
  \leq
  \langle M\rangle^{-2(\kappa-\eta)}R^2 .
\end{aligned}
\]
Thus the high-frequency tail of \(K_R\) is uniformly small in
\(H^{-\kappa}\).  The set \(P_MK_R\) is bounded in a finite-dimensional
space and is therefore totally bounded.  Given \(\varepsilon>0\), choose
\(M\) so that
\(\langle M\rangle^{-(\kappa-\eta)}R<\varepsilon/3\), cover \(P_MK_R\) by
finitely many \(H^{-\kappa}\)-balls of radius \(\varepsilon/3\), and add the
tail estimate.  This proves that \(K_R\) is totally bounded in
\(H^{-\kappa}\).

It remains only to see that \(K_R\) is closed in \(H^{-\kappa}\).  If
\(\phi_n\in K_R\) and \(\phi_n\to\phi\) in \(H^{-\kappa}\), then each
Fourier coefficient converges.  Fatou's lemma gives
\[
  \|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^2
  =
  \sum_k
  \langle k\rangle^{-2\eta}|\widehat\phi(k)|^2
  \leq
  \liminf_{n\to\infty}
  \sum_k
  \langle k\rangle^{-2\eta}|\widehat\phi_n(k)|^2
  \leq R^2 .
\]
Therefore \(\phi\in K_R\), so \(K_R\) is compact in \(H^{-\kappa}\).
Finally, Markov's inequality applied to
\eqref{eq:spde-tightness-h-minus-eta-moment} gives
\[
  \nu_N(K_R^c)
  =
  \nu_N\{\|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}>R\}
  \leq
  R^{-p}\int\|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^p\,\dd\nu_N
  \leq C R^{-p}.
\]
Choosing \(R\) large proves tightness.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Massive Gaussian cutoff tightness in negative Sobolev topology]
\label{prop:spde-free-gaussian-negative-sobolev-tightness}
Let \(A=-\Delta\) on \(\mathbb T^2\), and let
\(\{e_\alpha\}_{\alpha\in\mathcal I}\) be a real orthonormal eigenbasis of
\(L^2(\mathbb T^2)\), with \(Ae_\alpha=\lambda_\alpha e_\alpha\),
\(\lambda_\alpha\geq0\).  Fix \(m^2>0\), and for \(N\geq1\) set
\[
  \mathcal I_N=\{\alpha\in\mathcal I:\lambda_\alpha\leq N^2\}.
\]
Let \(\gamma_N\) be the centered Gaussian law of
\[
  \phi_N
  =
  \sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_N}
  g_\alpha(\lambda_\alpha+m^2)^{-1/2}e_\alpha ,
\]
where \(\{g_\alpha\}\) are independent real standard Gaussian random
variables.  Then for every \(\eta>0\),
\[
  \sup_N
  \int
  \|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}(\mathbb T^2)}^2\,\dd\gamma_N(\phi)
  <\infty .
\]
Consequently, if \(0<\eta<\kappa\), the family \(\{\gamma_N\}\) is tight as
a family of probability measures on \(H^{-\kappa}(\mathbb T^2)\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By definition of the Hilbert Sobolev norm associated with the Laplacian,
\[
  \|\phi_N\|_{H^{-\eta}}^2
  =
  \sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_N}
  (1+\lambda_\alpha)^{-\eta}
  |(\phi_N,e_\alpha)_{L^2}|^2 .
\]
Taking expectation and using \(\mathbb E g_\alpha^2=1\) gives
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb E\|\phi_N\|_{H^{-\eta}}^2
  =
  \sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_N}
  (1+\lambda_\alpha)^{-\eta}
  (\lambda_\alpha+m^2)^{-1}.
  \label{eq:spde-free-gaussian-hminus-eta-second-moment}
\end{equation}
There is a constant \(c_m<\infty\) such that
\((\lambda+m^2)^{-1}\leq c_m(1+\lambda)^{-1}\) for all \(\lambda\geq0\).
Thus the right hand side of
\eqref{eq:spde-free-gaussian-hminus-eta-second-moment} is bounded by
\[
  c_m
  \sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I}
  (1+\lambda_\alpha)^{-1-\eta}.
\]
For the flat two-torus \(\R^2/(2\pi\mathbb Z)^2\), the complex Fourier basis
has eigenvalues \(|k|^2\), \(k\in\mathbb Z^2\).  Passing from the complex
basis to a real sine-cosine eigenbasis changes the counting by a bounded
factor.  It therefore suffices to prove convergence of
\[
  \sum_{k\in\mathbb Z^2}(1+|k|^2)^{-1-\eta}.
\]
Write \(\langle k\rangle=(1+|k|^2)^{1/2}\).
Let \(A_0=\{k:\langle k\rangle<2\}\) and, for \(j\geq1\),
\[
  A_j=\{k\in\mathbb Z^2:2^j\leq \langle k\rangle<2^{j+1}\}.
\]
There is a universal constant \(C\) such that the cardinality of \(A_j\) is
at most \(C2^{2j}\), while each summand on \(A_j\) is at most
\(2^{-2(1+\eta)j}\).  Hence
\[
  \sum_{k\in A_j}(1+|k|^2)^{-1-\eta}
  \leq
  C2^{-2\eta j}.
\]
The geometric series over \(j\) converges because \(\eta>0\).  This proves
the uniform second-moment bound.  Since each \(\gamma_N\) is carried by the
finite-dimensional space spanned by \(\{e_\alpha:\alpha\in\mathcal I_N\}\),
it is carried by \(H^{-\eta}\).
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-sobolev-compactness-tightness} with \(p=2\) now
gives tightness in \(H^{-\kappa}\).
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[\(L^q\)-density criterion for interacting negative-Sobolev moments]
\label{lem:spde-lq-density-negative-sobolev-moment}
Let \(0<\eta<\kappa\).  For each \(N\), let \(\gamma_N\) be a centered
Gaussian probability measure carried by a finite-dimensional subspace of
\(H^{-\eta}(\mathbb T^2)\), and assume
\[
  \sigma^2:=
  \sup_N
  \int \|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^2\,\dd\gamma_N(\phi)
  <\infty .
\]
Let \(\mu_N=\rho_N\gamma_N\), where
\(\rho_N\geq0\), \(\int\rho_N\,\dd\gamma_N=1\), and, for some \(q>1\),
\[
  A_q:=\sup_N\|\rho_N\|_{L^q(\gamma_N)}<\infty .
\]
Then, for every \(r<\infty\),
\[
  \sup_N
  \int\|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^r\,\dd\mu_N(\phi)
  <\infty .
\]
Consequently \(\{\mu_N\}\) is tight in \(H^{-\kappa}(\mathbb T^2)\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Let \(a=q/(q-1)\).  Holder's inequality gives
\begin{equation}
  \int\|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^r\,\dd\mu_N(\phi)
  =
  \int\|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^r\rho_N(\phi)\,\dd\gamma_N(\phi)
  \leq
  A_q
  \left(
    \int\|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^{ar}\,\dd\gamma_N(\phi)
  \right)^{1/a}.
  \label{eq:spde-lq-density-holder}
\end{equation}
It remains to bound the Gaussian moment uniformly.  Since \(\gamma_N\) is a
finite-dimensional centered Gaussian law on the Hilbert space
\(H^{-\eta}\), its covariance operator is a nonnegative symmetric operator
of finite rank.  Diagonalize this covariance in an
\(H^{-\eta}\)-orthonormal basis:
\[
  \phi_N=\sum_i \lambda_{N,i}^{1/2}g_i e_{N,i},
  \qquad
  \|\phi_N\|_{H^{-\eta}}^2=\sum_i\lambda_{N,i}g_i^2,
\]
where the \(g_i\) are independent standard real Gaussians and
\(\sum_i\lambda_{N,i}\leq\sigma^2\).  For an integer \(m\geq1\),
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \mathbb E_{\gamma_N}\|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^{2m}
  &=
  \sum_{i_1,\ldots,i_m}
  \lambda_{N,i_1}\cdots\lambda_{N,i_m}
  \mathbb E(g_{i_1}^2\cdots g_{i_m}^2)
\\
  &\leq
  (2m-1)!!
  \left(\sum_i\lambda_{N,i}\right)^m
  \leq
  (2m-1)!!\,\sigma^{2m}.
\end{aligned}
\]
Choose \(m\) with \(2m\geq ar\).  The elementary inequality
\(x^{ar}\leq1+x^{2m}\) for \(x\geq0\) gives a uniform bound for the
Gaussian moment in \eqref{eq:spde-lq-density-holder}.  Thus the
\(H^{-\eta}\) \(r\)-th moments under \(\mu_N\) are uniformly bounded.
Applying Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-sobolev-compactness-tightness} with any
positive \(r\) proves tightness in \(H^{-\kappa}\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Density route to \(\Phi^4_2\) stationary-law tightness]
\label{rem:spde-phi-four-two-density-tightness-route}
Let \(\mu_{0,N}\) be the massive Gaussian cutoff law in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-free-gaussian-negative-sobolev-tightness}, and
let
\[
  \dd\mu_N(\phi)
  =
  Z_N^{-1}
  \exp\!\left[
    -\frac{\lambda}{4}
    \int_{\mathbb T^2}:\!(P_N\phi)^4\!:\,\dd^2x
  \right]\dd\mu_{0,N}(\phi)
\]
be a finite-dimensional Wick-ordered \(\Phi^4_2\) cutoff measure.  If there
exists \(q>1\) such that the normalized densities
\[
  \rho_N(\phi)=
  Z_N^{-1}
  \exp\!\left[
    -\frac{\lambda}{4}
    \int_{\mathbb T^2}:\!(P_N\phi)^4\!:\,\dd^2x
  \right]
\]
satisfy
\[
  \sup_N\|\rho_N\|_{L^q(\mu_{0,N})}<\infty ,
\]
then \(\{\mu_N\}\) is tight in \(H^{-\kappa}(\mathbb T^2)\) for every
\(\kappa>0\).
Choose any \(0<\eta<\kappa\).  The Gaussian reference law has a uniform
\(H^{-\eta}\) second moment by
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-free-gaussian-negative-sobolev-tightness}.  The
assumed \(L^q\) density bound then gives a uniform interacting
\(H^{-\eta}\) moment by
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-lq-density-negative-sobolev-moment}, and
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-sobolev-compactness-tightness} turns that moment
bound into tightness in \(H^{-\kappa}\).
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Nelson stability implies normalized \(L^q\) density bounds]
\label{lem:spde-nelson-stability-implies-lq-density}
Let \(\mu_{0,N}\) be a finite-dimensional massive Gaussian cutoff law on
\(\mathbb T^2\), and set
\[
  V_N(\phi)=
  \frac{\lambda}{4}
  \int_{\mathbb T^2}:\!(P_N\phi)^4\!:\,\dd^2x ,
  \qquad \lambda>0,
\]
where Wick ordering is taken with respect to \(\mu_{0,N}\).  Suppose that
the cutoff family satisfies the Nelson stability exponential estimate
\begin{equation}
  \sup_N
  \int \exp[-pV_N(\phi)]\,\dd\mu_{0,N}(\phi)<\infty
  \qquad\hbox{for every finite }p\geq1 .
  \label{eq:spde-nelson-stability-exponential-input}
\end{equation}
Let
\[
  Z_N=\int e^{-V_N(\phi)}\,\dd\mu_{0,N}(\phi),
  \qquad
  \rho_N=Z_N^{-1}e^{-V_N}.
\]
Then, for every finite \(q\geq1\),
\[
  \sup_N\|\rho_N\|_{L^q(\mu_{0,N})}<\infty .
\]
Consequently, for every \(0<\eta<\kappa\), the interacting cutoff measures
\(\mu_N=\rho_N\mu_{0,N}\) are tight in \(H^{-\kappa}(\mathbb T^2)\), provided
the Gaussian reference laws have the uniform \(H^{-\eta}\) second-moment
bound of Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-free-gaussian-negative-sobolev-tightness}.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The normalization cannot be allowed to hide a cutoff-dependent loss.  Wick
ordering gives
\[
  \int :\!(P_N\phi(x))^4\!:\,\dd\mu_{0,N}(\phi)=0
  \qquad\hbox{for every }x,
\]
and hence, by Fubini in the finite-dimensional cutoff space,
\[
  \int V_N(\phi)\,\dd\mu_{0,N}(\phi)=0 .
\]
Jensen's inequality for the convex function \(u\mapsto e^{-u}\) gives
\begin{equation}
  Z_N
  =
  \int e^{-V_N}\,\dd\mu_{0,N}
  \geq
  \exp\!\left[-\int V_N\,\dd\mu_{0,N}\right]
  =1 .
  \label{eq:spde-wick-quartic-partition-lower-bound}
\end{equation}
Therefore, for \(q\geq1\),
\[
  \|\rho_N\|_{L^q(\mu_{0,N})}^q
  =
  Z_N^{-q}
  \int e^{-qV_N}\,\dd\mu_{0,N}
  \leq
  \int e^{-qV_N}\,\dd\mu_{0,N}.
\]
The right-hand side is bounded uniformly in \(N\) by
\eqref{eq:spde-nelson-stability-exponential-input} with \(p=q\).  This
proves the normalized \(L^q\) density bound.  The tightness conclusion is
then exactly
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-phi-four-two-density-tightness-route}, or,
equivalently, Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-lq-density-negative-sobolev-moment}
followed by Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-sobolev-compactness-tightness}.
\end{proof}

The preceding proposition proves the probabilistic consequence of Nelson
stability without losing constants in the normalization.  For cutoff
families covered by
Quoted Theorem~\ref{qthm:p-phi-two-stability}, the hypothesis
\eqref{eq:spde-nelson-stability-exponential-input} is exactly the
\(P(\phi)_2\) stability and exponential-integrability estimate.  For a
sharp Fourier-Galerkin stochastic regulator, the same conclusion requires
either a direct Nelson stability proof for that regulator or a comparison
with a smooth ultraviolet regulator for which the stability theorem has
already been established.  This is a regulator-specific constructive
estimate, not a formal property of Wick ordering alone.

\begin{lemma}[Bounded-cylinder comparison from a common density limit]
\label{lem:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-density-limit}
Let \((\Omega,\mathcal F,\gamma)\) be a probability space.  For
\(\sigma\in\{A,B\}\) and \(N\geq1\), let
\[
  X_N^\sigma:\Omega\to\R^r,\qquad W_N^\sigma:\Omega\to[0,\infty)
\]
be measurable, and let \(X:\Omega\to\R^r\), \(W:\Omega\to[0,\infty)\) be
measurable limits.  Assume
\begin{equation}
  X_N^\sigma\longrightarrow X
  \quad\hbox{in }\gamma\hbox{-probability},
  \qquad
  W_N^\sigma\longrightarrow W
  \quad\hbox{in }L^1(\gamma)
  \label{eq:spde-common-density-limit-hypotheses}
\end{equation}
for \(\sigma=A,B\).  Assume also that there is \(p>1\) such that
\begin{equation}
  \sup_{N,\sigma}\|W_N^\sigma\|_{L^p(\gamma)}<\infty .
  \label{eq:spde-common-density-limit-uniform-integrability}
\end{equation}
Set
\[
  Z_N^\sigma=\int W_N^\sigma\,\dd\gamma,
  \qquad
  Z=\int W\,\dd\gamma,
\]
and suppose \(Z>0\).  Then, for every bounded continuous
\(F:\R^r\to\C\),
\begin{equation}
  \lim_{N\to\infty}
  \frac{\int F(X_N^A)W_N^A\,\dd\gamma}{Z_N^A}
  =
  \frac{\int F(X)W\,\dd\gamma}{Z}
  =
  \lim_{N\to\infty}
  \frac{\int F(X_N^B)W_N^B\,\dd\gamma}{Z_N^B}.
  \label{eq:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-density-limit}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The \(L^1\)-convergence of \(W_N^\sigma\) gives
\[
  Z_N^\sigma\longrightarrow Z
\]
for \(\sigma=A,B\).  Thus it is enough to prove convergence of the
unnormalized numerators.  Fix \(\sigma\) and write
\[
\begin{aligned}
  &\int F(X_N^\sigma)W_N^\sigma\,\dd\gamma
  -
  \int F(X)W\,\dd\gamma
\\
  &=
  \int \bigl(F(X_N^\sigma)-F(X)\bigr)W_N^\sigma\,\dd\gamma
  +
  \int F(X)\bigl(W_N^\sigma-W\bigr)\,\dd\gamma .
\end{aligned}
\]
The second term tends to zero because \(F\) is bounded and
\(W_N^\sigma\to W\) in \(L^1\).  For the first term, the convergence
\(X_N^\sigma\to X\) in probability and continuity of \(F\) imply
\[
  F(X_N^\sigma)-F(X)\longrightarrow0
  \quad\hbox{in probability}.
\]
The difference is bounded by \(2\|F\|_\infty\), while
\eqref{eq:spde-common-density-limit-uniform-integrability} implies uniform
integrability of \(\{W_N^\sigma\}\) by Holder's inequality:
\[
  \int_E W_N^\sigma\,\dd\gamma
  \leq
  \|W_N^\sigma\|_{L^p(\gamma)}
  \gamma(E)^{1-1/p}.
\]
Given \(\varepsilon>0\), choose \(\delta>0\) so small that the right-hand
side is at most \(\varepsilon\) for every \(N,\sigma\) whenever
\(\gamma(E)<\delta\).  On the event
\(\{|F(X_N^\sigma)-F(X)|\leq\varepsilon\}\), the first term is bounded by
\(\varepsilon\int W_N^\sigma\dd\gamma\), and the integrals of
\(W_N^\sigma\) are uniformly bounded by the \(L^p\) hypothesis.  On the
complement, the uniform-integrability estimate applies because the
complement has \(\gamma\)-probability tending to zero.  Hence the first term
tends to zero for each fixed regulator type \(\sigma\).  Applying this
conclusion for \(\sigma=A\) and for \(\sigma=B\) gives the two unnormalized
limits, and the normalized limits follow from \(Z_N^\sigma\to Z>0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Bounded-cylinder comparison from a common potential]
\label{cor:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-potential}
In the setting of
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-density-limit}, replace
the \(L^1\)-convergence assumption on the densities by the following
potential-level assumptions.  Let
\[
  V_N^\sigma:\Omega\to\R,\qquad V:\Omega\to\R,
  \qquad \sigma\in\{A,B\},
\]
be measurable real-valued interaction functionals, put
\[
  W_N^\sigma=e^{-V_N^\sigma},\qquad W=e^{-V},
\]
and assume
\begin{equation}
  X_N^\sigma\longrightarrow X,
  \qquad
  V_N^\sigma\longrightarrow V
  \quad\hbox{in }\gamma\hbox{-probability}
  \label{eq:spde-common-potential-convergence}
\end{equation}
for \(\sigma=A,B\).  Assume further that, for some \(p>1\),
\begin{equation}
  \sup_{N,\sigma}\|e^{-V_N^\sigma}\|_{L^p(\gamma)}<\infty,
  \qquad
  Z:=\int e^{-V}\,\dd\gamma>0 .
  \label{eq:spde-common-potential-lp-stability}
\end{equation}
Then the normalized bounded cylinder expectations of the two regulators
have the common limit
\begin{equation}
  \lim_{N\to\infty}
  \frac{\int F(X_N^\sigma)e^{-V_N^\sigma}\,\dd\gamma}
       {\int e^{-V_N^\sigma}\,\dd\gamma}
  =
  \frac{\int F(X)e^{-V}\,\dd\gamma}
       {\int e^{-V}\,\dd\gamma},
  \qquad
  \sigma=A,B,
  \label{eq:spde-common-potential-cylinder-limit}
\end{equation}
for every bounded continuous \(F:\R^r\to\C\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
It is enough to verify the density hypotheses of
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-density-limit}.  Since
the exponential map is continuous,
\[
  e^{-V_N^\sigma}\longrightarrow e^{-V}
  \quad\hbox{in }\gamma\hbox{-probability}.
\]
We first record explicitly that the limiting weight belongs to \(L^p\).
From any subsequence of \(e^{-V_N^\sigma}\) one may choose a further
subsequence converging to \(e^{-V}\) almost surely.  Fatou's lemma gives
\[
  \|e^{-V}\|_{L^p(\gamma)}^p
  \leq
  \liminf_{k\to\infty}
  \|e^{-V_{N_k}^\sigma}\|_{L^p(\gamma)}^p
  \leq
  \sup_{N,\sigma}\|e^{-V_N^\sigma}\|_{L^p(\gamma)}^p .
\]
Thus the family
\[
  \{e^{-V}\}\cup
  \{e^{-V_N^\sigma}:N\geq1,\ \sigma=A,B\}
\]
is uniformly integrable.  Indeed, for every measurable \(E\subset\Omega\),
Holder's inequality gives
\[
  \int_E e^{-V_N^\sigma}\,\dd\gamma
  \leq
  \|e^{-V_N^\sigma}\|_{L^p(\gamma)}
  \gamma(E)^{1-1/p},
  \qquad
  \int_E e^{-V}\,\dd\gamma
  \leq
  \|e^{-V}\|_{L^p(\gamma)}
  \gamma(E)^{1-1/p}.
\]
We now prove the \(L^1\)-convergence rather than citing Vitali's theorem.
Fix \(\varepsilon>0\).  By the preceding uniform-integrability estimate,
choose \(\delta>0\) so that the integral of any member of the displayed
family over a set of \(\gamma\)-measure less than \(\delta\) is at most
\(\varepsilon\).  Let
\[
  E_N^\sigma=\{|e^{-V_N^\sigma}-e^{-V}|>\varepsilon\}.
\]
Convergence in probability gives \(\gamma(E_N^\sigma)<\delta\) for all
sufficiently large \(N\).  Then
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \int |e^{-V_N^\sigma}-e^{-V}|\,\dd\gamma
  &\leq
  \varepsilon
  +\int_{E_N^\sigma} e^{-V_N^\sigma}\,\dd\gamma
  +\int_{E_N^\sigma} e^{-V}\,\dd\gamma  \\
  &\leq 3\varepsilon
\end{aligned}
\]
for all sufficiently large \(N\).  Hence
\[
  e^{-V_N^\sigma}\longrightarrow e^{-V}
  \quad\hbox{in }L^1(\gamma),
  \qquad \sigma=A,B .
\]
The hypotheses of
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-density-limit} are now
satisfied, and its conclusion is exactly
\eqref{eq:spde-common-potential-cylinder-limit}.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Bounded Wick-cylinder comparison for stable quartic cutoffs.}
Let \(X_N^A\) and \(X_N^B\) be two cutoff approximations of the same massive
two-dimensional Gaussian field on a common probability space
\((\Omega,\mathcal F,\gamma)\).  Fix \(\lambda\in\R\) and define
\[
  V_N^\sigma
  =
  \frac{\lambda}{4}\,:\!(X_N^\sigma)^4\!:(1),
  \qquad \sigma\in\{A,B\}.
\]
Assume that the finite Wick coordinates
\[
  :\!(X_N^\sigma)^{n_j}\!:(f_j),
  \qquad 1\leq j\leq r,
\]
converge in \(L^2(\Omega)\), for both \(\sigma=A,B\), to common limits
\(:\!X^{n_j}\!:(f_j)\), and that
\begin{equation}
  V_N^\sigma
  \longrightarrow
  V:=\frac{\lambda}{4}\,:\!X^4\!:(1)
  \quad\hbox{in }L^2(\Omega),
  \qquad \sigma=A,B.
  \label{eq:spde-stable-quartic-comparison-potential-l2}
\end{equation}
Assume also that there is \(p>1\) such that
\begin{equation}
  \sup_{N,\sigma}
  \left\|e^{-V_N^\sigma}\right\|_{L^p(\gamma)}
  <\infty .
  \label{eq:spde-stable-quartic-comparison-lp}
\end{equation}
Let
\[
  \mathcal X_N^\sigma
  =
  \bigl(:\!(X_N^\sigma)^{n_1}\!:(f_1),\ldots,
        :\!(X_N^\sigma)^{n_r}\!:(f_r)\bigr),
  \qquad
  \mathcal X
  =
  \bigl(:\!X^{n_1}\!:(f_1),\ldots,:\!X^{n_r}\!:(f_r)\bigr).
\]
Then, for every bounded continuous \(G:\R^r\to\C\),
\begin{equation}
  \lim_{N\to\infty}
  \frac{\int G(\mathcal X_N^A)e^{-V_N^A}\,\dd\gamma}
       {\int e^{-V_N^A}\,\dd\gamma}
  =
  \frac{\int G(\mathcal X)e^{-V}\,\dd\gamma}
       {\int e^{-V}\,\dd\gamma}
  =
  \lim_{N\to\infty}
  \frac{\int G(\mathcal X_N^B)e^{-V_N^B}\,\dd\gamma}
       {\int e^{-V_N^B}\,\dd\gamma}.
  \label{eq:spde-stable-quartic-bounded-cylinder-comparison}
\end{equation}

Remark~\ref{rem:spde-common-wick-coordinate-limits} gives
\[
  \mathcal X_N^\sigma\longrightarrow \mathcal X
  \quad\hbox{in probability},
  \qquad \sigma=A,B.
\]
The assumed \(L^2\)-convergence
\eqref{eq:spde-stable-quartic-comparison-potential-l2} gives
\[
  V_N^\sigma\longrightarrow V
  \quad\hbox{in probability}.
\]
From every subsequence one may choose a further subsequence along which
\(V_N^\sigma\to V\) almost surely.  Fatou's lemma and
\eqref{eq:spde-stable-quartic-comparison-lp} imply
\[
  \int e^{-pV}\,\dd\gamma
  \leq
  \liminf_{k\to\infty}
  \int e^{-pV_{N_k}^\sigma}\,\dd\gamma
  <\infty .
\]
Thus \(e^{-V}\in L^p(\gamma)\), while \(e^{-V}>0\) almost surely because
\(V\) is real-valued and finite almost surely.  Hence
\[
  0<\int e^{-V}\,\dd\gamma<\infty .
\]
All hypotheses of
Corollary~\ref{cor:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-potential} are satisfied,
and its conclusion is precisely
\eqref{eq:spde-stable-quartic-bounded-cylinder-comparison}.

\subsection{Regulators, Reflection Positivity, and the \texorpdfstring{\(\Phi^4_2\)}{Phi-four-two} Assembly}
\label{subsec:spde-dpd-regulators-os-assembly}

\begin{proposition}[Smooth regulator consequences of Nelson stability]
\label{prop:spde-smooth-regulator-nelson-consequences}
Let \(\gamma\) be the massive Gaussian free-field law on
\(\mathbb T^2\).  For \(\sigma\in\{A,B\}\), let
\[
  X_N^\sigma=\mu^\sigma(D/N)X
\]
be smooth Fourier multiplier cutoffs as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-smooth-fourier-multiplier-covariance-convergence},
and let
\[
  V_N^\sigma
  =
  \frac{\lambda}{4}\int_{\mathbb T^2}
  :\!(X_N^\sigma(x))^4\!:\,\dd^2x,
  \qquad \lambda>0,
\]
with Wick ordering taken with respect to the cutoff covariance of
\(X_N^\sigma\).  Assume the Nelson stability input
\begin{equation}
  \sup_{N,\sigma}
  \int \exp[-pV_N^\sigma]\,\dd\gamma<\infty
  \qquad\hbox{for every finite }p\geq1 .
  \label{eq:spde-smooth-regulator-nelson-input}
\end{equation}
Set
\[
  Z_N^\sigma=\int e^{-V_N^\sigma}\,\dd\gamma,
  \qquad
  \rho_N^\sigma=(Z_N^\sigma)^{-1}e^{-V_N^\sigma},
  \qquad
  \dd\nu_N^\sigma=\rho_N^\sigma\,\dd\gamma .
\]
Then the following statements hold.
\begin{enumerate}
\item For every finite \(q\geq1\),
\begin{equation}
  \sup_{N,\sigma}
  \|\rho_N^\sigma\|_{L^q(\gamma)}<\infty .
  \label{eq:spde-smooth-regulator-density-lq}
\end{equation}
\item For every \(\kappa>0\), the two families
\(\{\nu_N^A\}\) and \(\{\nu_N^B\}\) are tight in
\(H^{-\kappa}(\mathbb T^2)\).
\item For every finite list of Wick coordinates
\(:\!(X_N^\sigma)^{n_j}\!:(f_j)\), \(1\leq j\leq r\), and every bounded
continuous \(G:\R^r\to\C\), the normalized expectations of
\(G\) under the two cutoff families have the common continuum limit stated in
\eqref{eq:spde-stable-quartic-bounded-cylinder-comparison}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Wick centering gives
\[
  \int V_N^\sigma\,\dd\gamma=0 .
\]
Jensen's inequality therefore gives
\[
  Z_N^\sigma=\int e^{-V_N^\sigma}\,\dd\gamma
  \geq
  \exp\!\left[-\int V_N^\sigma\,\dd\gamma\right]
  =1 .
\]
Consequently
\[
  \|\rho_N^\sigma\|_{L^q(\gamma)}^q
  =
  (Z_N^\sigma)^{-q}
  \int e^{-qV_N^\sigma}\,\dd\gamma
  \leq
  \int e^{-qV_N^\sigma}\,\dd\gamma,
\]
and \eqref{eq:spde-smooth-regulator-density-lq} follows from
\eqref{eq:spde-smooth-regulator-nelson-input}.

For tightness, choose \(0<\eta<\kappa\).  The massive Gaussian field has
finite \(H^{-\eta}\)-moments of every order: diagonalizing the covariance
in Fourier modes gives
\[
  \mathbb E_\gamma\|X\|_{H^{-\eta}}^2
  =
  \sum_{k\in\mathbb Z^2}
  \frac{(1+|k|^2)^{-\eta}}{|k|^2+m^2}
  <\infty,
\]
and the higher moments are bounded by the same Gaussian Hilbert-norm
argument used in
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-lq-density-negative-sobolev-moment}.  Holder's
inequality with the uniform \(L^q\) bound for \(\rho_N^\sigma\) gives
\[
  \sup_{N,\sigma}
  \int\|\phi\|_{H^{-\eta}}^r\,\dd\nu_N^\sigma(\phi)<\infty
  \qquad (r<\infty).
\]
The compact embedding \(H^{-\eta}\hookrightarrow H^{-\kappa}\), quantified
in Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-sobolev-compactness-tightness}, proves
tightness in \(H^{-\kappa}\).

It remains to prove the comparison statement.  By
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-smooth-fourier-multiplier-covariance-convergence}
and
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-mixed-covariance-common-wick-limits}, the finite
Wick-coordinate vectors of the two smooth regulators have common \(L^2\)
limits.  Applying the fourth Wick-power convergence statement with
\(f\equiv1\) gives
\[
  V_N^\sigma\longrightarrow
  \frac{\lambda}{4}:\!X^4\!:(1)
  \quad\hbox{in }L^2(\gamma),
  \qquad \sigma=A,B .
\]
The stability input \eqref{eq:spde-smooth-regulator-nelson-input} supplies
the uniform \(L^p\) bound on \(e^{-V_N^\sigma}\).  Hence the bounded
Wick-cylinder comparison
\eqref{eq:spde-stable-quartic-bounded-cylinder-comparison} applies and gives
the stated comparison.
\end{proof}

In the regulator-comparison problem, \(X_N^\sigma\) is the finite list of
smeared field or Wick-polynomial coordinates entering a bounded positive-time
cylinder observable, and \(W_N^\sigma\) is the finite-cutoff interaction
density.  Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-density-limit}
therefore proves the bounded-observable comparison once both regulators are
constructed on a common Gaussian probability space and their Wick densities
are shown to have the same \(L^1\) limit.
Corollary~\ref{cor:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-potential}
gives the common route used in cutoff constructions: it is enough to prove
that the renormalized interaction functionals converge in probability to the
same limiting potential and that their exponential weights obey a uniform
\(L^p\) stability estimate.  In the Wick quartic case,
the comparison
\eqref{eq:spde-stable-quartic-bounded-cylinder-comparison} is obtained once
the common Wick-coordinate limits and exponential-weight stability have been
proved.
For smooth Fourier multiplier regulators satisfying the Nelson stability
input, Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-smooth-regulator-nelson-consequences}
derives the normalized \(L^q\) density bounds, tightness, and bounded
Wick-cylinder comparison in one statement.
Unbounded polynomial observables still require the separate
uniform-integrability argument in
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-polynomial-os-uniform-integrability}.

\begin{proposition}[Brascamp--Lieb covariance domination for convex cutoffs]
\label{prop:spde-brascamp-lieb-convex-cutoff-moment}
Let \(H_N\) be a finite-dimensional real Hilbert space, let \(A_N\) be a
positive self-adjoint operator on \(H_N\), and let \(S_N\in C^2(H_N)\)
satisfy
\begin{equation}
  \nabla^2S_N(\phi)\geq A_N
  \label{eq:spde-brascamp-lieb-hessian-lower-bound}
\end{equation}
as quadratic forms on \(H_N\), for every \(\phi\in H_N\).  Define
\[
  \dd\nu_N(\phi)=Z_N^{-1}e^{-S_N(\phi)}\,\dd\phi
\]
where \(\dd\phi\) is Lebesgue measure in an orthonormal coordinate system
and \(Z_N=\int e^{-S_N(\phi)}\dd\phi\).  Then \(Z_N<\infty\), the
integration-by-parts identities used below hold for smooth functions of
polynomial growth, and every linear functional
\(\ell_v(\phi)=(v,\phi)_{H_N}\) satisfies
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Var}_{\nu_N}(\ell_v)
  \leq
  (v,A_N^{-1}v)_{H_N}.
  \label{eq:spde-brascamp-lieb-linear-covariance}
\end{equation}

Suppose in addition that \(L_N\) is a nonnegative self-adjoint operator with
orthonormal eigenvectors \(e_{N,\alpha}\) and eigenvalues
\(\lambda_{N,\alpha}\), that \(A_N\geq L_N+m^2{\bf 1}\) for some \(m^2>0\),
and that \(\nu_N\) is invariant under \(\phi\mapsto-\phi\).  Define
\begin{equation}
  \|\phi\|_{H_N^{-\eta}}^2
  =
  \sum_\alpha
  (1+\lambda_{N,\alpha})^{-\eta}
  |(\phi,e_{N,\alpha})_{H_N}|^2 .
  \label{eq:spde-discrete-negative-sobolev-norm}
\end{equation}
Then, for every \(\eta>0\),
\begin{equation}
  \int\|\phi\|_{H_N^{-\eta}}^2\,\dd\nu_N(\phi)
  \leq
  \sum_\alpha
  (1+\lambda_{N,\alpha})^{-\eta}
  (\lambda_{N,\alpha}+m^2)^{-1}.
  \label{eq:spde-convex-cutoff-hminus-moment-bound}
\end{equation}
Consequently, any cutoff family for which the right hand side of
\eqref{eq:spde-convex-cutoff-hminus-moment-bound} is uniformly bounded and
whose \(H_N^{-\eta}\) spaces embed into a common \(H^{-\eta}\) approximation
scheme satisfies the moment hypothesis in
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-sobolev-compactness-tightness}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let \(a_N>0\) be the smallest eigenvalue of \(A_N\).  Taylor's formula gives
\[
  S_N(\phi)
  \geq
  S_N(0)+(\nabla S_N(0),\phi)_{H_N}
  +\frac{a_N}{2}\|\phi\|_{H_N}^2
  \geq
  \frac{a_N}{4}\|\phi\|_{H_N}^2-C_N
\]
for a finite constant \(C_N\).  Hence \(e^{-S_N}\) has Gaussian decay.
This proves \(Z_N<\infty\) and justifies the integration by parts below
after inserting radial cutoffs and sending their radii to infinity.

We first prove the covariance estimate.  Write
\[
  \mathcal L=\Delta-\nabla S_N\cdot\nabla .
\]
This operator is symmetric in \(L^2(\nu_N)\) on smooth compactly supported
functions, and
\begin{equation}
  -\int f\,\mathcal Lg\,\dd\nu_N
  =
  \int(\nabla f,\nabla g)_{H_N}\,\dd\nu_N .
  \label{eq:spde-finite-log-concave-dirichlet-form}
\end{equation}
Let \(f\) be a smooth centered test function.  On the centered subspace of
\(L^2(\nu_N)\), let \(u_\varepsilon=(\varepsilon-\mathcal L)^{-1}f\),
\(\varepsilon>0\), where the inverse is the Friedrichs resolvent of the
closed Dirichlet form in
\eqref{eq:spde-finite-log-concave-dirichlet-form}.  The resolvent satisfies
\begin{equation}
  \varepsilon u_\varepsilon-\mathcal L u_\varepsilon=f .
  \label{eq:spde-bl-resolvent-equation}
\end{equation}
Pairing \eqref{eq:spde-bl-resolvent-equation} with \(f\) and using
\eqref{eq:spde-finite-log-concave-dirichlet-form} gives
\begin{equation}
  \int f^2\,\dd\nu_N
  =
  \varepsilon\int fu_\varepsilon\,\dd\nu_N
  +
  \int(\nabla f,\nabla u_\varepsilon)_{H_N}\,\dd\nu_N .
  \label{eq:spde-bl-resolvent-pairing}
\end{equation}
The spectral calculus of the nonnegative operator
\(-\mathcal L\) on centered \(L^2(\nu_N)\) gives
\(\varepsilon u_\varepsilon\to0\) and
\(-\mathcal L u_\varepsilon\to f\) in \(L^2(\nu_N)\).  Hence the first term
on the right of \eqref{eq:spde-bl-resolvent-pairing} vanishes as
\(\varepsilon\downarrow0\).

For smooth compactly supported \(u\), differentiating \(\mathcal L u\) and
integrating by parts gives the finite-dimensional Bochner identity
\begin{equation}
  \int(\mathcal L u)^2\,\dd\nu_N
  =
  \int\|\nabla^2u\|_{\mathrm{HS}}^2\,\dd\nu_N
  +
  \int(\nabla u,\nabla^2S_N\,\nabla u)_{H_N}\,\dd\nu_N .
  \label{eq:spde-finite-bochner-identity}
\end{equation}
Indeed, expanding
\(\int(\Delta u-\nabla S_N\cdot\nabla u)^2e^{-S_N}\dd\phi\), moving one
derivative from each second-derivative term, and collecting the mixed terms
leaves precisely the Hessian term displayed above.  Applying
\eqref{eq:spde-finite-bochner-identity} to resolvent approximants and using
\eqref{eq:spde-brascamp-lieb-hessian-lower-bound} yields
\begin{equation}
  \int(\nabla u_\varepsilon,A_N\nabla u_\varepsilon)_{H_N}\,\dd\nu_N
  \leq
  \int(\mathcal L u_\varepsilon)^2\,\dd\nu_N .
  \label{eq:spde-bl-gradient-resolvent-bound}
\end{equation}
Taking \(\varepsilon\downarrow0\) gives
\begin{equation}
  \limsup_{\varepsilon\downarrow0}
  \int(\nabla u_\varepsilon,A_N\nabla u_\varepsilon)_{H_N}\,\dd\nu_N
  \leq
  \int f^2\,\dd\nu_N .
  \label{eq:spde-bl-gradient-limsup}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \int f^2\,\dd\nu_N
  &=
  \lim_{\varepsilon\downarrow0}
  \int(\nabla f,\nabla u_\varepsilon)_{H_N}\,\dd\nu_N
\\
  &\leq
  \left[
    \int(\nabla f,A_N^{-1}\nabla f)_{H_N}\,\dd\nu_N
  \right]^{1/2}
  \left[
    \limsup_{\varepsilon\downarrow0}
    \int(\nabla u_\varepsilon,A_N\nabla u_\varepsilon)_{H_N}\,\dd\nu_N
  \right]^{1/2}
\\
  &\leq
  \left[
    \int(\nabla f,A_N^{-1}\nabla f)_{H_N}\,\dd\nu_N
  \right]^{1/2}
  \left[
    \int f^2\,\dd\nu_N
  \right]^{1/2}.
\end{aligned}
\]
Dividing by \((\int f^2\,\dd\nu_N)^{1/2}\), and then applying this estimate
to \(f-\int f\,\dd\nu_N\), gives
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Var}_{\nu_N}(f)
  \leq
  \int(\nabla f,A_N^{-1}\nabla f)_{H_N}\,\dd\nu_N .
  \label{eq:spde-brascamp-lieb-general-bound}
\end{equation}
Linear functions are obtained by multiplying \(\ell_v\) by smooth radial
cutoffs and sending the cutoff radius to infinity; the quadratic lower bound
following from \eqref{eq:spde-brascamp-lieb-hessian-lower-bound} supplies the
needed dominated-convergence bounds.  Since
\(\nabla\ell_v=v\), \eqref{eq:spde-brascamp-lieb-linear-covariance} follows.

For the negative-Sobolev moment, the symmetry
\(\phi\mapsto-\phi\) gives
\(\int(\phi,e_{N,\alpha})_{H_N}\dd\nu_N=0\).  Applying
\eqref{eq:spde-brascamp-lieb-linear-covariance} with
\(v=e_{N,\alpha}\) and using \(A_N\geq L_N+m^2{\bf 1}\) gives
\[
  \int |(\phi,e_{N,\alpha})_{H_N}|^2\,\dd\nu_N(\phi)
  \leq
  (e_{N,\alpha},A_N^{-1}e_{N,\alpha})_{H_N}
  \leq
  (\lambda_{N,\alpha}+m^2)^{-1}.
\]
Multiplying by \((1+\lambda_{N,\alpha})^{-\eta}\) and summing over
\(\alpha\) proves
\eqref{eq:spde-convex-cutoff-hminus-moment-bound}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Closedness of OS reflection positivity under weak convergence]
\label{rem:spde-os-positivity-closed-under-weak-convergence}
Let \(E\) be a Hausdorff locally convex real vector space of Euclidean
fields, let \(\Theta:E\to E\) be a continuous involution, and let
\(\mu_N\Rightarrow\mu\) be weak convergence of Borel probability measures
on \(E\).  Let \(\mathcal A_+\) be an algebra of bounded continuous
cylinder functions on \(E\) such that
\[
  \Theta F(\phi)=F(\Theta\phi)
\]
is again a bounded continuous cylinder function whenever
\(F\in\mathcal A_+\).  If
\begin{equation}
  \int_E \overline{F(\Theta\phi)}\,F(\phi)\,\dd\mu_N(\phi)\geq0
  \qquad
  (F\in\mathcal A_+,\; N\geq1),
  \label{eq:spde-finite-cutoff-os-positivity}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
  \int_E \overline{F(\Theta\phi)}\,F(\phi)\,\dd\mu(\phi)\geq0
  \qquad(F\in\mathcal A_+).
  \label{eq:spde-limit-os-positivity}
\end{equation}
If \(F\) is an unbounded polynomial cylinder observable, the same conclusion
holds provided the random variables
\[
  \overline{F(\Theta\phi)}\,F(\phi)
\]
are uniformly integrable under \(\{\mu_N\}\) and integrable under \(\mu\),
and \(F\) is approximated by bounded continuous cylinder cutoffs in
\(\mathcal A_+\).
For \(F\in\mathcal A_+\), define
\[
  Q_F(\phi)=\overline{F(\Theta\phi)}\,F(\phi).
\]
Continuity of \(\Theta\) and bounded continuity of \(F\) imply that \(Q_F\)
is a bounded continuous function on \(E\).  Weak convergence therefore gives
\[
  \int_E Q_F\,\dd\mu
  =
  \lim_{N\to\infty}\int_E Q_F\,\dd\mu_N .
\]
Each term in the sequence on the right is nonnegative by
\eqref{eq:spde-finite-cutoff-os-positivity}; the limit is therefore
nonnegative, giving \eqref{eq:spde-limit-os-positivity}.

For an unbounded polynomial cylinder observable, choose bounded continuous
functions \(\chi_R\) on the finite-dimensional cylinder coordinate space
such that \(\chi_R=1\) on the radius-\(R\) ball, \(\chi_R=0\) outside the
radius-\(2R\) ball, and \(0\leq\chi_R\leq1\).  Set \(F_R=\chi_R F\).
The bounded part of this observation gives
\[
  \int_E \overline{F_R(\Theta\phi)}\,F_R(\phi)\,\dd\mu\geq0 .
\]
Uniform integrability of
\(\overline{F(\Theta\phi)}F(\phi)\) under \(\{\mu_N\}\), together with
integrability under \(\mu\), permits \(R\to\infty\) in the cutoff
quadratic form.  Hence the unbounded polynomial cylinder inequality follows
whenever the stated moment hypothesis is available.  This final step is
substantive: in constructive field theory it is exactly where uniform moment
or exponential-integrability estimates for the cutoff measures enter.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Fourier cutoffs and reflection-positive regulators]
\label{rem:spde-fourier-cutoff-os-regulator-separation}
The Fourier-Galerkin cutoff used above is an analytically convenient way to
construct the stochastic convolution and the local Da Prato--Debussche
solution map.  OS reflection positivity, however, is not a formal consequence
of being a reflection-symmetric ultraviolet cutoff.  It is a positivity
property of the Euclidean regulator with respect to a chosen time reflection.
Thus the reflection-positivity hypothesis in
Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-four-two-spde-main-theorem} must be read as a condition
on the actual cutoff family used to define the Euclidean measures, or else
one must prove a regulator-independence comparison between a
reflection-positive cutoff family and the Fourier-Galerkin SPDE
approximation.  The theorem below deliberately keeps this point visible:
Fourier cutoffs are used for the path-space stochastic estimates, while OS
positivity remains a separate regulator property until such a comparison is
proved.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Lattice scalar cutoffs as OS-positive Euclidean regulators]
\label{prop:spde-lattice-cutoff-os-positive-regulator}
Let \(\Lambda_{a,L}\) be a finite two-dimensional periodic lattice with
spacing \(a>0\), side length \(L\), and an involutive time reflection
\(\vartheta\) whose reflection plane is either a set of sites or a set of
mid-links.  Let
\[
  \dd\mu_{a,L}(\phi)
  =
  Z_{a,L}^{-1}e^{-S_{a,L}(\phi)}
  \prod_{x\in\Lambda_{a,L}}\dd\phi_x
\]
where
\[
  S_{a,L}(\phi)
  =
  \frac12\sum_{\langle x y\rangle}
  c_{xy}\,(\phi_x-\phi_y)^2
  +
  \sum_{x\in\Lambda_{a,L}}V_x(\phi_x).
\]
Assume \(c_{xy}=c_{\vartheta x,\vartheta y}>0\), the nearest-neighbor graph
is invariant under \(\vartheta\), \(V_{\vartheta x}=V_x\), and the finite
integral defining \(Z_{a,L}\) exists.  Let the reflected field be
\((\vartheta\phi)_x=\phi_{\vartheta x}\).  Then \(\mu_{a,L}\) is OS
reflection positive on bounded observables depending only on the chosen
nonnegative-time half-lattice, including the reflection plane when present:
\[
  \int \overline{F(\vartheta\phi)}\,F(\phi)\,\dd\mu_{a,L}(\phi)\geq0 .
\]
In particular, a lattice \(\Phi^4_2\) cutoff with reflection-invariant local
coordinates,
\[
  V_x(u)
  =
  a^2\left[
    \frac{m_{a,L}^2}{2}u^2
    +\frac{\lambda}{4}u^4
    +E_{a,L}
  \right],
  \qquad \lambda>0,
\]
and positive nearest-neighbor kinetic coefficients is reflection positive at
each finite cutoff whenever the displayed finite-dimensional integral is
finite.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
This is the scalar lattice reflection-positivity mechanism of
Proposition~\ref{prop:scalar-lattice-reflection-positivity}, specialized to
the regulators used in the constructive scalar theory.  We spell out the
assignment because it is the point at which the sign of the regulator is
used.  Split the lattice into the positive half, the reflected negative half,
and the reflection plane if the plane contains sites.  Terms contained
strictly in one half are assigned to \(S_+\) and \(\vartheta S_+\).
Reflection-plane on-site terms, and one half of every square term adjacent to
the plane, are split symmetrically.  A link crossing a mid-plane contributes
\[
  \frac12 c_{x,\vartheta x}(\phi_x-\phi_{\vartheta x})^2
  =
  \frac12 c_{x,\vartheta x}\phi_x^2
  +\frac12 c_{x,\vartheta x}\phi_{\vartheta x}^2
  -c_{x,\vartheta x}\phi_x\phi_{\vartheta x}.
\]
The first two summands have already been assigned to the two halves.  In
the Boltzmann weight the remaining cross-plane factor is therefore
\[
  \exp(c_{x,\vartheta x}\phi_x\phi_{\vartheta x})
  =
  \sum_{n=0}^{\infty}
  \frac{c_{x,\vartheta x}^{\,n}}{n!}\,
  \phi_x^n\phi_{\vartheta x}^{\,n},
\]
with nonnegative coefficients.  Multiplying these expansions for all
crossing links expresses the reflection quadratic form
\(\int\overline{F(\vartheta\phi)}F(\phi)\dd\mu_{a,L}\) as a sum of
nonnegative coefficients times absolute squares of half-lattice integrals.
Hence the quadratic form is nonnegative.  The local potential and local
counterterm coordinates do not enter this sign argument except through
reflection invariance, reality, and integrability, because they are assigned
to the two halves before the cross-plane kernel is expanded.
\end{proof}

Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-lattice-cutoff-os-positive-regulator} proves the
finite-cutoff OS-positivity input for a concrete lattice Euclidean regulator.
Identifying that lattice family with the Fourier-Galerkin family used in the
stochastic convolution estimates above is a separate comparison theorem.
After matching the relevant local coordinates, one must prove convergence of
the lattice and Fourier-Galerkin Schwinger functions, or construct a single
regulator whose Langevin estimates and OS positivity are both available.  Such
a theorem must supply analytic estimates beyond either weak convergence or
stochastic stationarity.

\begin{remark}[Regulator comparison criterion for OS-positive stochastic limits]
\label{rem:spde-regulator-comparison-os-criterion}
Let \(E\) be a Hausdorff locally convex real vector space of Euclidean
fields, let \(\Theta:E\to E\) be a continuous involution, and let
\(\{\mu_N^{\mathrm F}\}\) and \(\{\mu_N^{\mathrm L}\}\) be two cutoff
families of Borel probability measures on \(E\).  Think of
\(\mu_N^{\mathrm F}\) as the Fourier-Galerkin stochastic cutoff family and
\(\mu_N^{\mathrm L}\) as a lattice cutoff family, but assume only the
following properties.

First, suppose that
\[
  \mu_N^{\mathrm F}\Rightarrow\mu
  \qquad\text{weakly on }E.
\]
Second, let \(\mathcal A_+\) be an algebra of bounded continuous cylinder
observables supported in nonnegative Euclidean time, and assume finite-cutoff
OS positivity for the lattice family:
\begin{equation}
  \int_E \overline{F(\Theta\phi)}\,F(\phi)\,
  \dd\mu_N^{\mathrm L}(\phi)
  \geq0,
  \qquad F\in\mathcal A_+.
  \label{eq:spde-lattice-family-os-positive}
\end{equation}
Third, assume comparison of bounded cylinder observables in the following
literal sense: for every bounded continuous cylinder function \(G\) in the
algebra generated by \(\mathcal A_+\) and its reflected observables,
\begin{equation}
  \int_E G(\phi)\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm F}(\phi)
  -
  \int_E G(\phi)\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm L}(\phi)
  \longrightarrow0 .
  \label{eq:spde-bounded-cylinder-regulator-comparison}
\end{equation}
Then the Fourier-Galerkin limiting measure \(\mu\) is OS reflection positive
on \(\mathcal A_+\):
\begin{equation}
  \int_E \overline{F(\Theta\phi)}\,F(\phi)\,\dd\mu(\phi)\geq0,
  \qquad F\in\mathcal A_+.
  \label{eq:spde-regulator-comparison-limit-os-positive}
\end{equation}

Let now \(P\) be a polynomial cylinder observable in finitely many continuous
linear coordinates.  Assume that bounded continuous cutoffs \(P_R\) of
\(P\) can be chosen in the comparison algebra and that
\[
  |P_R(\phi)-P(\phi)|
  \leq
  2|P(\phi)|\,{\bf 1}_{\{|P(\phi)|>R\}},
  \qquad
  P_R(\phi)\to P(\phi)
\]
pointwise.  If the random variables \(|P|^2\) are uniformly integrable with
respect to both cutoff families
\(\{\mu_N^{\mathrm F}\}\), \(\{\mu_N^{\mathrm L}\}\), and are integrable
with respect to \(\mu\), then both cutoff limits exist and
\[
  \int_E P\,\dd\mu
  =
  \lim_{N\to\infty}\int_E P\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm F}
  =
  \lim_{N\to\infty}\int_E P\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm L}
\]
holds.  If, in addition, \(F\) is a positive-time polynomial observable and
\(|\overline{F\circ\Theta}F|\) has the same uniform-integrability property,
then the OS inequality also holds for \(F\).
For bounded \(F\in\mathcal A_+\), set
\[
  Q_F(\phi)=\overline{F(\Theta\phi)}\,F(\phi).
\]
The function \(Q_F\) is a bounded continuous cylinder observable in the
comparison algebra.  Weak convergence of \(\mu_N^{\mathrm F}\) gives
\[
  \int_E Q_F\,\dd\mu
  =
  \lim_{N\to\infty}\int_E Q_F\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm F}.
\]
The comparison hypothesis
\eqref{eq:spde-bounded-cylinder-regulator-comparison} gives
\[
  \lim_{N\to\infty}\int_E Q_F\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm F}
  =
  \lim_{N\to\infty}\int_E Q_F\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm L}
\]
because the Fourier limit exists and the difference tends to zero.  Each
lattice integral is nonnegative by
\eqref{eq:spde-lattice-family-os-positive}; hence its limit inferior is
nonnegative.  This proves
\eqref{eq:spde-regulator-comparison-limit-os-positive}.

For a polynomial cylinder observable \(P\), fix \(R\).  Since \(P_R\) is
bounded and belongs to the comparison algebra,
\[
  \lim_{N\to\infty}
  \left[
    \int_E P_R\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm F}
    -
    \int_E P_R\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm L}
  \right]
  =0,
\]
and weak convergence of \(\mu_N^{\mathrm F}\) gives
\[
  \int_E P_R\,\dd\mu
  =
  \lim_{N\to\infty}\int_E P_R\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm F}.
\]
Uniform integrability allows \(R\to\infty\) uniformly in \(N\):
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \left|
    \int(P-P_R)\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm F}
  \right|
  &\leq
  2\int |P|\,{\bf 1}_{\{|P|>R\}}\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm F},\\
  \left|
    \int(P-P_R)\,\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm L}
  \right|
  &\leq
  2\int |P|\,{\bf 1}_{\{|P|>R\}}\dd\mu_N^{\mathrm L}.
\end{aligned}
\]
The two \(L^1\)-tails tend to zero uniformly in \(N\), because uniform
integrability of \(|P|^2\) implies uniform integrability of \(|P|\) by
Cauchy's inequality.  Dominated convergence gives
\(\int P_R\,\dd\mu\to\int P\,\dd\mu\).  Taking first \(N\to\infty\) at fixed
\(R\), then \(R\to\infty\), proves equality of the polynomial
Schwinger-function limits.  Applying the same truncation argument to
\(P=Q_F=\overline{F\circ\Theta}F\), after using the bounded part for each
truncated \(F_R\), gives the polynomial OS inequality.
\end{remark}

The analytic comparison
\eqref{eq:spde-bounded-cylinder-regulator-comparison} is a separate
constructive estimate; the criterion records what such a comparison must
deliver.  In \(\Phi^4_2\), the comparison is a constructive statement about
two renormalized cutoff families in the same finite-volume local-coordinate
chart.  It must identify the mass and vacuum coordinates, prove convergence
of bounded smeared-field observables, and provide the uniform-integrability
estimates needed to remove the bounded truncations.  Once these estimates are
proved, lattice reflection positivity from
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-lattice-cutoff-os-positive-regulator} transfers to
the stochastic Fourier-Galerkin limit by the criterion above.

\begin{remark}[Polynomial OS observables from exponential moments]
\label{rem:spde-polynomial-os-uniform-integrability}
Let \(E\) be a Hausdorff locally convex real vector space, and let
\(\mu_N\Rightarrow\mu\) be Borel probability measures on \(E\).  Let
\(\ell_1,\ldots,\ell_r\) be continuous real linear functionals on \(E\), and
fix \(q>0\), \(\alpha>0\).  Put
\[
  V(\phi)=1+\sum_{j=1}^r|\ell_j(\phi)|^q .
\]
Assume
\begin{equation}
  \sup_N\int_E e^{\alpha V(\phi)}\,\dd\mu_N(\phi)<\infty,
  \qquad
  \int_E e^{\alpha V(\phi)}\,\dd\mu(\phi)<\infty .
  \label{eq:spde-exponential-cylinder-moment-bound}
\end{equation}
Then for every polynomial \(P\in\C[u_1,\ldots,u_r]\), the random variables
\[
  |P(\ell_1(\phi),\ldots,\ell_r(\phi))|^2
\]
are uniformly integrable with respect to \(\{\mu_N\}\) and integrable with
respect to \(\mu\).  Hence the unbounded polynomial-cylinder step in
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-os-positivity-closed-under-weak-convergence}
follows for such \(P\) whenever the bounded-cylinder reflection-positivity
inequality is available.

There is a constant \(C_P<\infty\) such that, for all \(u\in\R^r\),
\begin{equation}
  |P(u)|^2\leq C_P
  \exp\!\left(\frac{\alpha}{2}
    \left[1+\sum_{j=1}^r|u_j|^q\right]\right).
  \label{eq:spde-polynomial-by-exponential-bound}
\end{equation}
This is the elementary domination of polynomial growth by exponential
growth: each monomial is bounded by a constant times
\(\exp[(\alpha/4r)|u_j|^q]\) in each variable appearing in it, and the
finite sum of monomials is absorbed into \(C_P\).  Let
\[
  A(\phi)=
  \exp\!\left(\frac{\alpha}{2}V(\phi)\right).
\]
If \(|P(\ell(\phi))|^2>R\), then
\(C_PA(\phi)>R\).  Therefore
\[
  |P(\ell(\phi))|^2
  {\bf 1}_{\{|P(\ell(\phi))|^2>R\}}
  \leq
  C_P A(\phi)\,{\bf 1}_{\{A(\phi)>R/C_P\}}
  \leq
  \frac{C_P^2}{R}A(\phi)^2 .
\]
Integrating and using
\(A^2=e^{\alpha V}\) gives
\[
  \sup_N
  \int |P(\ell(\phi))|^2
  {\bf 1}_{\{|P(\ell(\phi))|^2>R\}}\,\dd\mu_N(\phi)
  \leq
  \frac{C_P^2}{R}
  \sup_N\int e^{\alpha V}\,\dd\mu_N
  \longrightarrow0 .
\]
This is uniform integrability.  The same estimate with \(\mu\) instead of
\(\mu_N\) gives integrability under the limiting measure.  Applying
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-os-positivity-closed-under-weak-convergence} to
bounded truncations of \(P(\ell_1,\ldots,\ell_r)\) proves the final claim.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Finite lattice quartic tails]
\label{lem:spde-finite-lattice-quartic-tails}
Let \(\Lambda\) be a finite set and let \(\mu\) be a finite-dimensional
scalar lattice measure
\[
  \dd\mu(\phi)=Z^{-1}e^{-S(\phi)}\prod_{x\in\Lambda}\dd\phi_x ,
  \qquad
  S(\phi)=K(\phi)+\sum_{x\in\Lambda}V_x(\phi_x),
\]
where \(K(\phi)\geq0\).  Suppose that, for constants \(a_x>0\),
\(b_x\geq0\), and \(d_x\in\R\),
\begin{equation}
  V_x(u)\geq a_xu^4-b_xu^2-d_x .
  \label{eq:spde-finite-lattice-quartic-coercivity}
\end{equation}
Then \(Z<\infty\), and for every \(0<\varepsilon<1\),
\begin{equation}
  \int
  \exp\!\left(\varepsilon\sum_{x\in\Lambda}a_x\phi_x^4\right)
  \dd\mu(\phi)
  <\infty .
  \label{eq:spde-finite-lattice-quartic-exponential-tail}
\end{equation}
Consequently every polynomial cylinder observable has finite moments at this
finite cutoff.  A uniform version of
\eqref{eq:spde-finite-lattice-quartic-exponential-tail} along a continuum
cutoff family is a separate estimate; if it is available for the smeared
coordinates entering an OS polynomial cylinder observable, then
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-polynomial-os-uniform-integrability} supplies the
uniform integrability needed to pass that observable to the limit.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Since \(K\geq0\), the density is bounded above by
\[
  \exp\!\left[
    -\sum_x a_x\phi_x^4+\sum_x b_x\phi_x^2+\sum_x d_x
  \right].
\]
For \(A_x=(1-\varepsilon)a_x\), the elementary inequality
\[
  b_xu^2\leq\frac{A_x}{2}u^4+\frac{b_x^2}{2A_x}
\]
gives
\[
  -A_xu^4+b_xu^2
  \leq
  -\frac{A_x}{2}u^4+\frac{b_x^2}{2A_x}.
\]
Therefore
\[
  e^{\varepsilon\sum_x a_x\phi_x^4}e^{-S(\phi)}
  \leq
  \exp\!\left[
    \sum_x d_x+\sum_x\frac{b_x^2}{2(1-\varepsilon)a_x}
  \right]
  \prod_x
  \exp\!\left[-\frac{(1-\varepsilon)a_x}{2}\phi_x^4\right].
\]
The product on the right is integrable over \(\R^\Lambda\).  Taking
\(\varepsilon=0\) in the same estimate proves \(Z<\infty\), while \(Z>0\)
because the density is positive on a set of positive Lebesgue measure.
Dividing by \(Z\) proves
\eqref{eq:spde-finite-lattice-quartic-exponential-tail}.  Polynomial
moments follow because every power of \(|u|\) is bounded by a constant times
\(e^{\delta u^4}\) for any fixed \(\delta>0\).  The final sentence is exactly
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-polynomial-os-uniform-integrability}
applied to the finite list of smeared cylinder coordinates.
\end{proof}

\begin{hypothesis}[\(\Phi^4_2\) stochastic-quantization assembly inputs on the torus]
\label{hyp:phi-four-two-spde-assembly-inputs}
Fix \(m^2>0\), \(\lambda>0\), \(0<\kappa<1/4\), and
\(\beta=1+2\kappa\).  Let \(P_N\) be a reflection-symmetric Fourier cutoff
on \(\mathbb T^2\).  Let \(\mu_N\) be the finite-dimensional Wick-ordered
Gibbs measure
\[
  \dd\mu_N(\phi)
  =
  Z_N^{-1}
  \exp\!\left[
    -\frac{\lambda}{4}\int_{\mathbb T^2}:\!(P_N\phi)^4\!:\,\dd^2x
  \right]\dd\mu_{0,N}(\phi),
\]
where \(\mu_{0,N}\) is the massive Gaussian law with covariance
\(P_N(-\Delta+m^2)^{-1}P_N\).  Let \(P_t^{(N)}\) be the Markov semigroup of
the corresponding finite-dimensional stochastic quantization equation, and
embed all laws in \(H^{-\kappa}(\mathbb T^2)\).  By
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-two-dimensional-enhanced-noise-path-convergence},
the enhanced Ornstein--Uhlenbeck fields
\[
  \mathbb X_N=(X_N,:\!X_N^2\!:,:\!X_N^3\!:)
\]
converge in probability in \(C([0,T];H^{-\kappa})^3\), for every
\(T<\infty\), to a limit
\(\mathbb X=(X,:\!X^2\!:,:\!X^3\!:)\).

Assume the following three further analytic facts.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
  \item For every \(Y_0\in H^\beta\), the local solution map of
  Theorem~\ref{thm:spde-dpd-deterministic-local-fixed-point} extends
  globally in stochastic time, and the cutoff solution maps converge to it
  uniformly on compact subsets of the enhanced-noise/initial-data space.
  Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-dpd-global-compact-continuity-criterion}
  reduces this assertion, in the Besov formulation, to a blow-up
  alternative plus a rough energy-to-Besov a priori bound on compact
  enhanced-noise sets.
  \item The stationary laws \(\{\mu_N\}\) are tight in \(H^{-\kappa}\), and
  every weak limit \(\mu\) is carried by fields admitting the decomposition
  \(\Phi=X+Y\) with \(Y\) given by the global DPD solution map.  By
  Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-sobolev-compactness-tightness}, this tightness
  follows from a cutoff-uniform moment bound in \(H^{-\eta}\) for some
  \(0<\eta<\kappa\); the interacting stationary cutoff family therefore
  requires an independent constructive estimate establishing that moment
  bound before the weak-convergence passage is invoked.  The corresponding
  free massive Gaussian estimate is
  Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-free-gaussian-negative-sobolev-tightness}.
  Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-lq-density-negative-sobolev-moment} and
  Remark~\ref{rem:spde-phi-four-two-density-tightness-route} gives one
  precise route: a cutoff-uniform \(L^q\) bound for the normalized
  Wick-ordered density with respect to the massive Gaussian reference law
  implies the required interacting negative-Sobolev moments.  If the cutoff
  Wick quartic satisfies the Nelson stability estimate
  \eqref{eq:spde-nelson-stability-exponential-input}, then
	  Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-nelson-stability-implies-lq-density} proves
  this \(L^q\) density bound.
  \item Reflection positivity of the cutoff measures \(\mu_N\) holds for
  bounded cylinder observables depending on positive Euclidean time, and
  the polynomial Wick observables used to identify Schwinger functions obey
  the uniform-integrability bounds needed for the truncation step in
  Remark~\ref{rem:spde-os-positivity-closed-under-weak-convergence}.
  This is a property of the chosen Euclidean regulator and must be proved for
  the regulator used in the limiting construction.  For the lattice scalar
  regulator of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-lattice-cutoff-os-positive-regulator}, the
  bounded-observable positivity statement is proved at finite cutoff, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-finite-lattice-quartic-tails} proves
  finite-cutoff polynomial integrability.  Passing polynomial observables
  uniformly through the continuum limit requires the exponential moment
  criterion of
  Remark~\ref{rem:spde-polynomial-os-uniform-integrability}.  Using
  lattice positivity in the present Fourier-Galerkin stochastic assembly
  requires the bounded-cylinder and uniform-integrability comparison
  hypotheses stated in
  Remark~\ref{rem:spde-regulator-comparison-os-criterion}.  A
  sufficient condition for the bounded-cylinder comparison part is the
  common \(L^1\) density-limit criterion of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-density-limit}; a
  still more primitive sufficient condition, stated in terms of convergence
  of the renormalized interaction potentials and a uniform \(L^p\) stability
  estimate for their exponential weights, is
  Corollary~\ref{cor:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-potential}.  For the
  two-dimensional Wick quartic interaction, the potential convergence part
  of this condition follows from
  Remark~\ref{rem:spde-wick-quartic-potential-convergence}; the remaining
  regulator-specific input is the uniform exponential-weight stability.
  The common finite cylinder-coordinate convergence for smeared Wick
  polynomials is supplied by
  Remark~\ref{rem:spde-common-wick-coordinate-limits}.  Equivalently,
  under these common Wick-limit hypotheses and the uniform \(L^p\) stability
  bound, the bounded Wick-cylinder comparison is precisely
  \eqref{eq:spde-stable-quartic-bounded-cylinder-comparison}.
  The common Wick-limit hypothesis itself can be checked from mixed
  covariance convergence by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-mixed-covariance-common-wick-limits}; for
  smooth compactly supported Fourier multiplier cutoffs, that covariance
  convergence is proved by
  Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-smooth-fourier-multiplier-covariance-convergence}.
  If, in addition, those smooth regulators satisfy the Nelson stability
  input, the density bounds, tightness, and bounded Wick-cylinder comparison
  are collected in
  Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-smooth-regulator-nelson-consequences}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{theorem}[\(\Phi^4_2\) stochastic-quantization assembly on the torus]
\label{thm:phi-four-two-spde-main-theorem}
Under Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:phi-four-two-spde-assembly-inputs}, every weak limit
\(\mu\) of \(\{\mu_N\}\) is an invariant law of the
limiting DPD Markov semigroup.  Its Schwinger functions are the limits of
the finite-cutoff Wick-ordered Schwinger functions, and \(\mu\) satisfies OS
reflection positivity for cylinder observables.  If, in addition, the
resulting Schwinger hierarchy satisfies the moment-continuity,
positive-time semigroup, and corrected OS-II linear-growth hypotheses in
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-invariant-law-os-reconstruction-criterion}, then
the hierarchy determines a two-dimensional Wightman theory by
Theorem~\ref{thm:os-reconstruction}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
At finite cutoff the Langevin generator is the gradient generator of the
finite-dimensional action defining \(\mu_N\).  The integration-by-parts
identity \eqref{eq:finite-dimensional-dirichlet-form}, together with the
finite-dimensional semigroup hypotheses recorded in
Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-cutoff-langevin-reversibility}, therefore gives
\[
  \int P_t^{(N)}F\,\dd\mu_N=\int F\,\dd\mu_N
\]
for every bounded smooth cylinder function \(F\).  Thus the word
``stationary'' at finite cutoff means reversibility and invariance of the
Markov semigroup in the cutoff Hilbert space, not only a formal adjoint
calculation for the infinitesimal generator.

The stochastic input is
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-two-dimensional-enhanced-noise-path-convergence},
which strengthens the equal-time Wick-power construction of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-two-dimensional-wick-powers} to path-space
convergence and fixes the Wick normalization.  Given this enhanced noise,
the products in the DPD nonlinearity are defined by
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-dpd-sobolev-products}, and
Theorem~\ref{thm:spde-dpd-deterministic-local-fixed-point} gives the local
solution map.  Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:phi-four-two-spde-assembly-inputs}\textup{(a)}
is precisely the global rough-energy and
compact-continuity upgrade of the smooth estimate
	Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-dpd-smooth-energy-estimate}; in the Besov
topology this upgrade is organized by
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-dpd-global-compact-continuity-criterion}.  Thus
the limiting Markov semigroup \(P_t\) is well-defined on the support of every
weak stationary limit in
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:phi-four-two-spde-assembly-inputs}\textup{(b)}, and
\(P_t^{(N)}F\to P_tF\) uniformly on the high-probability compact sets supplied
by Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:phi-four-two-spde-assembly-inputs}\textup{(a),(b)}.

Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-invariant-measure-limit} now applies with
\(E=H^{-\kappa}\).  Therefore
\[
  \int P_tF\,\dd\mu=\int F\,\dd\mu
\]
for every bounded continuous cylinder observable \(F\), and hence \(\mu\) is
invariant.  The convergence of Schwinger functions follows by applying the
same weak convergence to products of smeared fields and Wick powers after
approximating the polynomial observables by bounded cylinder observables;
the uniform moment bounds needed for this approximation are part of the
tightness and rough-energy input in
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:phi-four-two-spde-assembly-inputs}\textup{(b)}.

For OS positivity, let \(\Theta\) be Euclidean time reflection and let
\(F\) be a cylinder observable supported in positive Euclidean time.  The
finite-cutoff reflection-positivity assumption gives
\[
  \int \overline{\Theta F}\,F\,\dd\mu_N\geq0 .
\]
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-os-positivity-closed-under-weak-convergence}
passes this inequality to the weak limit, so
\[
  \int \overline{\Theta F}\,F\,\dd\mu\geq0 .
\]
This is OS reflection positivity on the cylinder algebra.  Once the
remaining OS growth and regularity estimates are verified, the OS
reconstruction theorem of Chapter~\ref{ch:os-reconstruction} applies.
\end{proof}

The theorem separates the logical assembly from the analytic estimates.  In
the chapter we have proved the finite-dimensional Langevin identity, the
Sobolev Wick-power construction, the path-space enhanced-noise convergence,
the Sobolev DPD local solution map, the smooth enhanced-noise energy
inequality, and the abstract invariant-law passage.  The sharp global
two-dimensional theorem still requires four further inputs: a rough
energy-to-Besov bound strong enough, by
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-dpd-global-compact-continuity-criterion}, to
give global compact-continuity of the DPD solution map; a cutoff-uniform
negative-Sobolev moment strong enough to imply tightness by
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-sobolev-compactness-tightness}; for Wick
\(\Phi^4_2\) this moment follows from the density criterion
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-phi-four-two-density-tightness-route} once the
uniform Nelson-type \(L^q\) density bound is proved, and
	Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-nelson-stability-implies-lq-density} proves that
bound from the Nelson exponential stability estimate; uniform integrability;
and either finite-cutoff OS positivity for the stochastic regulator itself or
a regulator-comparison theorem relating it to the
OS-positive lattice regulator of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-lattice-cutoff-os-positive-regulator}.  The
abstract form of the latter implication is
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-regulator-comparison-os-criterion}; the bounded
cylinder comparison follows from
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-density-limit} if the two
regulators have a common \(L^1\) interaction-density limit and identical
limiting cylinder coordinates; by
Corollary~\ref{cor:spde-bounded-cylinder-common-potential}, the common
\(L^1\) density limit follows from convergence in probability of the
renormalized interaction potentials plus a uniform \(L^p\) stability bound
on the exponential weights.  For the Wick quartic potential, the convergence
in probability is supplied by
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-wick-quartic-potential-convergence}, so the
remaining constructive estimate is the uniform \(L^p\) stability of the
weights in the chosen regulator family.  The matching convergence of finite
Wick-coordinate cylinder vectors is
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-common-wick-coordinate-limits}; combined with the
stability estimate, these inputs give the bounded comparison statement
\eqref{eq:spde-stable-quartic-bounded-cylinder-comparison}.
The common Wick-limit hypothesis is reduced to a covariance estimate by
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-mixed-covariance-common-wick-limits}, and for
smooth Fourier multiplier cutoffs the needed covariance estimate follows
from
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-smooth-fourier-multiplier-covariance-convergence}.
The uniform-integrability input can be supplied by the exponential
cylinder-moment criterion in
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-polynomial-os-uniform-integrability}; finite
quartic tails at each lattice cutoff are proved by
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-finite-lattice-quartic-tails}, while uniformity
as the cutoff is removed remains part of the constructive estimate.  These
inputs are listed explicitly in
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:phi-four-two-spde-assembly-inputs}.

\paragraph{Sharp two-dimensional DPD closure status.}
The classical two-dimensional Da Prato--Debussche construction packages a
local pathwise solution, global extension from the dissipative quartic drift,
and identification of the invariant law with the Wick-ordered Euclidean
\(\Phi^4_2\) measure on a finite torus.  In this chapter that package is
used through the explicit ingredients above, rather than as an imported
black box.  The mild form of \eqref{eq:dpd-remainder-equation} is
\[
  Y(\tau)
  =
  e^{\tau(\Delta-m^2)}Y(0)
  -
  \lambda\int_0^\tau
  e^{(\tau-s)(\Delta-m^2)}
  \mathcal N(Y(s),\mathbb X(s))\,\dd s ,
\]
where \(\mathcal N\) is the cubic expression in
\eqref{eq:dpd-remainder-equation}.  Parabolic Schauder estimates increase
spatial regularity by two derivatives relative to the forcing; the Sobolev
version is the heat-kernel estimate
\eqref{eq:spde-heat-kernel-smoothing}, while the
sharp two-dimensional fixed point uses the corresponding parabolic
Besov--Holder estimates.
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-two-dimensional-wick-powers} constructs the Wick
powers in a Sobolev topology; the sharper fixed-point input places
\(:\!X^2\!:\) and \(:\!X^3\!:\) in negative Holder/Besov spaces of
arbitrarily small negative regularity.
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-dpd-sobolev-products} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:spde-dpd-deterministic-local-fixed-point} give a
self-contained Sobolev version of the local fixed-point argument.  The sharp
proof upgrades these Sobolev exponents to the scale-invariant parabolic
Besov--Holder spaces.  Multiplying the equation by \(Y\), integrating over
space, and using the sign of
\(\lambda Y^4\) gives an energy inequality with random lower-order forcing;
the local rough-forcing estimate
\eqref{eq:spde-local-rough-forcing-estimate} is the precise remaining
estimate that turns this energy mechanism into the global
compact-continuity input of
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:phi-four-two-spde-assembly-inputs}.  The invariant law
is identified through finite-cutoff Langevin reversibility, tightness, and
regulator comparison.  Those steps have been reduced above to Nelson
stability for the chosen Wick quartic cutoff family, common Wick-coordinate
limits, uniform integrability of polynomial cylinders, and the OS-II growth
conditions in
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-invariant-law-os-reconstruction-criterion}.  Thus the
remaining two-dimensional work is a finite list of constructive estimates,
not a separate theorem imported under the name Da Prato--Debussche.

\subsection{Why the Two-Dimensional Decomposition Fails in Three Dimensions}
\label{subsec:spde-dpd-three-dimensional-obstruction}

\begin{remark}[Sobolev DPD closure and the three-dimensional obstruction]
\label{rem:spde-sobolev-dpd-three-dimensional-obstruction}
The Sobolev fixed-point mechanism used above for \(\Phi^4_2\) cannot close
the dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\) equation by replacing \(2\) with \(3\).  More
precisely, let \(X\) be the three-dimensional stationary stochastic
convolution.  Its spatial regularity is
\[
  X\in H^{-1/2-\kappa-\varepsilon}(\mathbb T^3)
  \quad\text{for every }\varepsilon>0,
\]
and the cubic Wick power has the formal Sobolev regularity
\[
  :\!X^3\!:\in H^{-3/2-3\kappa-\varepsilon}(\mathbb T^3)
  \quad\text{for every }\varepsilon>0.
\]
If the remainder \(Y\) is sought in \(H^\beta\), then even the minimal
Sobolev multiplier requirement for the product \(YX\) is
\begin{equation}
  \beta>\frac12+\kappa .
  \label{eq:spde-three-dpd-minimal-multiplier-threshold}
\end{equation}
The Duhamel map from the cubic forcing
\(:\!X^3\!:\) to \(H^\beta\) would require
\begin{equation}
  \theta
  =
  \frac{\beta+\frac32+3\kappa}{2}>1 .
  \label{eq:spde-three-dpd-duhamel-obstruction}
\end{equation}
But the heat-kernel Duhamel estimate
\eqref{eq:spde-duhamel-smoothing} is locally integrable at the upper time
endpoint only for \(\theta<1\).  Therefore the two-dimensional Sobolev DPD
argument has no three-dimensional analogue.
\par
The covariance of the massive three-dimensional Gaussian field has
short-distance singularity \(\|x-y\|^{-1}\).  Equivalently, the field has
Sobolev regularity below \(-1/2\), and the \(k\)-th Wick power has the
additive formal regularity below \(-k/2\).  With the small loss parameter
\(\kappa\), this gives the displayed regularities for \(X\) and
\(:\!X^3\!:\).

For multiplication in three spatial dimensions, a distribution of regularity
\(-1/2-\kappa\) can be multiplied by a Sobolev function of regularity
\(\beta\) only when the sum of regularities is positive; this gives
\eqref{eq:spde-three-dpd-minimal-multiplier-threshold}.  If the forcing is
in \(H^{-3/2-3\kappa-\varepsilon}\), reaching \(H^\beta\) by the heat
equation requires, after letting \(\varepsilon\downarrow0\), gain
\[
  2\theta>\beta+\frac32+3\kappa .
\]
Combining this with
\eqref{eq:spde-three-dpd-minimal-multiplier-threshold} gives
\[
  \theta
  >
  \frac{\frac12+\kappa+\frac32+3\kappa}{2}
  =
  1+2\kappa .
\]
This contradicts the condition \(\theta<1\) needed for the time singularity
\((t-s)^{-\theta}\) to be integrable.  If one instead requires
\(H^\beta\) to be an algebra, then \(\beta>3/2\), and the obstruction is
even stronger:
\(\theta>3/2+\frac32\kappa\).  Thus the failure is structural, not an
artifact of a nonoptimal exponent choice.
\end{remark}

\section{\texorpdfstring{Regularity Structures and \(\Phi^4_3\)}{Regularity Structures and Phi-four-three}}

In three spatial dimensions the decomposition \(\Phi=X+Y\) is not
sufficient: \(X\) has regularity \(-\frac12-\kappa\), and the products
generated by the cubic drift fall below the classical multiplication
threshold.  Regularity structures supply the missing local expansion
calculus.

\subsection{Models, Modelled Distributions, and Reconstruction}
\label{subsec:spde-regularity-models-reconstruction}

\begin{definition}[Regularity structure]
\label{def:regularity-structure}
A regularity structure is a triple \((A,T,G)\), where \(A\subset\R\) is a
locally finite set of homogeneities bounded below, \(T=\bigoplus_{\alpha\in
A}T_\alpha\) is a graded model space, and \(G\) is a structure group acting
on \(T\) such that for \(\tau\in T_\alpha\),
\[
  \Gamma\tau-\tau\in\bigoplus_{\beta<\alpha}T_\beta
  \qquad(\Gamma\in G).
\]
A model on spacetime assigns to every point \(z\) a linear map
\(\Pi_z:T\to\mathcal D'(\R^{1+d})\) and to every pair \(z,z'\) an element
\(\Gamma_{zz'}\in G\), satisfying
\[
  \Pi_z=\Pi_{z'}\Gamma_{z'z},\qquad
  \Gamma_{zz'}\Gamma_{z'z''}=\Gamma_{zz''},
\]
together with analytic bounds compatible with the homogeneities.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Parabolic model and modelled-distribution norms]
\label{def:spde-parabolic-modelled-distribution-norms}
Let \(\mathfrak s=(2,1,\ldots,1)\) be the parabolic scaling on
\(\R^{1+d}\), let \(|\mathfrak s|=d+2\), and set
\[
  \|(\tau,x)\|_{\mathfrak s}
  =
  |\tau|^{1/2}+|x_1|+\cdots+|x_d|.
\]
For \(0<\delta\leq1\), \(z\in\R^{1+d}\), and
