by enlarging the finite index set \(I\).  The model construction for
dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\) must therefore provide, for each negative tree and each
coordinate chart entering the model seminorm, the two estimates appearing in
the theorem: the uniform coordinate moment estimate and the dyadic cutoff
increment estimate with enough excess exponent \(\varepsilon_i\) to dominate
the metric entropy of the coordinate parameters.

For dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\), the symbols are generated by the noise \(\Xi\), the
abstract integration map \(\mathcal I\), multiplication, and polynomials in
the spacetime coordinates.  Negative-homogeneity trees encode precisely the
subdivergent stochastic diagrams.  Renormalization acts on these trees before
the reconstruction theorem is applied.

\begin{lemma}[Finite negative-sector coordinates for dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\)]
\label{lem:spde-phi-four-three-negative-sector-coordinate-chart}
Let \(0<\kappa<1/14\), and set
\[
  X=\mathcal I(\Xi),\qquad
  Y=\mathcal I(X^3),\qquad
  |X|=-\frac12-\kappa,\qquad |Y|=\frac12-3\kappa .
\]
Put
\[
  \gamma_-=\frac12-7\kappa>0 .
\]
Among the monomials \(X^aY^b\) with \(a+b\leq3\), the non-polynomial
symbols of homogeneity \(<\gamma_-\) are
\begin{equation}
  X,\quad X^2,\quad X^3,\quad XY,\quad X^2Y .
  \label{eq:spde-negative-sector-monomial-list}
\end{equation}
Together with the noise symbol \(\Xi\) and the constant symbol \(\mathbf 1\),
these form the finite sector
\[
  \mathcal T_-=
  \{\mathbf 1,\Xi,X,X^2,X^3,XY,X^2Y\}.
\]
Their homogeneities are
\[
\begin{array}{c|c}
  \tau & |\tau|\\
  \hline
  \mathbf 1 & 0\\
  \Xi & -\frac52-\kappa\\
  X & -\frac12-\kappa\\
  X^2 & -1-2\kappa\\
  X^3 & -\frac32-3\kappa\\
  XY & -4\kappa\\
  X^2Y & -\frac12-5\kappa .
\end{array}
\]
The excluded cubic monomial \(XY^2\) has homogeneity
\[
  |XY^2|=\gamma_-,
\]
and is therefore not part of the strict sector \(T_{<\gamma_-}\).

Let \(Z_n=(\Pi^{(n)},\Gamma^{(n)})\) be cutoff models whose restriction to
\(\mathcal T_-\) is multiplicative and whose reexpansion of \(Y\), modulo
terms of homogeneity \(\geq\gamma_-\), has the form
\begin{equation}
  \Gamma_{zz'}^{(n)}Y
  =
  Y+c_n(z,z')\mathbf 1 .
  \label{eq:spde-y-reexpansion-coefficient}
\end{equation}
Then, on \(\mathcal T_-\), the only strict lower stochastic reexpansion
coefficients are
\begin{equation}
  \Gamma_{zz'}^{(n)}(XY)
  =
  XY+c_n(z,z')X,
  \qquad
  \Gamma_{zz'}^{(n)}(X^2Y)
  =
  X^2Y+c_n(z,z')X^2 .
  \label{eq:spde-negative-sector-gamma-coordinates}
\end{equation}
In particular, for a compact \(K\), the model seminorm below
\(\gamma_-\) is controlled by the following explicit coordinate fields:
\[
  P_{n,\tau}(z,\delta,\varphi)
  =
  \delta^{-|\tau|}
  \left|
    \langle\Pi_z^{(n)}\tau,\varphi_z^\delta\rangle
  \right|,
  \qquad
  \tau\in\{\Xi,X,X^2,X^3,XY,X^2Y\},
\]
and
\[
  G_n(z,z')
  =
  \frac{|c_n(z,z')|}
       {\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,|Y|}}
  \qquad
  (0<\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq1).
\]
More precisely, with the basis vectors above assigned norm one,
\begin{equation}
  1+\|\Pi^{(n)}\|_{K;\gamma_-}+\|\Gamma^{(n)}\|_{K;\gamma_-}
  \leq
  A_-
  \left(
    1+
    \sum_{\tau\in\mathcal T_-\setminus\{\mathbf 1\}}
    \sup_{z,\delta,\varphi} P_{n,\tau}(z,\delta,\varphi)
    +
    \sup_{z,z'}G_n(z,z')
  \right)
  \label{eq:spde-negative-sector-coordinate-domination}
\end{equation}
for a numerical constant \(A_-<\infty\) depending only on this finite basis.
The same inequality holds for the model distance
\(d_{K;\gamma_-}(Z_{n+1},Z_n)\) after replacing \(P_{n,\tau}\) and \(G_n\)
by the corresponding cutoff differences.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The homogeneity of \(X^aY^b\) is
\[
  a\left(-\frac12-\kappa\right)
  +
  b\left(\frac12-3\kappa\right).
\]
For \(a+b\leq3\), direct evaluation gives
\[
\begin{array}{c|c}
  X & -\frac12-\kappa\\
  X^2 & -1-2\kappa\\
  X^3 & -\frac32-3\kappa\\
  Y & \frac12-3\kappa\\
  XY & -4\kappa\\
  X^2Y & -\frac12-5\kappa\\
  Y^2 & 1-6\kappa\\
  XY^2 & \frac12-7\kappa\\
  Y^3 & \frac32-9\kappa .
\end{array}
\]
Since \(0<\kappa<1/14\), the entries in
\eqref{eq:spde-negative-sector-monomial-list} are strictly below
\(\gamma_-\), while \(Y\), \(Y^2\), and \(Y^3\) are above
\(\gamma_-\), and \(XY^2\) is exactly at \(\gamma_-\).  The strict
truncation \(T_{<\gamma_-}\) therefore contains the displayed
non-polynomial monomials and not \(XY^2\).

The symbol \(Y\) has homogeneity \(|Y|=\frac12-3\kappa\), which lies in
\((0,1)\).  Below \(\gamma_-\), the only polynomial symbol with lower
homogeneity than \(Y\) that can appear in its reexpansion is the constant
symbol.  This is the coefficient \(c_n(z,z')\) in
\eqref{eq:spde-y-reexpansion-coefficient}.  The negative symbols
\(\Xi,X,X^2,X^3\) have no lower polynomial component in the sector
\(\mathcal T_-\).  Multiplicativity of the model then gives
\[
  \Gamma_{zz'}^{(n)}(XY)
  =
  \Gamma_{zz'}^{(n)}X\,\Gamma_{zz'}^{(n)}Y
  =
  X(Y+c_n(z,z')\mathbf 1),
\]
and similarly
\[
  \Gamma_{zz'}^{(n)}(X^2Y)
  =
  X^2(Y+c_n(z,z')\mathbf 1).
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:spde-negative-sector-gamma-coordinates}.  The
homogeneity gaps are
\[
  |XY|-|X|=|Y|,\qquad
  |X^2Y|-|X^2|=|Y|.
\]
Thus the normalized \(\Gamma\)-seminorms of these two strict lower
components are both bounded by \(\sup G_n\); all other strict lower
components in this sector vanish.

For \(\Pi\), the seminorm in
Definition~\ref{def:spde-parabolic-modelled-distribution-norms} is the
supremum over unit vectors in a finite-dimensional graded space.  In the
chosen basis, the unit-vector supremum is bounded by a finite multiple of
the sum of the basis-vector suprema.  The constant symbol contributes the
deterministic bound
\[
  |\langle1,\varphi_z^\delta\rangle|
  \leq
  \|\varphi\|_{L^1}
  \leq C_r .
\]
Combining this deterministic constant, the six non-polynomial \(\Pi\)
coordinates, and the single \(c_n\)-coordinate proves
\eqref{eq:spde-negative-sector-coordinate-domination}.  Applying the same
finite-dimensional norm comparison to
\(\Pi^{(n+1)}-\Pi^{(n)}\) and to the coefficient
\(c_{n+1}-c_n\) gives the stated model-distance version.
\end{proof}

\begin{hypothesis}[Negative-sector scale-summed coordinate scheme]
\label{hyp:spde-negative-sector-scale-summed-coordinate-scheme}
Fix \(0<\kappa<1/14\), set
\[
  \gamma_-=\frac12-7\kappa,
\]
and let \(K\subset\R^{1+3}\) be compact.  Choose
\[
  r>\frac52+\kappa .
\]
Let \(Z_n=(\Pi^{(n)},\Gamma^{(n)})\), \(n\geq1\), be random cutoff models on
the finite sector \(\mathcal T_-\) of
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-phi-four-three-negative-sector-coordinate-chart},
with the same basis norms and with reexpansion coefficient \(c_n(z,z')\) as in
\eqref{eq:spde-y-reexpansion-coefficient}.  Put
\[
  N_n^-
  =
  1+\|\Pi^{(n)}\|_{K;\gamma_-}
   +\|\Gamma^{(n)}\|_{K;\gamma_-},
  \qquad
  D_n^-=d_{K;\gamma_-}(Z_{n+1},Z_n).
\]
For
\[
  \mathfrak C_\Pi=\{\Xi,X,X^2,X^3,XY,X^2Y\},
  \qquad
  \mathfrak C=\mathfrak C_\Pi\sqcup\{\mathfrak g\},
\]
define the physical coordinate functions
\[
  Q_{n,\tau}(z,\delta,\varphi)
  =
  \delta^{-|\tau|}
  \left|
    \langle\Pi_z^{(n)}\tau,\varphi_z^\delta\rangle
  \right|,
  \qquad \tau\in\mathfrak C_\Pi,
\]
\[
  \Delta Q_{n,\tau}(z,\delta,\varphi)
  =
  \delta^{-|\tau|}
  \left|
    \langle(\Pi_z^{(n+1)}-\Pi_z^{(n)})\tau,\varphi_z^\delta\rangle
  \right|,
\]
for \(z\in K\), \(0<\delta\leq1\), \(\varphi\in\mathcal B_r\), and
\[
  Q_{n,\mathfrak g}(z,z')
  =
  \frac{|c_n(z,z')|}
       {\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,|Y|}},
  \qquad
  \Delta Q_{n,\mathfrak g}(z,z')
  =
  \frac{|c_{n+1}(z,z')-c_n(z,z')|}
       {\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,|Y|}},
\]
for \(z,z'\in K\) with \(0<\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq1\).  For every
\(i\in\mathfrak C\) and \(m\geq0\), let \((\mathcal X_{i,m},d_{i,m})\) be a
compact metric space with finite nets \(\mathcal X_{i,m,\ell}\), projections
\[
  \pi_{i,m,\ell}:\mathcal X_{i,m}\to\mathcal X_{i,m,\ell},
\]
and edge sets
\[
  \mathcal E_{i,m,\ell}
  =
  \{(\pi_{i,m,\ell}x,\pi_{i,m,\ell+1}x):x\in\mathcal X_{i,m}\}.
\]
Assume that there are constants \(C_{i,0},C_{i,1},D_i,d_i>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
  |\mathcal X_{i,m,0}|\leq C_{i,0}2^{D_i m},
  \qquad
  |\mathcal E_{i,m,\ell}|\leq C_{i,1}2^{D_i m}2^{d_i\ell}
  \label{eq:spde-negative-sector-scale-entropy}
\end{equation}
for all \(m,\ell\geq0\).  Suppose further that there are real random fields
\[
  U_{n,i,m},V_{n,i,m}:\mathcal X_{i,m}\to L^p(\Omega),
  \qquad n\geq1,\quad i\in\mathfrak C,\quad m\geq0,
\]
with almost surely continuous sample paths, such that the coordinate
domination inequalities
\begin{equation}
  \sup Q_{n,i}
  \leq
  \sup_{m\geq0}\sup_{x\in\mathcal X_{i,m}}|U_{n,i,m}(x)|,
  \qquad
  \sup \Delta Q_{n,i}
  \leq
  \sup_{m\geq0}\sup_{x\in\mathcal X_{i,m}}|V_{n,i,m}(x)|
  \label{eq:spde-negative-sector-coordinate-scale-domination}
\end{equation}
hold almost surely.  In \eqref{eq:spde-negative-sector-coordinate-scale-domination},
the first supremum is over the displayed physical variables of \(Q_{n,i}\), and
the second supremum is over the displayed physical variables of
\(\Delta Q_{n,i}\).

Fix \(p\geq1\) and \(\rho>0\).  For each \(i\in\mathfrak C\), assume there are
positive constants \(B_{i,0},B_i,\widetilde B_{i,0},\widetilde B_i,\sigma_i\),
and \(\varepsilon_i\), with
\begin{equation}
  \sigma_i>\frac{D_i}{p},
  \label{eq:spde-negative-sector-scale-slack}
\end{equation}
such that, for every \(n,m,\ell\),
\[
  \mathbb E|U_{n,i,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  B_{i,0}^{\,p}2^{-p\sigma_i m}
  \quad(u\in\mathcal X_{i,m,0}),
\]
\[
  \mathbb E|U_{n,i,m}(v)-U_{n,i,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  B_i^{\,p}2^{-p\sigma_i m}2^{-(d_i+\varepsilon_i)\ell}
  \quad((u,v)\in\mathcal E_{i,m,\ell}),
\]
and
\[
  \mathbb E|V_{n,i,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  \widetilde B_{i,0}^{\,p}2^{-p\rho n}2^{-p\sigma_i m}
  \quad(u\in\mathcal X_{i,m,0}),
\]
\[
  \mathbb E|V_{n,i,m}(v)-V_{n,i,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  \widetilde B_i^{\,p}2^{-p\rho n}2^{-p\sigma_i m}
  2^{-(d_i+\varepsilon_i)\ell}
  \quad((u,v)\in\mathcal E_{i,m,\ell}).
\]
Define
\[
  S_i^{\rm sc}
  =
  \frac{
    C_{i,0}^{1/p}B_{i,0}
    +C_{i,1}^{1/p}B_i(1-2^{-\varepsilon_i/p})^{-1}
  }
  {1-2^{-(\sigma_i-D_i/p)}},
\]
and
\[
  \widetilde S_i^{\rm sc}
  =
  \frac{
    C_{i,0}^{1/p}\widetilde B_{i,0}
    +C_{i,1}^{1/p}\widetilde B_i(1-2^{-\varepsilon_i/p})^{-1}
  }
  {1-2^{-(\sigma_i-D_i/p)}} .
\]
\end{hypothesis}

\paragraph{Negative-sector model convergence from scale-summed coordinates.}
\label{thm:spde-phi-four-three-negative-sector-model-convergence}
Under Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:spde-negative-sector-scale-summed-coordinate-scheme},
\[
  \sup_{n\geq1}\|N_n^-\|_{L^p(\Omega)}
  \leq
  A_-\left(1+\sum_{i\in\mathfrak C}S_i^{\rm sc}\right),
\]
and
\begin{equation}
  \|D_n^-\|_{L^p(\Omega)}
  \leq
  A_-\left(\sum_{i\in\mathfrak C}\widetilde S_i^{\rm sc}\right)2^{-\rho n}.
  \label{eq:spde-negative-sector-model-cauchy-bound}
\end{equation}
Consequently \(Z_n|_{\mathcal T_-}\) converges in \(L^p\) and almost surely,
in the model distance \(d_{K;\gamma_-}\), to a limiting random model on
\(\mathcal T_-\).  More precisely,
\[
  \left(
    \mathbb E\,d_{K;\gamma_-}(Z_n,Z_\infty)^p
  \right)^{1/p}
  \leq
  \frac{
    A_-\sum_{i\in\mathfrak C}\widetilde S_i^{\rm sc}
  }
  {1-2^{-\rho}}\,2^{-\rho n}.
\]

For a fixed coordinate label \(i\), the entropy hypothesis
\eqref{eq:spde-negative-sector-scale-entropy} and the four moment hypotheses
are exactly the hypotheses of
Corollary~\ref{cor:spde-scale-summed-coordinate-upgrade}, first for
\(U_{n,i,m}\) and then for \(V_{n,i,m}\).  Hence
\[
  \left\|
    \sup_{m\geq0}\sup_{x\in\mathcal X_{i,m}}
    |U_{n,i,m}(x)|
  \right\|_{L^p}
  \leq
  S_i^{\rm sc},
\]
uniformly in \(n\), and
\[
  \left\|
    \sup_{m\geq0}\sup_{x\in\mathcal X_{i,m}}
    |V_{n,i,m}(x)|
  \right\|_{L^p}
  \leq
  \widetilde S_i^{\rm sc}2^{-\rho n}.
\]

Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-phi-four-three-negative-sector-coordinate-chart}
gives the finite-dimensional coordinate domination
\[
  N_n^-
  \leq
  A_-\left(1+\sum_{i\in\mathfrak C}\sup Q_{n,i}\right)
\]
and the corresponding distance domination
\[
  D_n^-
  \leq
  A_-\sum_{i\in\mathfrak C}\sup\Delta Q_{n,i}.
\]
Insert \eqref{eq:spde-negative-sector-coordinate-scale-domination} into these
two inequalities and apply the \(L^p\) triangle inequality.  This proves the
two displayed bounds for \(N_n^-\) and \(D_n^-\).

The hypotheses of Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-random-model-cauchy-criterion} are
therefore satisfied with
\[
  C_N=
  A_-^{\,p}\left(1+\sum_{i\in\mathfrak C}S_i^{\rm sc}\right)^p,
  \qquad
  C_D=
  A_-^{\,p}\left(\sum_{i\in\mathfrak C}\widetilde S_i^{\rm sc}\right)^p .
\]
Applying that theorem on the finite sector \(\mathcal T_-\) gives the limiting
model and the stated \(L^p\) tail estimate.

\begin{proposition}[Physical parameter entropy for the strict negative sector]
\label{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy}
Let \(K\subset\R^{1+3}\) be compact, fix \(r>0\), let
\[
  \mathfrak C_\Pi=\{\Xi,X,X^2,X^3,XY,X^2Y\},
\]
let \(|Y|>0\) be the exponent used to normalize the \(c_n\)-coordinate,
let \(\mathfrak s=(2,1,1,1)\), and let
\[
  Q=|\mathfrak s|=5 .
\]
For \(\lambda>0\), write
\[
  \mathsf D_\lambda(t,x_1,x_2,x_3)
  =
  (\lambda^2t,\lambda x_1,\lambda x_2,\lambda x_3).
\]
For \(\tau\in\mathfrak C_\Pi\), set
\[
  Q_{n,\tau}^{\#}(z,\delta)
  =
  \sup_{\varphi\in\mathcal B_r}
  \delta^{-|\tau|}
  \left|
    \langle\Pi_z^{(n)}\tau,\varphi_z^\delta\rangle
  \right|.
\]
Then the supremum over \(z\in K\) and \(0<\delta\leq1\) is the supremum over
the dyadic-scale spaces
\[
  \mathcal X_{\Pi,m}=K\times[1/2,1],
  \qquad
  (z,a)\longmapsto Q_{n,\tau}^{\#}(z,2^{-m}a),
  \qquad m\geq0.
\]
Equip \(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\) with
\[
  d_{\Pi,m}((z,a),(z',a'))
  =
  2^m\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}+|a-a'|.
\]
There are finite nets and projections as in
Corollary~\ref{cor:spde-scale-summed-coordinate-upgrade} for which
\begin{equation}
  |\mathcal X_{\Pi,m,0}|\leq C_{\Pi,0}2^{Qm},
  \qquad
  |\mathcal E_{\Pi,m,\ell}|
  \leq
  C_{\Pi,1}2^{Qm}2^{(Q+1)\ell}.
  \label{eq:spde-pi-physical-parameter-entropy}
\end{equation}

For the \(\Gamma\)-coordinate, let
\[
  A_{\mathfrak s}
  =
  \{h\in\R^{1+3}:1/2\leq\|h\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq1\},
\]
and, for the reexpansion coefficient \(c_n(z,z')\), set
\[
  Q_{n,\mathfrak g}(z,z')
  =
  \frac{|c_n(z,z')|}
       {\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,|Y|}} .
\]
For \(m\geq0\), define
\[
  \mathcal X_{\Gamma,m}
  =
  \{(z,h)\in K\times A_{\mathfrak s}:
      z+\mathsf D_{2^{-m}}h\in K\}.
\]
The map
\[
  (z,h)
  \longmapsto
  Q_{n,\mathfrak g}(z,z+\mathsf D_{2^{-m}}h)
\]
parametrizes the part of the \(\Gamma\)-seminorm with
\[
  2^{-(m+1)}
  \leq
  \|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}
  \leq
  2^{-m}.
\]
Equip \(\mathcal X_{\Gamma,m}\) with
\[
  d_{\Gamma,m}((z,h),(z',h'))
  =
  2^m\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}+\|h-h'\|_{\mathfrak s}.
\]
There are finite nets and projections for which
\begin{equation}
  |\mathcal X_{\Gamma,m,0}|\leq C_{\Gamma,0}2^{Qm},
  \qquad
  |\mathcal E_{\Gamma,m,\ell}|
  \leq
  C_{\Gamma,1}2^{Qm}2^{2Q\ell}.
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-physical-parameter-entropy}
\end{equation}
The constants in
\eqref{eq:spde-pi-physical-parameter-entropy} and
\eqref{eq:spde-gamma-physical-parameter-entropy} depend on \(K\) and on the
chosen parabolic norm, but not on \(m\), \(\ell\), \(n\), or the coordinate
label \(\tau\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
First record the covering estimate used twice.  Since \(K\) is compact, it is
contained in a rectangular box
\[
  [-R,R]\times[-R,R]^3 .
\]
A grid with temporal mesh \(\eta^2\) and spatial mesh \(\eta\) covers this box
by at most \(C_R\eta^{-5}\) parabolic balls of radius \(C\eta\), for
\(0<\eta\leq1\).  After changing the constant, every compact subset of
\(\R^{1+3}\) therefore has parabolic covering number at scale \(\eta\) bounded
by \(C_K\eta^{-Q}\).  The interval \([1/2,1]\) has covering number
\(\leq C\eta^{-1}\) in the ordinary metric, and the annulus
\(A_{\mathfrak s}\) has covering number \(\leq C\eta^{-Q}\) in
\(\|\cdot\|_{\mathfrak s}\).

For \(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\), a ball of radius \(2^{-\ell}\) in
\(d_{\Pi,m}\) requires resolution \(2^{-m-\ell}\) in \(K\) and resolution
\(2^{-\ell}\) in \([1/2,1]\).  Hence
\[
  N(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m},d_{\Pi,m};2^{-\ell})
  \leq
  C\,2^{Qm}2^{(Q+1)\ell}.
\]
Choose a \(2^{-\ell}\)-net \(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m,\ell}\) with this cardinality,
increasing in \(\ell\) after replacing it by the union of the previous nets if
needed.  Let \(\pi_{\Pi,m,\ell}\) be any nearest-net projection.  The base
bound in \eqref{eq:spde-pi-physical-parameter-entropy} is the case \(\ell=0\),
and the edge set
\[
  \mathcal E_{\Pi,m,\ell}
  =
  \{(\pi_{\Pi,m,\ell}x,\pi_{\Pi,m,\ell+1}x):x\in\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\}
\]
has cardinality no larger than \(|\mathcal X_{\Pi,m,\ell+1}|\).  Absorbing the
extra factor \(2^{Q+1}\) into \(C_{\Pi,1}\) gives the displayed edge estimate.

For \(\mathcal X_{\Gamma,m}\), cover \(K\) by \(O(2^{Q(m+\ell)})\) balls of
radius \(2^{-m-\ell}\) and \(A_{\mathfrak s}\) by \(O(2^{Q\ell})\) balls of
radius \(2^{-\ell}\).  The product cover has \(d_{\Gamma,m}\)-radius
\(2^{-\ell}\), so
\[
  N(\mathcal X_{\Gamma,m},d_{\Gamma,m};2^{-\ell})
  \leq
  C\,2^{Qm}2^{2Q\ell}.
\]
The subset condition \(z+\mathsf D_{2^{-m}}h\in K\) only decreases the covering
number.  The same projection and edge-set construction proves
\eqref{eq:spde-gamma-physical-parameter-entropy}.

It remains to check the parametrization.  If \(0<\delta\leq1\), choose
\(m\geq0\) and \(a\in[1/2,1]\) with \(\delta=2^{-m}a\).  This gives the
\(\Pi\)-coordinate decomposition.  If \(0<\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq1\), choose
\(m\geq0\) so that
\[
  2^{-(m+1)}
  \leq
  \|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}
  \leq
  2^{-m}
\]
and set
\[
  h=\mathsf D_{2^m}(z'-z).
\]
The parabolic norm is homogeneous under \(\mathsf D_\lambda\), hence
\(h\in A_{\mathfrak s}\) and \(z'=z+\mathsf D_{2^{-m}}h\).  This proves the
\(\Gamma\)-coordinate decomposition.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Gaussian \(\Pi\)-coordinate input for scale-summed model convergence]
\label{prop:spde-gaussian-negative-pi-coordinate-input}
Let \(K\subset\R^{1+3}\) be compact, let
\[
  Q=5,\qquad 0<\kappa<\frac1{14},
\]
and choose \(r,\theta\) with
\[
  0<\theta<r-\frac Q2 .
\]
Let \(\xi\) be a centered Gaussian space-time white noise and
\[
  X=G*\xi
\]
be the massive heat-convolution field used in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-gaussian-wick-coordinate-scale-estimates}.  For
\[
  \mathfrak C_{\rm G}=\{\Xi,X,X^2,X^3\}
\]
interpret \(X^k\) as the Wick power \(:X^k:\), \(k=1,2,3\), and assign
\[
  |\Xi|=-\frac Q2-\kappa,\qquad
  |X^k|=-\frac k2-k\kappa .
\]
For \(m\geq0\) and \(a\in[1/2,1]\) set
\[
  x=(z,2^{-m}a)
\]
and define the random fields on
\(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}=K\times[1/2,1]\) by
\begin{equation}
  U_{\Xi,m}(z,a)=\|\mathcal W_x\|_{E_r'},
  \qquad
  U_{X^k,m}(z,a)=\|\mathcal X_{k,x}\|_{E_r'},
  \quad k=1,2,3,
  \label{eq:spde-gaussian-pi-coordinate-fields}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal W_x\) and \(\mathcal X_{k,x}\) are the \(E_r'\)-valued
functionals of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-gaussian-wick-dual-norm-coordinate-estimates}.
Equivalently,
\[
  U_{\Xi,m}(z,a)
  =
  \sup_{\varphi\in\mathcal B_r}
  (2^{-m}a)^{Q/2+\kappa}
  |\xi(\varphi_z^{2^{-m}a})|,
\]
and
\[
  U_{X^k,m}(z,a)
  =
  \sup_{\varphi\in\mathcal B_r}
  (2^{-m}a)^{k/2+k\kappa}
  |\langle :X^k:,\varphi_z^{2^{-m}a}\rangle|.
\]
Let \(p=2m_0\) be an even integer satisfying
\begin{equation}
  p\kappa>Q,
  \qquad
  p\theta>Q+1 .
  \label{eq:spde-gaussian-negative-input-moment-condition}
\end{equation}
Then, after choosing the net system of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy}, the
fields \(U_{\tau,m}\), \(\tau\in\mathfrak C_{\rm G}\), have continuous
modifications on each \(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\) and satisfy the
\(\Pi\)-coordinate hypotheses of
the negative-sector coordinate-control consequence with
\[
  D_\tau=Q,\qquad d_\tau=Q+1,
\]
\begin{equation}
  \sigma_\Xi=\kappa,
  \qquad
  \sigma_{X^k}=k\kappa,
  \qquad
  \varepsilon_\tau=p\theta-(Q+1)>0 .
  \label{eq:spde-gaussian-negative-input-slacks}
\end{equation}
More explicitly, there are constants \(B_{\tau,0},B_\tau<\infty\) such that,
for every \(m,\ell\geq0\),
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb E|U_{\tau,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  B_{\tau,0}^{\,p}2^{-p\sigma_\tau m}
  \qquad
  (u\in\mathcal X_{\Pi,m,0})
  \label{eq:spde-gaussian-negative-input-base}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb E|U_{\tau,m}(v)-U_{\tau,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  B_\tau^{\,p}2^{-p\sigma_\tau m}
  2^{-(Q+1+\varepsilon_\tau)\ell}
  \qquad
  ((u,v)\in\mathcal E_{\Pi,m,\ell}).
  \label{eq:spde-gaussian-negative-input-edge}
\end{equation}
Consequently the Gaussian coordinate labels \(\Xi,X,X^2,X^3\) already feed
into the scale-summed negative-sector model theorem without an additional
stochastic supremum argument.

If a cutoff or mollifier sequence
\((\xi_n,X_n,:X_n^2:,:X_n^3:)\) satisfies the same dual-norm bounds for the
increments of the corresponding fields \(U_{\tau,m}^{(n+1)}-U_{\tau,m}^{(n)}\),
with an additional factor \(2^{-\rho n}\) in \(L^p\) for some \(\rho>0\),
then the associated cutoff-difference variables satisfy the \(V\)-hypotheses
of
the negative-sector coordinate-control consequence with
the same \(D_\tau,d_\tau,\sigma_\tau,\varepsilon_\tau\) and with that
convergence rate \(\rho\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
We first identify the scale-normalized physical coordinates with the
dual-norm fields.  For \(\tau=\Xi\),
\[
  \delta^{-|\Xi|}
  |\langle\Pi_z\Xi,\varphi_z^\delta\rangle|
  =
  \delta^{Q/2+\kappa}|\xi(\varphi_z^\delta)|,
\]
and this is \(|\mathcal W_{(z,\delta)}(\varphi)|\).  For
\(\tau=X^k\),
\[
  \delta^{-|X^k|}
  |\langle\Pi_z X^k,\varphi_z^\delta\rangle|
  =
  \delta^{k/2+k\kappa}
  |\langle :X^k:,\varphi_z^\delta\rangle|,
\]
which is \(|\mathcal X_{k,(z,\delta)}(\varphi)|\).  Taking the supremum over
\(\mathcal B_r\), which is the unit ball of the same test space \(E_r\) with
the support convention used in the dual-norm proposition, gives
\eqref{eq:spde-gaussian-pi-coordinate-fields}.  This is the promised map from
physical \(\Pi\)-coordinates to the abstract coordinate fields of
the negative-sector coordinate-control consequence.

Set \(\delta=2^{-m}a\) with \(a\in[1/2,1]\).  The factor \(a\) is bounded
above and below by numerical constants, hence
\[
  \delta^{\sigma_\tau}\asymp 2^{-\sigma_\tau m}
\]
for \(\sigma_\Xi=\kappa\) and \(\sigma_{X^k}=k\kappa\).  Applying
\eqref{eq:spde-gaussian-dual-norm-uniform} and raising the \(L^p\)-bound to a
\(p\)-th moment proves
\eqref{eq:spde-gaussian-negative-input-base}.

Let \((u,v)\in\mathcal E_{\Pi,m,\ell}\), say
\[
  u=(z,a),\qquad v=(z',a').
\]
The nearest-net construction in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy} gives
\begin{equation}
  2^m\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}+|a-a'|
  \leq
  C_{\Pi}2^{-\ell}.
  \label{eq:spde-gaussian-negative-input-edge-distance}
\end{equation}
With \(x=(z,2^{-m}a)\) and \(y=(z',2^{-m}a')\), the parameter
\(\eta\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-gaussian-wick-dual-norm-coordinate-estimates}
satisfies
\[
  \eta\leq C2^{-\ell}.
\]
The edge estimates
\eqref{eq:spde-gaussian-dual-norm-white-edge} and
\eqref{eq:spde-gaussian-dual-norm-wick-edge}, together with
\[
  \bigl|\|A\|_{E_r'}-\|B\|_{E_r'}\bigr|
  \leq
  \|A-B\|_{E_r'},
\]
therefore give
\[
  \|U_{\tau,m}(v)-U_{\tau,m}(u)\|_{L^p}
  \leq
  C_\tau 2^{-\sigma_\tau m}2^{-\theta\ell}.
\]
Raising to the \(p\)-th power yields
\[
  \mathbb E|U_{\tau,m}(v)-U_{\tau,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  C_\tau^p2^{-p\sigma_\tau m}2^{-p\theta\ell}.
\]
Since \(\varepsilon_\tau=p\theta-(Q+1)\), this is exactly
\eqref{eq:spde-gaussian-negative-input-edge}.

The entropy dimensions are
\[
  D_\tau=Q,\qquad d_\tau=Q+1
\]
by Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy}.
The moment condition \eqref{eq:spde-gaussian-negative-input-moment-condition}
implies
\[
  \sigma_\Xi=\kappa>\frac Qp,
  \qquad
  \sigma_{X^k}=k\kappa\geq\kappa>\frac Qp,
\]
and it also implies \(\varepsilon_\tau>0\).  These are precisely the
scale-slack and edge-slack inequalities required in
the negative-sector coordinate-control consequence.

It remains only to justify the continuity hypothesis.  The same edge estimate,
before restriction to the dyadic edge set, holds for arbitrary
\((z,a),(z',a')\in\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\) with
\[
  d_{\Pi,m}((z,a),(z',a'))\leq1,
\]
with \(2^{-\ell}\) replaced by that metric distance.  Since
\(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\) has metric covering dimension \(Q+1\) uniformly in
\(m\), the Kolmogorov--Chentsov dyadic-net proof gives, for every
\[
  0<\alpha<\theta-\frac{Q+1}{p},
\]
a modification that is \(\alpha\)-Holder continuous on
\(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\).  This proves the required sample-path continuity.

For a cutoff sequence, apply the preceding Kolmogorov-net construction to
\[
  U_{\tau,m}^{(n+1)}-U_{\tau,m}^{(n)}
\]
in place of \(U_{\tau,m}\).  The assumed extra factor \(2^{-\rho n}\) is
carried unchanged through the base estimate, the edge estimate, and the
dyadic-net continuity argument, and hence gives the \(V\)-hypotheses of the
scale-summed theorem.
\end{proof}

For the nonlinear \(\Pi\)-coordinates \(XY\) and \(X^2Y\), and for the
\(\Gamma\)-coordinate \(c_n(z,z')\), the same assembly theorem applies but
the analytic inputs are different.  The \(XY\) and \(X^2Y\) coordinates require
the concrete BPHZ kernel estimates for products involving
\(Y=\mathcal I(X^3)\).  The \(\Gamma\)-coordinate has no test-function dual
norm; it is a scalar finite-chaos estimate on
\(\mathcal X_{\Gamma,m}\), with entropy exponent \(d_{\mathfrak g}=10\) by
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy}.  Thus
the stochastic and entropy mechanism is now completely explicit, while the
remaining \(\Phi^4_3\) work is the model-specific BPHZ kernel analysis for
\(XY\), \(X^2Y\), and the reexpansion coefficient of \(Y\).

\begin{proposition}[Heat-integration reexpansion estimate]
\label{prop:spde-heat-integration-reexpansion-coefficient-estimate}
Let \(\mathfrak s=(2,1,1,1)\) and \(Q=5\).  Let
\[
  -2<\alpha<0,\qquad
  0<\sigma,\qquad
  \beta=\alpha+2,\qquad
  \gamma=\beta+\sigma ,
\]
and assume
\[
  0<\beta<1,\qquad 0<\gamma<1 .
\]
Fix \(r>-\alpha-\sigma\).  Let \(K=\sum_{j\geq0}K_j\) be a dyadic
decomposition of a parabolic heat kernel, with the following properties.
There are constants \(A,C_K\) and a number \(\vartheta\in(\gamma,1]\) such
that, after enlarging \(A\) if necessary, \(A\geq1\) and
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{supp}K_j\subset B_{\mathfrak s}(0,A2^{-j}),
  \qquad
  |K_j(u)|\leq C_K2^{(Q-2)j},
  \qquad j\geq0,
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-kernel-size}
\end{equation}
and, for every \(a,b\) with
\(\|a-b\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq A2^{-j}\), the translated kernel difference
admits the test-function representation
\begin{equation}
  K_j(a-\cdot)-K_j(b-\cdot)
  =
  C_K2^{-2j}
  (2^j\|a-b\|_{\mathfrak s})^\vartheta
  \psi_{a,b,j}^{\,2^{-j}},
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-kernel-difference-test}
\end{equation}
where \(\psi_{a,b,j}\in C_c^r\) is supported in a fixed
\(\mathfrak s\)-ball and \(\|\psi_{a,b,j}\|_{C^r}\leq1\).  The translated
kernel itself has the analogous representation
\begin{equation}
  K_j(a-\cdot)=C_K2^{-2j}\psi_{a,j}^{\,2^{-j}},
  \qquad
  \|\psi_{a,j}\|_{C^r}\leq1 .
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-kernel-test}
\end{equation}

Let \(T\) be a distribution on a fixed compact neighborhood \(U\) such that
\begin{equation}
  \|T\|_{\alpha+\sigma;U,r}
  :=
  \sup_{\substack{x\in U,\ 0<\lambda\leq1\\ \varphi\in\mathcal B_r}}
  \lambda^{-(\alpha+\sigma)}
  |\langle T,\varphi_x^\lambda\rangle|
  <\infty .
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-negative-distribution-norm}
\end{equation}
For \(a\in U\) whose unit parabolic neighborhood lies in \(U\), define
\begin{equation}
  (\mathcal KT)(a)
  =
  \sum_{j\geq0}\langle T,K_j(a-\cdot)\rangle .
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-integrated-distribution}
\end{equation}
Then the increment series is absolutely convergent and is given by
\begin{equation}
  \mathfrak c_T(a,b)
  =
  (\mathcal KT)(b)-(\mathcal KT)(a)
  =
  \sum_{j\geq0}
  \langle T,K_j(b-\cdot)-K_j(a-\cdot)\rangle .
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-coefficient-definition}
\end{equation}
Moreover, whenever \(0<\|a-b\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq1\),
\begin{equation}
  |\mathfrak c_T(a,b)|
  \leq
  C\|T\|_{\alpha+\sigma;U,r}
  \|a-b\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,\beta+\sigma}.
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-coefficient-holder}
\end{equation}
Consequently the coefficient normalized with the model homogeneity \(\beta\)
has scale slack \(\sigma\):
\begin{equation}
  \frac{|\mathfrak c_T(a,b)|}
       {\|a-b\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,\beta}}
  \leq
  C\|T\|_{\alpha+\sigma;U,r}
  \|a-b\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,\sigma}.
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-normalized-scale-slack}
\end{equation}

If \((a,b)\) and \((a',b')\) satisfy
\[
  h=\|a-b\|_{\mathfrak s},\qquad
  h'=\|a'-b'\|_{\mathfrak s},\qquad
  h,h'\in[2^{-m-1},2^{-m}],
\]
and
\[
  \eta=
  2^m\bigl(\|a-a'\|_{\mathfrak s}+\|b-b'\|_{\mathfrak s}\bigr)
  \leq1,
\]
then, for every \(0<\theta\leq\gamma\),
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  &\left|
    \frac{\mathfrak c_T(a,b)}{\|a-b\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,\beta}}
    -
    \frac{\mathfrak c_T(a',b')}{\|a'-b'\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,\beta}}
  \right|                                                   \\
  &\qquad\leq
  C_\theta
  \|T\|_{\alpha+\sigma;U,r}
  2^{-\sigma m}\eta^\theta .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-normalized-edge-bound}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
First prove the Schauder increment estimate for
\(\mathcal KT\).  Set
\[
  M=\|T\|_{\alpha+\sigma;U,r}.
\]
The representation \eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-kernel-test} and the
definition of \(M\) give
\begin{equation}
  |\langle T,K_j(a-\cdot)\rangle|
  \leq
  C_K2^{-2j}M(2^{-j})^{\alpha+\sigma}
  =
  C_KM2^{-\gamma j}.
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-single-kernel-bound}
\end{equation}
This bound is summable for \(j\to\infty\), since \(\gamma>0\).  The possible
large-scale additive ambiguity is the usual harmless constant in the
parabolic Schauder estimate; it cancels in increments.  Hence
\(\mathfrak c_T(a,b)\) is given by the absolutely convergent difference
series in
\eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-coefficient-definition}.

Let
\[
  h=\|a-b\|_{\mathfrak s}
\]
and choose \(J\geq0\) so that
\[
  2^{-J-1}<h\leq2^{-J}.
\]
For the fine scales \(j>J\), use
\eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-single-kernel-bound} separately at \(a\) and
\(b\):
\begin{equation}
  \sum_{j>J}
  |\langle T,K_j(b-\cdot)-K_j(a-\cdot)\rangle|
  \leq
  CM\sum_{j>J}2^{-\gamma j}
  \leq
  CMh^\gamma .
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-fine-scale-bound}
\end{equation}
For the coarse scales \(j\leq J\), the kernel-difference representation
\eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-kernel-difference-test} gives
\[
\begin{aligned}
  |\langle T,K_j(b-\cdot)-K_j(a-\cdot)\rangle|
  &\leq
  C_K2^{-2j}(2^jh)^\vartheta M(2^{-j})^{\alpha+\sigma}     \\
  &=
  CMh^\vartheta 2^{(\vartheta-\gamma)j}.
\end{aligned}
\]
Since \(\vartheta>\gamma\),
\begin{equation}
  \sum_{j\leq J}
  h^\vartheta 2^{(\vartheta-\gamma)j}
  \leq
  Ch^\vartheta 2^{(\vartheta-\gamma)J}
  \leq
  Ch^\gamma .
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-coarse-scale-bound}
\end{equation}
Combining \eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-fine-scale-bound} and
\eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-coarse-scale-bound} proves
\eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-coefficient-holder}; dividing by \(h^\beta\)
proves \eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-normalized-scale-slack}.

For the normalized edge estimate, write
\[
  F(a)=(\mathcal KT)(a).
\]
The estimate just proved says
\begin{equation}
  |F(x)-F(y)|\leq CM\|x-y\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\gamma}
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-F-holder}
\end{equation}
on the compact region under consideration.  The assumptions on
\((a,b)\) and \((a',b')\) imply \(h'\simeq h\simeq2^{-m}\) and
\begin{equation}
  \|a-a'\|_{\mathfrak s}+\|b-b'\|_{\mathfrak s}
  \leq
  C\eta h .
  \label{eq:spde-reexpansion-edge-geometry}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\[
\begin{aligned}
  |(F(b)-F(a))-(F(b')-F(a'))|
  &\leq
  CM\bigl(\|b-b'\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\gamma}
          +\|a-a'\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\gamma}\bigr)       \\
  &\leq
  CMh^\gamma\eta^\gamma .
\end{aligned}
\]
Dividing by \(h^\beta\) gives \(CMh^\sigma\eta^\gamma\).  The remaining
effect is the change of denominator:
\[
  |h^{-\beta}-{h'}^{-\beta}|
  \leq
  C_\beta h^{-\beta}\frac{|h-h'|}{h}
  \leq
  C_\beta h^{-\beta}\eta ,
\]
while \(|F(b')-F(a')|\leq CMh^\gamma\).  This contribution is bounded by
\(CMh^\sigma\eta\).  Since \(0<\eta\leq1\), \(h\simeq2^{-m}\), and
\(\theta\leq\gamma<1\), the sum of the two contributions is bounded by the
right-hand side of
\eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-normalized-edge-bound}.
\end{proof}

Apply
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-heat-integration-reexpansion-coefficient-estimate}
to the symbol \(Y=\mathcal I(X^3)\) in dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\).  Here
\[
  \alpha=|X^3|=-\frac32-3\kappa,\qquad
  \beta=|Y|=\alpha+2=\frac12-3\kappa .
\]
The primitive Gaussian estimate for \(X^3\) proved above gives the additional
regularity slack
\[
  \sigma=3\kappa,
  \qquad
  \alpha+\sigma=-\frac32,
  \qquad
  \beta+\sigma=\frac12 .
\]
Thus the constant reexpansion coefficient
\begin{equation}
  c_n(z,z')
  =
  \bigl(\mathcal K\Pi_z^{(n)}X^3\bigr)(z')
  -
  \bigl(\mathcal K\Pi_z^{(n)}X^3\bigr)(z)
  \label{eq:spde-cn-from-x3-coordinate}
\end{equation}
has the deterministic normalization
\begin{equation}
  \frac{|c_n(z,z')|}
       {\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,|Y|}}
  \leq
  C\,\|\Pi_z^{(n)}X^3\|_{-3/2;U,r}
  \|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,3\kappa}.
  \label{eq:spde-cn-scale-slack-from-x3}
\end{equation}

\begin{proposition}[\(\Gamma\)-coordinate input from heat integration of \(X^3\)]
\label{prop:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-from-x3-heat-integration}
Let \(K\subset\R^{1+3}\) be compact and let \(U\) be a compact neighborhood
containing the unit parabolic neighborhoods of the points of \(K\).  Fix
\[
  0<\kappa<\frac1{14},
  \qquad
  \beta=\frac12-3\kappa,
  \qquad
  \sigma_{\mathfrak g}=3\kappa .
\]
Let \(T_n\), \(n\geq1\), be random distributions on \(U\).  Assume that the
heat-kernel decomposition satisfies the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-heat-integration-reexpansion-coefficient-estimate}
with
\[
  \alpha=-\frac32-3\kappa,
  \qquad
  \sigma=3\kappa,
  \qquad
  \gamma=\beta+\sigma=\frac12 .
\]
For \(z,z'\in K\), define
\[
  c_n(z,z')=(\mathcal KT_n)(z')-(\mathcal KT_n)(z).
\]
Choose \(0<\theta\leq1/2\) and an even integer \(p\) such that
\begin{equation}
  3p\kappa>5,
  \qquad
  p\theta>10 .
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-moment-condition}
\end{equation}
Suppose that, for some constants \(B_{\mathfrak g}\),
\(\widetilde B_{\mathfrak g}\), and \(\rho>0\),
\begin{equation}
  \sup_{n\geq1}
  \bigl\|\|T_n\|_{-3/2;U,r}\bigr\|_{L^p(\Omega)}
  \leq
  B_{\mathfrak g},
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-x3-uniform}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
  \bigl\|\|T_{n+1}-T_n\|_{-3/2;U,r}\bigr\|_{L^p(\Omega)}
  \leq
  \widetilde B_{\mathfrak g}2^{-\rho n}.
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-x3-cauchy}
\end{equation}
Here \(\|\cdot\|_{-3/2;U,r}\) is the norm
\eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-negative-distribution-norm} with exponent
\(-3/2\).

For \(m\geq0\), let \(\mathcal X_{\Gamma,m}\) be the physical
\(\Gamma\)-coordinate parameter space of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy}.  For
\((z,h)\in\mathcal X_{\Gamma,m}\), set
\[
  z_h=z+\mathsf D_{2^{-m}}h,
  \qquad
  U_{n,\mathfrak g,m}(z,h)
  =
  \frac{|c_n(z,z_h)|}
       {\|z-z_h\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,\beta}},
\]
and
\begin{equation}
  V_{n,\mathfrak g,m}(z,h)
  =
  \frac{|(c_{n+1}-c_n)(z,z_h)|}
       {\|z-z_h\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,\beta}} .
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-fields}
\end{equation}
Then the \(\mathfrak g\)-coordinate hypotheses of
the negative-sector coordinate-control consequence hold
with
\begin{equation}
  D_{\mathfrak g}=5,
  \qquad
  d_{\mathfrak g}=10,
  \qquad
  \sigma_{\mathfrak g}=3\kappa,
  \qquad
  \varepsilon_{\mathfrak g}=p\theta-10>0 .
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-slacks}
\end{equation}
More explicitly, after choosing the nets of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy}, there
are constants \(C_0,C_1\), independent of \(n,m,\ell\), such that
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb E|U_{n,\mathfrak g,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  C_0^pB_{\mathfrak g}^{\,p}2^{-3p\kappa m}
  \qquad
  (u\in\mathcal X_{\Gamma,m,0}),
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-base}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb E|U_{n,\mathfrak g,m}(v)-U_{n,\mathfrak g,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  C_1^pB_{\mathfrak g}^{\,p}2^{-3p\kappa m}
  2^{-(10+\varepsilon_{\mathfrak g})\ell}
  \qquad
  ((u,v)\in\mathcal E_{\Gamma,m,\ell}),
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-edge}
\end{equation}
and the same two estimates hold for \(V_{n,\mathfrak g,m}\) with
\(B_{\mathfrak g}^{\,p}\) replaced by
\(\widetilde B_{\mathfrak g}^{\,p}2^{-p\rho n}\).

For the primitive dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\) reexpansion coefficient, one takes
\[
  T_n=\Pi_z^{(n)}X^3 ,
\]
which is independent of the base point \(z\) for this primitive Wick-cubic
symbol.  When \(T_n\) is the cutoff Wick cubic \(:X_n^3:\), the uniform bound
\eqref{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-x3-uniform} is the scale-summed
\(X^3\) consequence of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-gaussian-negative-pi-coordinate-input} applied on
the enlarged compact region \(U\).  The cutoff-Cauchy input
\eqref{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-x3-cauchy} is the corresponding
cutoff-increment estimate for the Wick cubic.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let \((z,h)\in\mathcal X_{\Gamma,m}\) and put
\[
  z_h=z+\mathsf D_{2^{-m}}h,
  \qquad
  h_m=\|z-z_h\|_{\mathfrak s}.
\]
Since \(h\in A_{\mathfrak s}\), one has
\begin{equation}
  2^{-m-1}\leq h_m\leq 2^{-m}.
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-annular-scale}
\end{equation}
Apply
\eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-normalized-scale-slack} with
\(T=T_n\), \(\beta=1/2-3\kappa\), and \(\sigma=3\kappa\).  This gives
\begin{equation}
  U_{n,\mathfrak g,m}(z,h)
  \leq
  C\|T_n\|_{-3/2;U,r}h_m^{3\kappa}
  \leq
  C\|T_n\|_{-3/2;U,r}2^{-3\kappa m}.
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-pointwise-base}
\end{equation}
Taking \(L^p\)-norms and using
\eqref{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-x3-uniform} proves
\eqref{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-base}.

Let \(u=(z,h)\) and \(v=(z',h')\) be an edge in
\(\mathcal E_{\Gamma,m,\ell}\).  The net construction gives
\begin{equation}
  2^m\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}+\|h-h'\|_{\mathfrak s}
  \leq
  C2^{-\ell}.
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-edge-distance}
\end{equation}
Set
\[
  a=z,\quad b=z+\mathsf D_{2^{-m}}h,\qquad
  a'=z',\quad b'=z'+\mathsf D_{2^{-m}}h' .
\]
Then \(a,b,a',b'\in U\), their separations are in
\([2^{-m-1},2^{-m}]\), and the edge parameter
\[
  \eta=
  2^m(\|a-a'\|_{\mathfrak s}+\|b-b'\|_{\mathfrak s})
\]
is bounded by \(C2^{-\ell}\).  The normalized edge estimate
\eqref{eq:spde-reexpansion-normalized-edge-bound} therefore gives
\[
  \left|
    \frac{c_n(a,b)}{\|a-b\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,\beta}}
    -
    \frac{c_n(a',b')}{\|a'-b'\|_{\mathfrak s}^{\,\beta}}
  \right|
  \leq
  C_\theta\|T_n\|_{-3/2;U,r}2^{-3\kappa m}2^{-\theta\ell}.
\]
Since \(\bigl||A|-|B|\bigr|\leq |A-B|\), this implies
\begin{equation}
  |U_{n,\mathfrak g,m}(v)-U_{n,\mathfrak g,m}(u)|
  \leq
  C_\theta\|T_n\|_{-3/2;U,r}2^{-3\kappa m}2^{-\theta\ell}.
  \label{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-pointwise-edge}
\end{equation}
After taking the \(p\)-th moment, this is exactly
\eqref{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-edge}, because
\[
  10+\varepsilon_{\mathfrak g}=p\theta .
\]

The same deterministic inequalities apply to \(T_{n+1}-T_n\), and
\eqref{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-x3-cauchy} supplies the additional
factor \(2^{-\rho n}\) in \(L^p\).  The entropy exponents
\[
  D_{\mathfrak g}=5,\qquad d_{\mathfrak g}=10
\]
are those of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy}.  The
conditions \eqref{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-moment-condition} say
precisely that
\[
  \sigma_{\mathfrak g}=3\kappa>\frac{D_{\mathfrak g}}p,
  \qquad
  \varepsilon_{\mathfrak g}=p\theta-d_{\mathfrak g}>0 .
\]
Thus the scale-slack and edge-slack hypotheses in
the negative-sector coordinate-control consequence hold.
The deterministic Holder estimate
\eqref{eq:spde-gamma-coordinate-input-pointwise-edge} also gives continuous
sample paths whenever the norm \(\|T_n\|_{-3/2;U,r}\) is finite, which proves
the required continuity on each compact coordinate space.
\end{proof}

Hence the \(c_n\)-coordinate does not require an independent singular
stochastic contraction: its model-convergence input is a heat-integration
consequence of the \(X^3\) coordinate estimates.  What remains genuinely new
in the strict negative sector is the BPHZ analysis of the nonlinear products
\(XY\) and \(X^2Y\), where multiplication with the integrated field
introduces additional contraction sectors.

\subsection{Nonlinear Negative Coordinates and Local Shell Bounds}
\label{subsec:spde-nonlinear-negative-coordinates-shell-bounds}

\paragraph{Finite-cutoff Wick decomposition for nonlinear negative coordinates.}
Let \(X_\epsilon\) be a smooth centered Gaussian field on spacetime, with
covariance
\[
  G_\epsilon(a,b)
  =
  \mathbb E[X_\epsilon(a)X_\epsilon(b)] ,
\]
and let \(K_\epsilon(a,b)\) be a smooth retarded heat kernel with the same
ultraviolet cutoff.  Define
\[
  Y_\epsilon(a)
  =
  \int K_\epsilon(a,b):X_\epsilon(b)^3:\,\dd b .
\]
The Wick product is always taken with respect to the joint Gaussian family
\(\{X_\epsilon(c)\}_c\).  Then
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  X_\epsilon(a)Y_\epsilon(a)
  &=
  \int K_\epsilon(a,b)
  :X_\epsilon(a)X_\epsilon(b)^3:\,\dd b                  \\
  &\quad
  +3\int K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)
  :X_\epsilon(b)^2:\,\dd b .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-xy-finite-cutoff-wick-decomposition}
\end{equation}
Furthermore, if
\begin{equation}
  C_{2,\epsilon}(a)
  =
  2\int K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)^2\,\dd b ,
  \label{eq:spde-c2-local-coordinate-for-x2y}
\end{equation}
then the two-loop locally subtracted coordinate is
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  &:\!X_\epsilon(a)^2\!:Y_\epsilon(a)-3C_{2,\epsilon}(a)X_\epsilon(a) \\
  &=
  \int K_\epsilon(a,b)
  :X_\epsilon(a)^2X_\epsilon(b)^3:\,\dd b                         \\
  &\quad
  +6\int K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)
  :X_\epsilon(a)X_\epsilon(b)^2:\,\dd b                            \\
  &\quad
  +6\int K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)^2
  \bigl(X_\epsilon(b)-X_\epsilon(a)\bigr)\,\dd b .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-x2y-finite-cutoff-wick-decomposition}
\end{equation}
Thus \(XY\) has only fourth- and second-chaos pieces, while the BPHZ
coordinate \(X^2Y\) has fifth-, third-, and locally subtracted first-chaos
pieces.  The last line of
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-finite-cutoff-wick-decomposition} is the exact place
where the local Taylor-subtraction gain of
\eqref{eq:spde-taylor-subtraction-gain} enters the multiscale estimate.

The verification is the two-variable Wick product identity.
For two centered Gaussian variables \(A,B\), with
\(C=\mathbb E[AB]\), the Wick product identity is
\begin{equation}
  :\!A^m\!:\,:\!B^n\!:
  =
  \sum_{r=0}^{\min(m,n)}
  \binom{m}{r}\binom{n}{r}r!\,C^r
  :\!A^{m-r}B^{n-r}\!: .
  \label{eq:spde-two-point-wick-product-identity}
\end{equation}
This identity follows by comparing coefficients of \(s^mt^n/(m!n!)\) in
\[
  \exp\!\left(sA-\frac{s^2}{2}\mathbb E[A^2]\right)
  \exp\!\left(tB-\frac{t^2}{2}\mathbb E[B^2]\right)
  =
  e^{stC}
  \exp\!\left(sA+tB-\frac12\mathbb E[(sA+tB)^2]\right).
\]
Apply \eqref{eq:spde-two-point-wick-product-identity} first with
\((m,n)=(1,3)\), \(A=X_\epsilon(a)\), \(B=X_\epsilon(b)\).  The terms
\(r=0,1\) have coefficients \(1\) and \(3\), and integration against
\(K_\epsilon(a,b)\) gives
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-finite-cutoff-wick-decomposition}.

Next apply the same identity with \((m,n)=(2,3)\).  The coefficients are
\[
  \binom{2}{0}\binom{3}{0}0!=1,\qquad
  \binom{2}{1}\binom{3}{1}1!=6,\qquad
  \binom{2}{2}\binom{3}{2}2!=6 .
\]
Therefore
\[
\begin{aligned}
  :\!X_\epsilon(a)^2\!:Y_\epsilon(a)
  &=
  \int K_\epsilon(a,b)
  :X_\epsilon(a)^2X_\epsilon(b)^3:\,\dd b                         \\
  &\quad
  +6\int K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)
  :X_\epsilon(a)X_\epsilon(b)^2:\,\dd b                            \\
  &\quad
  +6\int K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)^2
  X_\epsilon(b)\,\dd b .
\end{aligned}
\]
By \eqref{eq:spde-c2-local-coordinate-for-x2y},
\[
  3C_{2,\epsilon}(a)X_\epsilon(a)
  =
  6\int K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)^2
  X_\epsilon(a)\,\dd b .
\]
Subtracting this local part from the preceding identity proves
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-finite-cutoff-wick-decomposition}.

The formal homogeneity bookkeeping is now tied to concrete finite-cutoff
coordinates.  The analytic estimates still to be proved for
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-finite-cutoff-wick-decomposition} and
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-finite-cutoff-wick-decomposition} are not generic
Holder-product estimates: the sums of the classical regularities are
borderline or negative.  They are finite-chaos kernel estimates after
Wick expansion and BPHZ local subtraction.  The target regularity slacks are
\[
  0-|XY|=4\kappa,\qquad
  \left(-\frac12\right)-|X^2Y|=5\kappa .
\]
Once the fifth-, fourth-, third-, second-, and locally subtracted first-chaos
kernels in the two displayed decompositions are bounded with these slacks,
the dual-norm finite-chaos estimate, physical-parameter entropy theorem, and
negative-sector model convergence theorem above apply without further
stochastic input.

\paragraph{Finite-chaos kernels for tested nonlinear coordinates.}
Let \(\mathcal H\) be a real Hilbert space and let
\(\xi:\mathcal H\to L^2(\Omega)\) be an isonormal Gaussian process.  Let
\[
  p_\epsilon(a)\in\mathcal H
\]
be a smooth cutoff noise-to-field kernel and set
\[
  X_\epsilon(a)=I_1(p_\epsilon(a)),\qquad
  G_\epsilon(a,b)=\langle p_\epsilon(a),p_\epsilon(b)\rangle_{\mathcal H}.
\]
Let \(K_\epsilon(a,b)\) be the cutoff retarded heat kernel and let
\(\chi\) be a smooth compactly supported test density in the \(a\)-variable.
Define
\[
  Y_\epsilon(a)
  =
  \int K_\epsilon(a,b):X_\epsilon(b)^3:\,\dd b .
\]
Write \(\operatorname{Sym}_q\) for orthogonal symmetrization in
\(\mathcal H^{\otimes q}\).  Assume that the Hilbert-valued integrands
displayed below are Bochner integrable; for the smooth compactly supported
cutoffs used here this follows from the \(L^1\)-integrability of
\(|K_\epsilon(a,b)|\), \(|K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)|\), and
\(|K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)^2|\) against the relevant products of
\(\|p_\epsilon(a)\|_{\mathcal H}\), \(\|p_\epsilon(b)\|_{\mathcal H}\), and
\(\|p_\epsilon(b)-p_\epsilon(a)\|_{\mathcal H}\).  Define
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  F_{XY,4}^{\chi}
  &=
  \operatorname{Sym}_4
  \int\chi(a)K_\epsilon(a,b)\,
  p_\epsilon(a)\otimes p_\epsilon(b)^{\otimes3}\,\dd a\,\dd b,\\
  F_{XY,2}^{\chi}
  &=
  3\,\operatorname{Sym}_2
  \int\chi(a)K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)\,
  p_\epsilon(b)^{\otimes2}\,\dd a\,\dd b .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-xy-tested-chaos-kernels}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
  \int\chi(a)X_\epsilon(a)Y_\epsilon(a)\,\dd a
  =
  I_4(F_{XY,4}^{\chi})+I_2(F_{XY,2}^{\chi}).
  \label{eq:spde-xy-tested-chaos-expansion}
\end{equation}

For the locally subtracted \(X^2Y\) coordinate, set
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  F_{X^2Y,5}^{\chi}
  &=
  \operatorname{Sym}_5
  \int\chi(a)K_\epsilon(a,b)\,
  p_\epsilon(a)^{\otimes2}\otimes p_\epsilon(b)^{\otimes3}
  \,\dd a\,\dd b,\\
  F_{X^2Y,3}^{\chi}
  &=
  6\,\operatorname{Sym}_3
  \int\chi(a)K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)\,
  p_\epsilon(a)\otimes p_\epsilon(b)^{\otimes2}\,\dd a\,\dd b,\\
  F_{X^2Y,1}^{\chi}
  &=
  6\int\chi(a)K_\epsilon(a,b)G_\epsilon(a,b)^2
  \bigl(p_\epsilon(b)-p_\epsilon(a)\bigr)\,\dd a\,\dd b .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-x2y-tested-chaos-kernels}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  &\int\chi(a)
  \bigl(:\!X_\epsilon(a)^2\!:Y_\epsilon(a)
        -3C_{2,\epsilon}(a)X_\epsilon(a)\bigr)\,\dd a\\
  &\qquad =
  I_5(F_{X^2Y,5}^{\chi})
  +I_3(F_{X^2Y,3}^{\chi})
  +I_1(F_{X^2Y,1}^{\chi}) .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-x2y-tested-chaos-expansion}
\end{equation}

The identities are finite-chaos bookkeeping.
The identity
\[
  :X_\epsilon(a)X_\epsilon(b)^3:
  =
  I_4\!\left(
    \operatorname{Sym}_4
    \bigl(p_\epsilon(a)\otimes p_\epsilon(b)^{\otimes3}\bigr)
  \right)
\]
is the definition of the fourth Wick chaos associated to the vector family
\(p_\epsilon(\cdot)\).  Likewise
\[
  :X_\epsilon(b)^2:
  =
  I_2(p_\epsilon(b)^{\otimes2}).
\]
Multiplying the pointwise identity
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-finite-cutoff-wick-decomposition} by \(\chi(a)\),
integrating in \(a\), and using the linearity and continuity of finite
multiple Wiener integrals gives
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-chaos-expansion} with the kernels in
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-chaos-kernels}.  The stated Bochner integrability
assumption permits approximation of the Hilbert-valued integrals by simple
functions.  Passing to the Hilbert-space limit and using
\(\mathbb E[I_q(f)I_q(g)]=q!\langle f,g\rangle_{\mathcal H^{\otimes q}}\)
justifies the interchange with \(I_q\).

For \(X^2Y\), the three Wick monomials in
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-finite-cutoff-wick-decomposition} are
\[
  :X_\epsilon(a)^2X_\epsilon(b)^3:
  =
  I_5\!\left(
    \operatorname{Sym}_5
    (p_\epsilon(a)^{\otimes2}\otimes p_\epsilon(b)^{\otimes3})
  \right),
\]
\[
  :X_\epsilon(a)X_\epsilon(b)^2:
  =
  I_3\!\left(
    \operatorname{Sym}_3
    (p_\epsilon(a)\otimes p_\epsilon(b)^{\otimes2})
  \right),
\]
and
\[
  X_\epsilon(b)-X_\epsilon(a)
  =
  I_1(p_\epsilon(b)-p_\epsilon(a)).
\]
Multiplying by \(\chi(a)\), integrating, and again using linearity of
\(I_q\) gives
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-tested-chaos-expansion}.  The coefficient of the
first-chaos kernel is precisely the local subtraction from
\eqref{eq:spde-c2-local-coordinate-for-x2y}; no additional contraction is
hidden in \(F_{X^2Y,1}^{\chi}\).

\begin{proposition}[Covariance integral formulas for nonlinear chaos kernels]
\label{prop:spde-nonlinear-negative-coordinate-kernel-norms}
Use the notation and hypotheses of the preceding finite-chaos kernel
calculation.
Write
\[
  G_{uv}=G_\epsilon(u,v),\qquad
  K_{ab}=K_\epsilon(a,b),
\]
and let all integrals below run over two copies of the spacetime variables
\((a,b)\) and \((a',b')\).  Then the Hilbert norms of the tested kernels are
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \|F_{XY,4}^{\chi}\|_{\mathcal H^{\otimes4}}^2
  &=
  \int\chi(a)\chi(a')K_{ab}K_{a'b'}
  \left(
     \frac14G_{aa'}G_{bb'}^3
    +\frac34G_{ab'}G_{ba'}G_{bb'}^2
  \right)\,\dd a\,\dd b\,\dd a'\,\dd b',\\
  \|F_{XY,2}^{\chi}\|_{\mathcal H^{\otimes2}}^2
  &=
  9\int\chi(a)\chi(a')K_{ab}K_{a'b'}G_{ab}G_{a'b'}G_{bb'}^2
  \,\dd a\,\dd b\,\dd a'\,\dd b'.
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-xy-kernel-norm-integrals}
\end{equation}
For the locally subtracted \(X^2Y\) coordinate,
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \|F_{X^2Y,5}^{\chi}\|_{\mathcal H^{\otimes5}}^2
  &=
  \int\chi(a)\chi(a')K_{ab}K_{a'b'}
  \Bigl(
    \frac1{10}G_{aa'}^2G_{bb'}^3
    +\frac35G_{aa'}G_{ab'}G_{ba'}G_{bb'}^2\\
  &\hspace{7.0em}
    +\frac3{10}G_{ab'}^2G_{ba'}^2G_{bb'}
  \Bigr)\,\dd a\,\dd b\,\dd a'\,\dd b',\\
  \|F_{X^2Y,3}^{\chi}\|_{\mathcal H^{\otimes3}}^2
  &=
  36\int\chi(a)\chi(a')K_{ab}K_{a'b'}G_{ab}G_{a'b'}
  \left(
    \frac13G_{aa'}G_{bb'}^2
    +\frac23G_{ab'}G_{ba'}G_{bb'}
  \right)\,\dd a\,\dd b\,\dd a'\,\dd b',\\
  \|F_{X^2Y,1}^{\chi}\|_{\mathcal H}^2
  &=
  36\int\chi(a)\chi(a')K_{ab}K_{a'b'}G_{ab}^2G_{a'b'}^2\\
  &\hspace{5.5em}\times
  \bigl(
    G_{bb'}-G_{ba'}-G_{ab'}+G_{aa'}
  \bigr)\,\dd a\,\dd b\,\dd a'\,\dd b'.
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-x2y-kernel-norm-integrals}
\end{equation}
Consequently, if
\[
\begin{aligned}
  Z_{XY}^{\chi}
  &=
  \int\chi(a)X_\epsilon(a)Y_\epsilon(a)\,\dd a,\\
  Z_{X^2Y}^{\chi}
  &=
  \int\chi(a)
  \bigl(:\!X_\epsilon(a)^2\!:Y_\epsilon(a)
        -3C_{2,\epsilon}(a)X_\epsilon(a)\bigr)\,\dd a ,
\end{aligned}
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathbb E\bigl[|Z_{XY}^{\chi}|^2\bigr]
  &=
  4!\,\|F_{XY,4}^{\chi}\|_{\mathcal H^{\otimes4}}^2
  +2!\,\|F_{XY,2}^{\chi}\|_{\mathcal H^{\otimes2}}^2,\\
  \mathbb E\bigl[|Z_{X^2Y}^{\chi}|^2\bigr]
  &=
  5!\,\|F_{X^2Y,5}^{\chi}\|_{\mathcal H^{\otimes5}}^2
  +3!\,\|F_{X^2Y,3}^{\chi}\|_{\mathcal H^{\otimes3}}^2
  +\|F_{X^2Y,1}^{\chi}\|_{\mathcal H}^2 .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-coordinate-second-moments-from-kernels}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For \(h_1,\ldots,h_q,k_1,\ldots,k_q\in\mathcal H\),
\begin{equation}
  \left\langle
    \operatorname{Sym}_q(h_1\otimes\cdots\otimes h_q),
    \operatorname{Sym}_q(k_1\otimes\cdots\otimes k_q)
  \right\rangle
  =
  \frac1{q!}
  \sum_{\sigma\in S_q}
  \prod_{i=1}^q\langle h_i,k_{\sigma(i)}\rangle_{\mathcal H}.
  \label{eq:spde-symmetrized-tensor-inner-product}
\end{equation}
This is the orthogonal projection formula for symmetrization:
\(\operatorname{Sym}_q^*=\operatorname{Sym}_q\) and
\(\operatorname{Sym}_q^2=\operatorname{Sym}_q\).

Apply \eqref{eq:spde-symmetrized-tensor-inner-product} first to
\(p(a)\otimes p(b)^{\otimes3}\) and
\(p(a')\otimes p(b')^{\otimes3}\).  In a random permutation of the four
right-hand factors, the single \(p(a')\) occupies the single \(p(a)\)-slot
with probability \(1/4\), and one of the three \(p(b)\)-slots with
probability \(3/4\).  This gives the two coefficients in the first line of
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-kernel-norm-integrals}.  The second line follows because
\(p(b)^{\otimes2}\) is already symmetric.

For \(p(a)^{\otimes2}\otimes p(b)^{\otimes3}\), let \(k\) be the number of
right-hand \(p(a')\)-factors landing in the two \(p(a)\)-slots.  The
hypergeometric weights are
\[
  \frac{\binom{2}{2}\binom{3}{0}}{\binom{5}{2}}=\frac1{10},\qquad
  \frac{\binom{2}{1}\binom{3}{1}}{\binom{5}{2}}=\frac35,\qquad
  \frac{\binom{2}{0}\binom{3}{2}}{\binom{5}{2}}=\frac3{10},
\]
for \(k=2,1,0\), respectively.  These are the three coefficients in
\(\|F_{X^2Y,5}^{\chi}\|^2\).  The same count for
\(p(a)\otimes p(b)^{\otimes2}\) gives weights \(1/3\) and \(2/3\), producing
\(\|F_{X^2Y,3}^{\chi}\|^2\).

Finally,
\[
  \langle p(b)-p(a),p(b')-p(a')\rangle_{\mathcal H}
  =
  G_{bb'}-G_{ba'}-G_{ab'}+G_{aa'},
\]
which proves the first-chaos formula.  The second-moment identities
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-coordinate-second-moments-from-kernels} follow from
orthogonality of distinct homogeneous Wiener chaoses and the isometry
\(\mathbb E[I_q(f)I_q(g)]
=q!\langle f,g\rangle_{\mathcal H^{\otimes q}}\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Logarithmic power-counting bound for tested \(XY\) covariance graphs]
\label{prop:spde-xy-tested-graph-log-bound}
Let \(Q=5\).  Assign to a heat edge the singular exponent \(3=Q-2\) and to
one covariance edge the singular exponent \(1=Q-4\).  Consider the three
four-vertex multigraphs on
\[
  V=\{a,b,a',b'\}
\]
which occur in the two \(XY\) covariance expressions
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-kernel-norm-integrals}:
\[
\begin{array}{ll}
  \mathcal G_{4,A}:&
  (a,b)_3,\ (a',b')_3,\ (a,a')_1,\ 3(b,b')_1,\\[0.25em]
  \mathcal G_{4,B}:&
  (a,b)_3,\ (a',b')_3,\ (a,b')_1,\ (b,a')_1,\ 2(b,b')_1,\\[0.25em]
  \mathcal G_{2}:&
  (a,b)_3,\ (a,b)_1,\ (a',b')_3,\ (a',b')_1,\ 2(b,b')_1 .
\end{array}
\]
The subscript is the singular exponent of the corresponding dyadic kernel;
parallel covariance edges are listed with multiplicity.  Let
\[
  s_{\mathcal G}(W)
  =
  \sum_{\substack{e=(u,v)\in E(\mathcal G)\\ u,v\in W}}s_e
\]
for \(W\subset V\), where \(s_e\) is the edge singular exponent.  Then,
for every graph \(\mathcal G\in\{\mathcal G_{4,A},\mathcal G_{4,B},
\mathcal G_2\}\),
\begin{equation}
  \sum_{e\in E(\mathcal G)}s_e
  =
  Q(|V|-2)=10 ,
  \label{eq:spde-xy-graph-total-degree}
\end{equation}
and every proper subset \(W\subsetneq V\) with \(|W|\geq2\) obeys the strict
subgraph inequality
\begin{equation}
  s_{\mathcal G}(W)<Q(|W|-1).
  \label{eq:spde-xy-graph-proper-subgraph-degree}
\end{equation}
More precisely, the smallest deficit
\[
  \Delta_{\mathcal G}(W)
  =
  Q(|W|-1)-s_{\mathcal G}(W)
\]
over proper \(W\) is \(2\) for \(\mathcal G_{4,A}\), \(2\) for
\(\mathcal G_{4,B}\), and \(1\) for \(\mathcal G_2\).

Consequently the only possible scale loss in the scalar second-moment power
counting for the tested \(XY\) kernels is an overall logarithm.  After
dyadic decomposition, all relative-scale sums are geometrically summable;
if \(2^{-M-1}<\delta\leq2^{-M}\), the remaining overall-scale sum is bounded
by \(C(1+M)\).  Hence any scalar covariance integral associated with the
three graphs above and tested by two \(L^1\)-normalized functions supported
in parabolic balls of radius \(O(\delta)\) satisfies a power bound
\begin{equation}
  |I_\delta|
  \leq C_\eta \delta^{-\eta}
  \qquad(\eta>0),
  \label{eq:spde-xy-graph-log-loss-bound}
\end{equation}
provided the dyadic heat and covariance blocks satisfy the support and size
bounds used in Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-dyadic-parabolic-convolution-bound}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The total singular exponent is \(3+3+1+3=10\) for
\(\mathcal G_{4,A}\), \(3+3+1+1+2=10\) for \(\mathcal G_{4,B}\), and
\((3+1)+(3+1)+2=10\) for \(\mathcal G_2\).  This proves
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-graph-total-degree}.

It remains to check proper subgraphs.  For two-vertex subsets, the largest
internal singular exponents are
\[
  \max_{|W|=2}s_{\mathcal G_{4,A}}(W)=3,\qquad
  \max_{|W|=2}s_{\mathcal G_{4,B}}(W)=3,\qquad
  \max_{|W|=2}s_{\mathcal G_2}(W)=4 .
\]
The two fourth-chaos graphs therefore have two-vertex deficit at least \(2\),
while the second-chaos graph has the smaller deficit \(1\), coming from the
parallel heat-covariance pairs \(\{a,b\}\) and \(\{a',b'\}\).  For three
vertices, inspection of the three displayed edge lists gives the following
maximal internal singular exponents:
\[
  \max_{|W|=3}s_{\mathcal G_{4,A}}(W)=6,\qquad
  \max_{|W|=3}s_{\mathcal G_{4,B}}(W)=6,\qquad
  \max_{|W|=3}s_{\mathcal G_2}(W)=6 .
\]
Because \(Q(|W|-1)=10\) when \(|W|=3\), these deficits are at least \(4\).
Thus \eqref{eq:spde-xy-graph-proper-subgraph-degree} holds, with the stated
minimum deficits \(2,2,1\).

Now decompose every heat and covariance factor into dyadic blocks.  A
relative-scale sector is obtained by choosing one overall scale \(n\) for a
spanning cluster of all four vertices and non-negative gap variables
recording how much smaller each proper connected subcluster is.  The support
and size assumptions give, in that sector, a factor
\[
  2^{-\sum_W \Delta_{\mathcal G}(W)r_W}
\]
up to a constant depending only on the dyadic partition and on the finite
graph.  The strict inequalities just proved imply
\(\Delta_{\mathcal G}(W)\geq1\) for every proper cluster which can occur in
the sector decomposition, so Theorem~\ref{thm:spde-multiscale-sector-kernel-summability}
applies to the relative gap variables.

After those relative sums have been performed, the exponent of the remaining
overall scale is zero, precisely because of
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-graph-total-degree} and because the two external test
functions are \(L^1\)-normalized.  Thus the contribution of all overall
scales \(0\leq n\leq M+O(1)\) is \(O(1+M)\); larger scales are killed by the
test-function support and the same proper-cluster estimates.  Finally, for
every \(\eta>0\),
\[
  1+M\leq C_\eta 2^{\eta M}\leq C_\eta\delta^{-\eta}.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:spde-xy-graph-log-loss-bound}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Scalar tested \(XY\) coordinate bound]
\label{prop:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-logarithmic-scale-bound}
Let the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-graph-log-bound} hold uniformly for the
cutoff heat and covariance blocks on a compact spacetime set.  Let
\(\varphi\in C_c^r(\R^{1+3})\) be supported in the unit parabolic ball, let
\(\|\varphi\|_{C^r}\leq1\), and define the \(L^1\)-normalized test density
\[
  \varphi_z^\delta(a)
  =
  \delta^{-Q}\varphi(\mathsf D_{\delta}^{-1}(a-z)),
  \qquad Q=5 .
\]
For the finite-cutoff field, set
\begin{equation}
  Z_{\epsilon,\delta,z}^{XY}(\varphi)
  =
  \int\varphi_z^\delta(a)X_\epsilon(a)Y_\epsilon(a)\,\dd a .
  \label{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-random-variable}
\end{equation}
Then, for every \(\eta>0\), there is a constant \(C_\eta\), uniform for
\(\epsilon\) and for \(z\) in the chosen compact set, such that
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb E\bigl|Z_{\epsilon,\delta,z}^{XY}(\varphi)\bigr|^2
  \leq
  C_\eta\delta^{-\eta}.
  \label{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-l2-log-loss}
\end{equation}
Consequently, for every even \(p\geq2\) and every
\[
  0<\zeta_{XY}<4\kappa ,
\]
there is a constant \(C_{p,\zeta_{XY}}\) such that
\begin{equation}
  \left\|
    \delta^{4\kappa}Z_{\epsilon,\delta,z}^{XY}(\varphi)
  \right\|_{L^p(\Omega)}
  \leq
  C_{p,\zeta_{XY}}\delta^{4\kappa-\zeta_{XY}} .
  \label{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-normalized-slack}
\end{equation}

This is the scalar tested base estimate for the \(XY\) coordinate.  The full
input required by
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-input-from-kernels}
additionally requires the same multiscale estimate after dualizing the
test-function variable and after taking differences in the parameters
\((z,\delta)\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Insert \(\chi=\varphi_z^\delta\) in
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-kernel-norm-integrals}.  The density
\(\varphi_z^\delta\) is \(L^1\)-normalized, and its support lies in a
parabolic ball of radius \(O(\delta)\).  Each of the three scalar covariance
graphs in \eqref{eq:spde-xy-kernel-norm-integrals} is therefore bounded by
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-graph-log-bound}.  The numerical
coefficients \(1/4\), \(3/4\), and \(9\), and the chaos factors \(4!\) and
\(2!\), are finite fixed constants.  Thus
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-coordinate-second-moments-from-kernels} gives
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-l2-log-loss}.

The random variable \(Z_{\epsilon,\delta,z}^{XY}(\varphi)\) is the sum of a
fourth-chaos and a second-chaos variable by
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-chaos-expansion}.  Applying
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-finite-wiener-chaos-moment-bound} to these two
homogeneous chaos components gives
\[
  \left\|Z_{\epsilon,\delta,z}^{XY}(\varphi)\right\|_{L^p}
  \leq
  C_p
  \left\|Z_{\epsilon,\delta,z}^{XY}(\varphi)\right\|_{L^2}.
 \]
Choose \(\eta=2\zeta_{XY}\) in
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-l2-log-loss}.  Multiplication by the
model normalization
\[
  \delta^{-|XY|}=\delta^{4\kappa}
\]
then gives
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-normalized-slack}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Scalar tested \(XY\) parameter-edge bound]
\label{prop:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-parameter-edge-bound}
Keep the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-logarithmic-scale-bound}.
Let \(r\geq1\), \(0<\theta\leq1\), and let
\[
  \mathcal X_{\Pi,m}=K\times[1/2,1],
  \qquad
  d_{\Pi,m}((z,a),(z',a'))=2^m\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}+|a-a'|.
\]
For \(u=(z,a)\in\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\), put
\[
  \delta_u=2^{-m}a,\qquad
  \varphi_u(a_0)
  =
  \delta_u^{-Q}\varphi(\mathsf D_{\delta_u}^{-1}(a_0-z)),
  \qquad \|\varphi\|_{C^r}\leq1 .
\]
Define
\[
  Z_{\epsilon,m,u}^{XY}(\varphi)
  =
  \int \varphi_u(a_0)X_\epsilon(a_0)Y_\epsilon(a_0)\,\dd a_0 .
\]
Then, whenever \(d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)\leq1\), for every even \(p\geq2\) and
every \(0<\zeta_{XY}<4\kappa\),
\begin{equation}
  \left\|
    2^{-4\kappa m}
    \bigl(
      Z_{\epsilon,m,v}^{XY}(\varphi)
      -Z_{\epsilon,m,u}^{XY}(\varphi)
    \bigr)
  \right\|_{L^p(\Omega)}
  \leq
  C_{p,\zeta_{XY},\theta}
  2^{-(4\kappa-\zeta_{XY})m}
  d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)^\theta .
  \label{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-edge-normalized}
\end{equation}
The constant is uniform in the cutoff and in \(u,v\) with centers in the
fixed compact set.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
First record the deterministic variation of the transported test density.
For \(r\geq1\), the map
\[
  (z,a)\longmapsto
  (2^{-m}a)^{-Q}\varphi(\mathsf D_{(2^{-m}a)^{-1}}(\,\cdot-z))
\]
is Lipschitz from \(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\) to \(L^1\), uniformly in \(m\) and
in \(\|\varphi\|_{C^1}\leq1\).  Indeed, translation by \(z\) differentiates
the test by \(\nabla_{\mathfrak s}\varphi\) and produces the dimensionless
factor \(2^m\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}\); differentiating in the scale
parameter \(a\in[1/2,1]\) differentiates the map
\[
  a^{-Q}\varphi(\mathsf D_{a^{-1}}w)
\]
on a compact interval.  Therefore
\begin{equation}
  \|\varphi_v-\varphi_u\|_{L^1}
  \leq
  C\,d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)
  \leq
  C\,d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)^\theta ,
  \label{eq:spde-xy-test-density-lone-edge}
\end{equation}
because \(d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)\leq1\).  The supports of \(\varphi_u\) and
\(\varphi_v\) lie in a common parabolic ball of radius \(C2^{-m}\).

Set \(\Delta\varphi=\varphi_v-\varphi_u\).  By linearity,
\[
  Z_{\epsilon,m,v}^{XY}(\varphi)-Z_{\epsilon,m,u}^{XY}(\varphi)
  =
  \int\Delta\varphi(a_0)X_\epsilon(a_0)Y_\epsilon(a_0)\,\dd a_0 .
\]
The covariance-graph estimate used in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-logarithmic-scale-bound} is
homogeneous in the two external test densities.  Applying it to
\(\Delta\varphi\) in both slots, using
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-test-density-lone-edge}, and taking
\(\delta=2^{-m}\) gives, for every \(\eta>0\),
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb E
  \left|
    Z_{\epsilon,m,v}^{XY}(\varphi)-Z_{\epsilon,m,u}^{XY}(\varphi)
  \right|^2
  \leq
  C_\eta
  d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)^{2\theta}
  2^{\eta m}.
  \label{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-edge-l2}
\end{equation}
The difference is again a sum of fourth- and second-chaos variables, so the
finite-chaos moment bound gives its \(L^p\)-norm from the square root of
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-edge-l2}.  Choose
\(\eta=2\zeta_{XY}\) and multiply by the model normalization
\(2^{-4\kappa m}\).  This proves
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-edge-normalized}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Scalar tested \(XY\) cutoff-shell gain]
\label{prop:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-cutoff-shell-gain}
Keep the notation and graph hypotheses of
Propositions~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-graph-log-bound} and
\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-logarithmic-scale-bound}.  Let
\((X_n,Y_n)\) be a dyadic ultraviolet cutoff sequence, and write
\[
  Z_{n,m,u}^{XY}(\varphi)
  =
  \int\varphi_u(a_0)X_n(a_0)Y_n(a_0)\,\dd a_0
\]
with \(\varphi_u\) as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-parameter-edge-bound}.
Assume the cutoff difference \(Z_{n+1,m,u}^{XY}-Z_{n,m,u}^{XY}\) has the
following admissible shell representation: after expanding the second moment
by the finite-chaos formulas
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-chaos-expansion} and
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-kernel-norm-integrals}, every term is a finite linear
combination of the three \(XY\) graph integrals in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-graph-log-bound}, with at least one
heat or covariance edge replaced by a cutoff-shell block whose dyadic scale
is \(\geq n-c_0\).  The shell block satisfies the same support and size
bounds as the corresponding ordinary dyadic block, with constants independent
of \(n\).

Then, for every \(\eta>0\), every \(0<\rho<1/2\), and every
\(u\in\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\),
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb E
  \left|
    Z_{n+1,m,u}^{XY}(\varphi)-Z_{n,m,u}^{XY}(\varphi)
  \right|^2
  \leq
  C_{\eta,\rho}\,
  2^{\eta m}\,
  2^{-2\rho(n-m)_+}.
  \label{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-cutoff-shell-l2}
\end{equation}
Consequently, for every even \(p\geq2\) and every
\[
  0<\zeta_{XY}<4\kappa ,
\]
\begin{equation}
  \left\|
    2^{-4\kappa m}
    \bigl(
      Z_{n+1,m,u}^{XY}(\varphi)-Z_{n,m,u}^{XY}(\varphi)
    \bigr)
  \right\|_{L^p(\Omega)}
  \leq
  C_{p,\zeta_{XY},\rho}
  2^{-(4\kappa-\zeta_{XY})m}
  2^{-\rho(n-m)_+}.
  \label{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-cutoff-shell-normalized}
\end{equation}
The estimate is uniform for \(u\) with center in a fixed compact set.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let \(M=m+O(1)\) be the largest overall graph scale that can interact with
two \(L^1\)-normalized test densities supported in parabolic balls of radius
\(O(2^{-m})\).  The unconstrained graph estimate in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-graph-log-bound} leaves only the
overall-scale sum \(0\leq N\leq M+O(1)\), producing the logarithmic loss
recorded there.

Now impose the shell condition from the cutoff increment.  In the dyadic
sector decomposition used in the proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-graph-log-bound}, the edge at scale
\(\geq n-c_0\) either lies at the overall scale or creates a proper
subcluster whose relative-scale gap is at least
\((n-M-C)_+\).  The first alternative can occur only when
\(n\leq M+C\).  In the second alternative, the sector carries the additional
factor
\[
  2^{-\Delta r}
\]
with \(r\geq n-M-C\) and with
\(\Delta\geq1\), because the smallest proper-subgraph deficit among the
three \(XY\) graphs is \(1\).  Therefore every sector with \(n>M+C\) gains
at least \(2^{-(n-M-C)}\).  Enlarging the constant absorbs the fixed \(C\)
and gives, for every graph contribution,
\[
  |I_{n,m}^{\Delta XY}|
  \leq
  C_\eta 2^{\eta m}2^{-(n-m)_+}.
\]
Since \(0<\rho<1/2\), the weaker bound
\[
  2^{-(n-m)_+}
  \leq C_\rho 2^{-2\rho(n-m)_+}
\]
holds uniformly in \(m,n\).  Summing the finite list of graph terms in the
admissible shell representation gives
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-cutoff-shell-l2}.

The cutoff difference is still a finite sum of homogeneous Wiener-chaos
variables of orders \(4\) and \(2\).  Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-finite-wiener-chaos-moment-bound}
therefore bounds its \(L^p\)-norm by a constant times the square root of
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-cutoff-shell-l2}.  Choose
\(\eta=2\zeta_{XY}\) and multiply by the model normalization
\(2^{-4\kappa m}\).  This proves
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-cutoff-shell-normalized}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Scalar tested high-chaos \(X^2Y\) bound]
\label{prop:spde-x2y-high-chaos-tested-coordinate-bound}
Let \(Q=5\).  Use the same dyadic heat and covariance block hypotheses as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-graph-log-bound}.  Consider the five
four-vertex multigraphs on \(V=\{a,b,a',b'\}\) which occur in the fifth- and
third-chaos parts of
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-kernel-norm-integrals}:
\[
\begin{array}{ll}
  \mathcal H_{5,A}:&
  (a,b)_3,\ (a',b')_3,\ 2(a,a')_1,\ 3(b,b')_1,\\[0.25em]
  \mathcal H_{5,B}:&
  (a,b)_3,\ (a',b')_3,\ (a,a')_1,\ (a,b')_1,\
  (b,a')_1,\ 2(b,b')_1,\\[0.25em]
  \mathcal H_{5,C}:&
  (a,b)_3,\ (a',b')_3,\ 2(a,b')_1,\ 2(b,a')_1,\ (b,b')_1,\\[0.25em]
  \mathcal H_{3,A}:&
  (a,b)_3,\ (a,b)_1,\ (a',b')_3,\ (a',b')_1,\
  (a,a')_1,\ 2(b,b')_1,\\[0.25em]
  \mathcal H_{3,B}:&
  (a,b)_3,\ (a,b)_1,\ (a',b')_3,\ (a',b')_1,\
  (a,b')_1,\ (b,a')_1,\ (b,b')_1 .
\end{array}
\]
The subscript again denotes the singular exponent of the edge.  For every
one of these graphs,
\begin{equation}
  \sum_{e\in E(\mathcal H)}s_e
  =
  Q(|V|-2)+1=11 .
  \label{eq:spde-x2y-high-chaos-graph-total-degree}
\end{equation}
Every proper subset \(W\subsetneq V\) with \(|W|\geq2\) obeys
\[
  s_{\mathcal H}(W)<Q(|W|-1).
\]
The minimum proper-subgraph deficit is \(2\) for each fifth-chaos graph and
\(1\) for each third-chaos graph.

Consequently, if \(\chi_z^\delta\) is an \(L^1\)-normalized test density
supported in a parabolic ball of radius \(O(\delta)\), then the scalar
covariance integrals belonging to the fifth- and third-chaos \(X^2Y\) kernels
obey
\begin{equation}
  |I_\delta^{X^2Y,\geq3}|
  \leq C\delta^{-1},
  \qquad 0<\delta\leq1 .
  \label{eq:spde-x2y-high-chaos-graph-power-bound}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, if
\[
  Z_{\epsilon,\delta,z}^{X^2Y,\geq3}(\varphi)
  =
  I_5(F_{X^2Y,5}^{\chi_z^\delta})
  +
  I_3(F_{X^2Y,3}^{\chi_z^\delta}),
\]
then, uniformly in the cutoff and for \(z\) in a fixed compact set,
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb E
  \left|
    Z_{\epsilon,\delta,z}^{X^2Y,\geq3}(\varphi)
  \right|^2
  \leq C\delta^{-1}.
  \label{eq:spde-x2y-high-chaos-tested-l2}
\end{equation}
For every even \(p\geq2\),
\begin{equation}
  \left\|
    \delta^{1/2+5\kappa}
    Z_{\epsilon,\delta,z}^{X^2Y,\geq3}(\varphi)
  \right\|_{L^p(\Omega)}
  \leq
  C_p\delta^{5\kappa}.
  \label{eq:spde-x2y-high-chaos-normalized-slack}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The edge lists give total degree \(3+3+5=11\) for the three fifth-chaos
graphs and \(3+1+3+1+3=11\) for the two third-chaos graphs, which proves
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-high-chaos-graph-total-degree}.  For two-vertex subsets,
the largest internal singular exponent is \(3\) in the fifth-chaos graphs and
\(4\) in the third-chaos graphs.  These give deficits \(2\) and \(1\),
respectively, relative to \(Q(|W|-1)=5\).  For three-vertex subsets,
inspection of the displayed edge lists gives maximal internal singular
exponent \(6\) in all five graphs, hence deficit \(4\) relative to
\(Q(|W|-1)=10\).  This proves the strict proper-subgraph inequalities and the
stated minimum deficits.

The dyadic sector argument uses the same multiscale sector decomposition as
the \(XY\) graph bound above.  The strict proper-subgraph deficits make every
relative-scale gap geometrically summable by the multiscale sector
summability theorem.  After the relative sums have been performed, the
remaining overall scale has exponent one, because the total graph degree is
\(Q(|V|-2)+1\) rather than \(Q(|V|-2)\).  If
\(2^{-M-1}<\delta\leq2^{-M}\), the relevant overall scales therefore
contribute
\[
  \sum_{0\leq n\leq M+O(1)}2^n\leq C2^M\leq C\delta^{-1},
\]
and scales larger than \(M+O(1)\) are excluded by the test supports together
with the same relative-cluster estimates.  This proves
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-high-chaos-graph-power-bound}.

Insert \(\chi=\chi_z^\delta\) in the fifth- and third-chaos lines of
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-kernel-norm-integrals}.  The fixed numerical coefficients
and the chaos factors \(5!\) and \(3!\) are absorbed into \(C\), and
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-coordinate-second-moments-from-kernels} gives
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-high-chaos-tested-l2}.  The variable
\(Z_{\epsilon,\delta,z}^{X^2Y,\geq3}\) is a finite sum of homogeneous Wiener
chaoses of orders \(5\) and \(3\); the finite-chaos moment estimate converts
the \(L^2\)-bound to \(L^p\).  Multiplication by the model normalization
\(\delta^{1/2+5\kappa}\), corresponding to true target regularity
\(-1/2\) and assigned regularity \(-1/2-5\kappa\), gives
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-high-chaos-normalized-slack}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scalar shell gain and projective cutoff input]
\label{rem:spde-xy-scalar-shell-versus-projective-cutoff}
Estimate~\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-coordinate-cutoff-shell-normalized} is a
scale-separated scalar Cauchy estimate.  It identifies where the ultraviolet
shell gain enters the \(XY\) graph analysis.
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-x2y-high-chaos-tested-coordinate-bound} supplies
the parallel scalar base estimate for the fifth- and third-chaos pieces of
\(X^2Y\).  The remaining \(X^2Y\) first-chaos component is different: its
local subtraction produces covariance increments, treated below in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-x2y-first-chaos-logarithmic-scale-bound}.
Corollary~\ref{cor:spde-scale-summed-shell-separated-cutoff-bridge} then
converts this scalar factor into a scale-summed cutoff rate whenever the
normalization slack exceeds the parameter entropy.  The projective
cutoff-increment hypothesis
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-cutoff-base} asks for a
uniform factor \(2^{-\rho n}\) in the full \(E_r'\)-dualized kernel norm.
The scalar estimate gives the finite-coordinate shell mechanism; the
dualized cutoff-increment estimate and its parameter-edge version supply the
corresponding projective-kernel input needed by the \(\Phi^4_3\)
model-convergence theorem.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Nonlinear \(\Pi\)-coordinate input from projective kernel bounds]
\label{prop:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-input-from-kernels}
Let \(K\subset\R^{1+3}\) be compact and let
\[
  \mathcal X_{\Pi,m}=K\times[1/2,1],
  \qquad
  d_{\Pi,m}((z,a),(z',a'))=2^m\|z-z'\|_{\mathfrak s}+|a-a'|
\]
be the physical \(\Pi\)-coordinate spaces of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy}.  Let
\[
  E_r=
  \{\varphi\in C^r(\R^{1+3}):
    \operatorname{supp}\varphi\subset B_{\mathfrak s}(0,1)\},
  \qquad
  \|\varphi\|_{E_r}=\|\varphi\|_{C^r}.
\]
Fix
\[
  0<\kappa<\frac1{14},
  \qquad
  0\leq\zeta_{XY}<4\kappa,
  \qquad
  0<\zeta_{X^2Y}<5\kappa,
\]
and set
\[
  |\!XY\!|=-4\kappa,\qquad
  |X^2Y|=-\frac12-5\kappa,
\]
\begin{equation}
  \sigma_{XY}=4\kappa-\zeta_{XY},
  \qquad
  \sigma_{X^2Y}=5\kappa-\zeta_{X^2Y} .
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-slacks}
\end{equation}
The loss \(\zeta_{XY}\) is optional: it may be set to zero only after the
concrete \(XY\) projective kernel estimate proves that the marginal
overall-scale logarithm in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-xy-tested-graph-log-bound} is absent
or harmless in the chosen norm.  The loss \(\zeta_{X^2Y}\) is reserved for
logarithmic factors in the locally subtracted first-chaos component of
\(X^2Y\).

For
\[
  \mathfrak C_{\rm nl}=\{XY,X^2Y\},
  \qquad
  \mathcal Q_{XY}=\{4,2\},
  \qquad
  \mathcal Q_{X^2Y}=\{5,3,1\},
\]
let \(F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u)\in\mathcal H^{\odot q}\widehat\otimes_\pi E_r'\),
where
\[
  n\geq1,\qquad
  \tau\in\mathfrak C_{\rm nl},\qquad
  q\in\mathcal Q_\tau,\qquad
  m\geq0,\qquad
  u=(z,a)\in\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}.
\]
Assume that the \(E_r'\)-valued chaos expansion
\begin{equation}
  Y_{n,\tau,m}(u)
  =
  \sum_{q\in\mathcal Q_\tau}I_q(F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u))
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-er-chaos}
\end{equation}
is the scale-normalized tested \(\Pi\)-coordinate:
\begin{equation}
  Y_{n,\tau,m}(z,a)(\varphi)
  =
  (2^{-m}a)^{-|\tau|}
  \left\langle
    \Pi_z^{(n)}\tau,\varphi_z^{\,2^{-m}a}
  \right\rangle .
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-er-identification}
\end{equation}
For \(X^2Y\), the kernels are those of the locally subtracted coordinate
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-finite-cutoff-wick-decomposition}; equivalently, after
pairing with a test density, they reduce to
\eqref{eq:spde-x2y-tested-chaos-kernels}.  For \(XY\), they reduce to
\eqref{eq:spde-xy-tested-chaos-kernels}.

Choose \(0<\theta\leq1\), an even integer \(p=2m_0\), and \(\rho>0\) such
that
\begin{equation}
  p\sigma_\tau>5
  \quad(\tau\in\mathfrak C_{\rm nl}),
  \qquad
  p\theta>6 .
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-moment-condition}
\end{equation}
Suppose that there are constants
\[
  B_{\tau,q,0},\ B_{\tau,q,1},\
  \widetilde B_{\tau,q,0},\ \widetilde B_{\tau,q,1}<\infty
\]
such that, for every \(n,m,\tau,q\) and \(u,v\in\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\) with
\(d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)\leq1\),
\begin{equation}
  \|F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u)\|_\pi
  \leq
  B_{\tau,q,0}2^{-\sigma_\tau m},
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-base}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
  \|F_{n,\tau,q,m}(v)-F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u)\|_\pi
  \leq
  B_{\tau,q,1}2^{-\sigma_\tau m}d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)^\theta,
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-edge}
\end{equation}
and the cutoff increments obey
\begin{equation}
  \|F_{n+1,\tau,q,m}(u)-F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u)\|_\pi
  \leq
  \widetilde B_{\tau,q,0}2^{-\rho n}2^{-\sigma_\tau m},
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-cutoff-base}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  &\|
    (F_{n+1,\tau,q,m}(v)-F_{n,\tau,q,m}(v))
    -(F_{n+1,\tau,q,m}(u)-F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u))
  \|_\pi                                             \\
  &\qquad\leq
  \widetilde B_{\tau,q,1}2^{-\rho n}
  2^{-\sigma_\tau m}d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)^\theta .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-cutoff-edge}
\end{equation}
Then the nonlinear coordinates \(XY\) and \(X^2Y\) satisfy the
\(\Pi\)-coordinate hypotheses of
the negative-sector coordinate-control consequence with
\begin{equation}
  D_\tau=5,\qquad d_\tau=6,\qquad
  \varepsilon_\tau=p\theta-6 .
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-entropy-data}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\[
  U_{n,\tau,m}(u)=\|Y_{n,\tau,m}(u)\|_{E_r'}
\]
and \(V_{n,\tau,m}\) is defined by replacing \(Y_{n,\tau,m}\) with
\(Y_{n+1,\tau,m}-Y_{n,\tau,m}\), then, on the nets of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy},
\[
  \mathbb E|U_{n,\tau,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  A_{\tau,0}^{\,p}2^{-p\sigma_\tau m},
  \qquad
  \mathbb E|V_{n,\tau,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  \widetilde A_{\tau,0}^{\,p}2^{-p\rho n}2^{-p\sigma_\tau m},
\]
and
\[
