  \mathbb E|U_{n,\tau,m}(v)-U_{n,\tau,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  A_{\tau,1}^{\,p}2^{-p\sigma_\tau m}2^{-(6+\varepsilon_\tau)\ell},
\]
\[
  \mathbb E|V_{n,\tau,m}(v)-V_{n,\tau,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  \widetilde A_{\tau,1}^{\,p}2^{-p\rho n}2^{-p\sigma_\tau m}
  2^{-(6+\varepsilon_\tau)\ell}
\]
for all \((u,v)\in\mathcal E_{\Pi,m,\ell}\).  The constants are
\begin{equation}
  A_{\tau,i}=
  \sum_{q\in\mathcal Q_\tau}C_{q,m_0}B_{\tau,q,i},
  \qquad
  \widetilde A_{\tau,i}=
  \sum_{q\in\mathcal Q_\tau}C_{q,m_0}\widetilde B_{\tau,q,i},
  \qquad i=0,1,
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-moment-constants}
\end{equation}
where \(C_{q,m_0}\) is the finite-chaos constant in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-dual-norm-finite-chaos-estimate}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-er-identification},
\[
  \|Y_{n,\tau,m}(z,a)\|_{E_r'}
  =
  \sup_{\varphi\in\mathcal B_r}
  (2^{-m}a)^{-|\tau|}
  \left|
    \left\langle
      \Pi_z^{(n)}\tau,\varphi_z^{\,2^{-m}a}
    \right\rangle
  \right| .
\]
Thus \(U_{n,\tau,m}\) is exactly the physical
\(\Pi\)-coordinate \(Q_{n,\tau}^\#\) restricted to dyadic scale \(m\), and
the analogous statement holds for cutoff differences.

Apply Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-dual-norm-finite-chaos-estimate} to
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-er-chaos}.  The projective base bound
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-base} gives
\begin{equation}
  \|U_{n,\tau,m}(u)\|_{L^p(\Omega)}
  \leq
  \sum_{q\in\mathcal Q_\tau}
  C_{q,m_0}B_{\tau,q,0}2^{-\sigma_\tau m}
  =
  A_{\tau,0}2^{-\sigma_\tau m}.
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-lp-base-proof}
\end{equation}
The cutoff base estimate follows in the same way from
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-cutoff-base}.  For
increments, use
\[
  \bigl|\|A\|_{E_r'}-\|B\|_{E_r'}\bigr|\leq\|A-B\|_{E_r'}
\]
and then apply the finite-chaos estimate to
\[
  Y_{n,\tau,m}(v)-Y_{n,\tau,m}(u)
  =
  \sum_{q\in\mathcal Q_\tau}
  I_q(F_{n,\tau,q,m}(v)-F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u)).
\]
This proves
\begin{equation}
  \|U_{n,\tau,m}(v)-U_{n,\tau,m}(u)\|_{L^p}
  \leq
  A_{\tau,1}2^{-\sigma_\tau m}d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)^\theta,
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-lp-edge-proof}
\end{equation}
and the cutoff edge estimate follows from
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-cutoff-edge}.

For an edge \((u,v)\in\mathcal E_{\Pi,m,\ell}\), the construction in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy} gives
\[
  d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)\leq C2^{-\ell}.
\]
Absorbing the fixed constant \(C^\theta\) into \(A_{\tau,1}\) and
\(\widetilde A_{\tau,1}\), and then raising the \(L^p\)-bounds to the
\(p\)-th power, gives the displayed edge moments because
\[
  p\theta=6+\varepsilon_\tau .
\]
The same entropy proposition gives \(D_\tau=5\) and \(d_\tau=6\).  The
conditions
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-moment-condition} are precisely
\[
  \sigma_\tau>\frac{D_\tau}{p},
  \qquad
  \varepsilon_\tau>0 .
\]
The required sample continuity follows from the same finite-net estimate and
does not require an additional stochastic input.  For fixed \(n,\tau,m\),
choose nested \(2^{-\ell}\)-nets in \(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\) as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-negative-sector-physical-parameter-entropy}.  The
edge family at level \(\ell\) has cardinality at most
\[
  C2^{5m}2^{6\ell}.
\]
By \eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-lp-edge-proof},
\[
  \sum_{\ell\geq0}
  \mathbb E
  \sum_{(u,v)\in\mathcal E_{\Pi,m,\ell}}
  |U_{n,\tau,m}(v)-U_{n,\tau,m}(u)|^p
  \leq
  C_{n,\tau,m}
  \sum_{\ell\geq0}2^{-(p\theta-6)\ell}<\infty .
\]
Fubini therefore gives almost sure summability of the \(p\)-th powers of the
dyadic edge increments.  Since a summable nonnegative sequence tends to zero
along the levels, the usual nearest-net telescoping sequence is almost surely
Cauchy uniformly along every chain of nested approximants.  This defines a
continuous modification on the compact metric space
\(\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}\).  Applying the identical dyadic-edge summability
estimate to \(V_{n,\tau,m}\), with the \(V\)-moment bounds in place of the
\(U\)-moment bounds, gives the required continuous modification for the
cutoff-difference field.  Hence all hypotheses needed for
the negative-sector coordinate-control consequence are
satisfied for the nonlinear \(\Pi\)-coordinates.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Shell-separated nonlinear \(\Pi\)-coordinate cutoff input]
\label{cor:spde-nonlinear-pi-shell-separated-cutoff-input}
Keep the notation and hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-input-from-kernels} for
the uniform base and parameter-edge bounds
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-base} and
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-edge}.  Replace the
cutoff assumptions
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-cutoff-base} and
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-projective-cutoff-edge} by the
shell-separated estimates
\begin{equation}
  \|F_{n+1,\tau,q,m}(u)-F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u)\|_\pi
  \leq
  \widehat B_{\tau,q,0}
  2^{-\sigma_\tau m}2^{-\rho_\tau(n-m)_+},
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-shell-projective-cutoff-base}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  &\|
    (F_{n+1,\tau,q,m}(v)-F_{n,\tau,q,m}(v))
    -(F_{n+1,\tau,q,m}(u)-F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u))
  \|_\pi                                             \\
  &\qquad\leq
  \widehat B_{\tau,q,1}
  2^{-\sigma_\tau m}2^{-\rho_\tau(n-m)_+}
  d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)^\theta ,
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-shell-projective-cutoff-edge}
\end{equation}
for constants \(\rho_\tau>0\).  Let \(p=2m_0\) be the chosen even moment
order, and assume
\[
  p\sigma_\tau>5,\qquad p\theta>6 .
\]
For any
\begin{equation}
  0<\rho_\tau^*
  <
  \min\left\{
    \rho_\tau,\,
    \sigma_\tau-\frac5p
  \right\},
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-shell-retained-rate}
\end{equation}
there is a finite constant \(\widehat S_\tau^{\rm sh}\) such that the
cutoff-difference field
\[
  V_{n,\tau,m}(u)
  =
  \left\|
    \sum_{q\in\mathcal Q_\tau}
    I_q(F_{n+1,\tau,q,m}(u)-F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u))
  \right\|_{E_r'}
\]
satisfies the scale-summed estimate
\begin{equation}
  \left\|
    \sup_{m\geq0}\sup_{u\in\mathcal X_{\Pi,m}} V_{n,\tau,m}(u)
  \right\|_{L^p(\Omega)}
  \leq
  \widehat S_\tau^{\rm sh}\,2^{-\rho_\tau^*n}.
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-shell-scale-summed-cutoff}
\end{equation}
One may take
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \widehat S_\tau^{\rm sh}
  &=
  H_{\rho_\tau^*,\rho_\tau,\sigma_\tau-5/p}
  \left(
    C_{\Pi,0}^{1/p}\widehat A_{\tau,0}
    +
    C_{\Pi,1}^{1/p}\widehat A_{\tau,1}
    (1-2^{-(p\theta-6)/p})^{-1}
  \right),\\
  \widehat A_{\tau,i}
  &=
  \sum_{q\in\mathcal Q_\tau}
  C_{q,m_0}\widehat B_{\tau,q,i},
  \qquad i=0,1 .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-shell-scale-summed-constant}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
For the cutoff-difference chaos kernels, apply
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-dual-norm-finite-chaos-estimate} exactly as in
the proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-nonlinear-pi-coordinate-input-from-kernels}.
The base estimate gives
\[
  \|V_{n,\tau,m}(u)\|_{L^p}
  \leq
  \widehat A_{\tau,0}
  2^{-\sigma_\tau m}2^{-\rho_\tau(n-m)_+}.
\]
For an edge \((u,v)\in\mathcal E_{\Pi,m,\ell}\), use the norm inequality
\[
  |V_{n,\tau,m}(v)-V_{n,\tau,m}(u)|
  \leq
  \left\|
    \Delta_nY_{\tau,m}(v)-\Delta_nY_{\tau,m}(u)
  \right\|_{E_r'}
\]
where
\[
  \Delta_nY_{\tau,m}(u)
  =
  \sum_{q\in\mathcal Q_\tau}
  I_q(F_{n+1,\tau,q,m}(u)-F_{n,\tau,q,m}(u)).
\]
The shell-separated edge hypothesis
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-shell-projective-cutoff-edge} and
the finite-chaos estimate give
\[
  \|V_{n,\tau,m}(v)-V_{n,\tau,m}(u)\|_{L^p}
  \leq
  \widehat A_{\tau,1}
  2^{-\sigma_\tau m}2^{-\rho_\tau(n-m)_+}
  d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)^\theta .
\]
On the dyadic edge set,
\[
  d_{\Pi,m}(u,v)\leq C2^{-\ell}.
\]
Absorb \(C^\theta\) into \(\widehat A_{\tau,1}\).  Since the edge entropy is
six, the edge moment has excess exponent
\[
  \varepsilon_\tau=p\theta-6>0 .
\]
The entropy in the physical scale \(m\) is \(D=5\), and the effective
scale slack is
\[
  a_\tau=\sigma_\tau-\frac5p>0 .
\]
Corollary~\ref{cor:spde-scale-summed-shell-separated-cutoff-bridge}, or
equivalently the projective version
Corollary~\ref{cor:spde-projective-shell-separated-coordinate-criterion}
with \(D=5\), \(d=6\), \(B_\pi=\widehat A_{\tau,0}\), and
\(B_\pi^{\rm ed}=\widehat A_{\tau,1}\), gives
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-shell-scale-summed-cutoff} with the constant
\eqref{eq:spde-nonlinear-pi-shell-scale-summed-constant}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Scale bound for the locally subtracted first-chaos kernel]
\label{prop:spde-x2y-first-chaos-logarithmic-scale-bound}
Let \(Q=5\), \(\mathfrak s=(2,1,1,1)\), and
\[
  \mathsf D_\delta(t,x)=(\delta^2t,\delta x).
\]
Fix \(0<\theta\leq1\).  Let
\[
  \chi_z^\delta(a)
  =
  \delta^{-Q}\chi(\mathsf D_\delta^{-1}(a-z)),
  \qquad
  0<\delta\leq1,
\]
where \(\chi\) is supported in a fixed unit parabolic ball and
\(\|\chi\|_{L^\infty}\leq1\).  For \(n\geq0\), let \(A_n(a,h)\) be the
shell packet of the local two-loop factor \(K(a,a+h)G(a,a+h)^2\).  Assume
there are constants \(R,A_0\) such that
\begin{equation}
  A_n(a,h)=0\quad\text{unless }\|h\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq R2^{-n},
  \qquad
  \sup_a\int |A_n(a,h)|\,\dd h\leq A_0 .
  \label{eq:spde-local-two-loop-shell-lone-bound}
\end{equation}
Let \(C_s\), \(s\geq0\), be dyadic covariance blocks of order \(4\).  Assume
that, whenever \(h\) and \(h'\) lie in the supports of \(A_n\) and
\(A_{n'}\), the double increment
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \Delta_{h,h'}C_s(a,a')
  &=
  C_s(a+h,a'+h')-C_s(a+h,a')\\
  &\qquad
  -C_s(a,a'+h')+C_s(a,a')
\end{aligned}
\]
satisfies
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  |\Delta_{h,h'}C_s(a,a')|
  &\leq
  A_0\,2^s\,
  2^{-\theta(n-s)_+}
  2^{-\theta(n'-s)_+}                                   \\
  &\quad\times
  \sum_{\rho\in\{0,h\}}\sum_{\rho'\in\{0,h'\}}
  \mathbf 1_{\{\|a+\rho-a'-\rho'\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq R2^{-s}\}} .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-covariance-block-double-increment-bound}
\end{equation}
For a finite ultraviolet cutoff \(N\), define the scalar sector sum
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  V_{\delta,N}^{(1)}
  &=
  \sum_{0\leq n,n',s\leq N}
  \int
  \chi_z^\delta(a)\chi_z^\delta(a')A_n(a,h)A_{n'}(a',h')\\
  &\hspace{8.0em}\times
  \Delta_{h,h'}C_s(a,a')\,
  \dd h\,\dd h'\,\dd a\,\dd a' .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-first-chaos-sector-sum}
\end{equation}
Then there is a constant \(C\), independent of \(z\), \(\delta\), and \(N\),
such that
\begin{equation}
  |V_{\delta,N}^{(1)}|
  \leq
  C\,\delta^{-1}
  \bigl(1+|\log_2\delta|\bigr)^2 .
  \label{eq:spde-first-chaos-logarithmic-variance-bound}
\end{equation}
Consequently, if \(Z_{\delta,N}^{(1)}\) is the first-chaos part of the
tested locally subtracted \(X^2Y\) coordinate whose second moment is bounded
by a finite sum of terms of the form
\eqref{eq:spde-first-chaos-sector-sum}, then, for every
\(\eta>0\),
\begin{equation}
  \left\|
    \delta^{1/2+5\kappa} Z_{\delta,N}^{(1)}
  \right\|_{L^2(\Omega)}
  \leq
  C_\eta\,\delta^{5\kappa-\eta}.
  \label{eq:spde-first-chaos-normalized-log-loss}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For a fixed shift \(r\), the test-function overlap obeys
\begin{equation}
  \int
  |\chi_z^\delta(a)\chi_z^\delta(a')|
  \mathbf 1_{\{\|a-a'-r\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq R2^{-s}\}}
  \,\dd a\,\dd a'
  \leq
  C_\chi\min\{1,\delta^{-Q}2^{-Qs}\}.
  \label{eq:spde-test-overlap-with-shift}
\end{equation}
Indeed, if \(2^{-s}\geq c\delta\), the left side is at most
\(\|\chi_z^\delta\|_{L^1}^2\).  If \(2^{-s}<c\delta\), then for each \(a\)
the allowed \(a'\)-set has volume \(O(2^{-Qs})\), while
\(\|\chi_z^\delta\|_{L^\infty}\leq C\delta^{-Q}\) and
\(\|\chi_z^\delta\|_{L^1}\leq C\).

Insert \eqref{eq:spde-covariance-block-double-increment-bound} into
\eqref{eq:spde-first-chaos-sector-sum}, use
\eqref{eq:spde-local-two-loop-shell-lone-bound} for the \(h\) and \(h'\)
integrals, and then use \eqref{eq:spde-test-overlap-with-shift}.  This gives
\[
  |V_{\delta,N}^{(1)}|
  \leq
  C
  \sum_{s=0}^N
  B_s(\delta)
  \left(
    \sum_{n=0}^N2^{-\theta(n-s)_+}
  \right)^2 ,
\]
where
\[
  B_s(\delta)
  =
  2^s\min\{1,\delta^{-Q}2^{-Qs}\}.
\]
The local two-loop packets are shell-summable but not summable over all
shells; this is exactly why the square of the shell count remains.  Since
\[
  \sum_{n=0}^N2^{-\theta(n-s)_+}
  \leq
  (s+1)+\frac{1}{1-2^{-\theta}}
  \leq
  C_\theta(1+s),
\]
we have
\[
  |V_{\delta,N}^{(1)}|
  \leq
  C
  \sum_{s\geq0}
  B_s(\delta)(1+s)^2 .
\]
Choose \(m\geq0\) such that \(2^{-m-1}<\delta\leq2^{-m}\).  For
\(s\leq m\), \(B_s(\delta)\leq2^s\), hence
\[
  \sum_{s\leq m}B_s(\delta)(1+s)^2
  \leq
  C2^m(1+m)^2
  \leq
  C\delta^{-1}(1+|\log_2\delta|)^2 .
\]
For \(s>m\),
\[
  B_s(\delta)
  \leq
  C2^{Qm}2^{-(Q-1)s}.
\]
Because \(Q-1=4>0\),
\[
  \sum_{s>m}B_s(\delta)(1+s)^2
  \leq
  C2^{Qm}2^{-(Q-1)m}(1+m)^2
  \leq
  C\delta^{-1}(1+|\log_2\delta|)^2 .
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:spde-first-chaos-logarithmic-variance-bound}.

The first-chaos sector is a centered Gaussian variable, so its \(L^2\)-norm
is the square root of its variance.  Multiplying by
\(\delta^{1/2+5\kappa}\) gives
\[
  \left\|
    \delta^{1/2+5\kappa}Z_{\delta,N}^{(1)}
  \right\|_{L^2}
  \leq
  C\delta^{5\kappa}(1+|\log_2\delta|).
\]
For every \(\eta>0\),
\[
  \sup_{0<\delta\leq1}
  \delta^\eta(1+|\log_2\delta|)<\infty ,
\]
which gives \eqref{eq:spde-first-chaos-normalized-log-loss}.
\end{proof}

Together with
Proposition~\ref{prop:spde-x2y-high-chaos-tested-coordinate-bound}, this
identifies the scalar base estimate for the whole locally subtracted
\(X^2Y\) coordinate.  The fifth- and third-chaos pieces have the sharp
\(\delta^{-1}\) variance dictated by target regularity \(-1/2\); only the
first-chaos covariance-increment sector consumes the logarithmic slack that
is recorded in the projective \(X^2Y\) input.

\begin{corollary}[Local \(KG^2\) shell bound in dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\)]
\label{cor:spde-local-kg2-shell-lone-bound}
Let \(Q=5\).  Let \(K_i\), \(i\geq0\), be dyadic heat-kernel pieces of
order \(2\), and let \(G_j\), \(j\geq0\), be dyadic covariance pieces of
order \(4\).  Thus, for a fixed parabolic ball constant \(R\),
with
\[
  \operatorname{supp}K_i\subset B_{\mathfrak s}(0,R2^{-i}),
  \qquad
  \operatorname{supp}G_j\subset B_{\mathfrak s}(0,R2^{-j}),
\]
and
\[
  |K_i(h)|\leq C_K2^{(Q-2)i},\qquad
  |G_j(h)|\leq C_G2^{(Q-4)j}.
\]
For \(n\geq0\), define the local two-loop shell packet
\[
  A_n(h)
  =
  \sum_{\max(i,j,\ell)=n}K_i(h)G_j(h)G_\ell(h).
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
  \int |A_n(h)|\,\dd h
  \leq C
  \label{eq:spde-kg2-shell-lone-bound-verified}
\end{equation}
uniformly in \(n\).  The same estimate holds uniformly in a base point
after translating the kernels, and hence supplies
\eqref{eq:spde-local-two-loop-shell-lone-bound} for the first-chaos
proposition.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
For a single triple \((i,j,\ell)\), set
\[
  n_*=\max(i,j,\ell),\qquad
  r_K=n_*-i,\qquad r_G=n_*-j,\qquad r_{G'}=n_*-\ell .
\]
The product is supported in a ball of radius \(O(2^{-n_*})\).  Therefore
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \int |K_i(h)G_j(h)G_\ell(h)|\,\dd h
  &\leq
  C\,2^{(Q-2)i+(Q-4)j+(Q-4)\ell}2^{-Qn_*}  \\
  &=
  C\,2^{-3r_K-r_G-r_{G'}} .
\end{aligned}
\]
Here the coefficient of \(n_*\) vanishes because
\[
  (Q-2)+(Q-4)+(Q-4)-Q=3+1+1-5=0 .
\]
Summing over the shell \(\max(i,j,\ell)=n\) gives
\[
  \int |A_n(h)|\,\dd h
  \leq
  C
  \sum_{\substack{r_K,r_G,r_{G'}\geq0\\ \min(r_K,r_G,r_{G'})=0}}
  2^{-3r_K-r_G-r_{G'}}
  \leq
  C
  \left(1+\frac{1}{1-2^{-3}}\right)
  \left(\frac{1}{1-2^{-1}}\right)^2 .
\]
This proves the uniform shell \(L^1\) estimate.  Translation of all kernels
does not change either the support radius or the integral bound.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Covariance double increment for compact order-four blocks]
\label{cor:spde-covariance-block-double-increment-bound}
Let \(Q=5\), \(0<\theta\leq1\), and let
\(\mathsf D_\lambda(t,x)=(\lambda^2t,\lambda x)\).  Suppose the dyadic
covariance blocks have the rescaled form
\[
  C_s(a,a')=2^s c_s\bigl(\mathsf D_{2^s}(a-a')\bigr),
  \qquad s\geq0,
\]
where the functions \(c_s\) are supported in a fixed parabolic unit-scale
ball and are bounded uniformly in \(C^2\).  Let \(h,h'\) satisfy
\[
  \|h\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq R_1 2^{-n},
  \qquad
  \|h'\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq R_1 2^{-n'} .
\]
Then there are constants \(A,R\), depending only on \(R_1\), \(\theta\), and
the uniform block bounds, such that
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  |\Delta_{h,h'}C_s(a,a')|
  &\leq
  A\,2^s\,
  2^{-\theta(n-s)_+}
  2^{-\theta(n'-s)_+}                                   \\
  &\quad\times
  \sum_{\rho\in\{0,h\}}\sum_{\rho'\in\{0,h'\}}
  \mathbf 1_{\{\|a+\rho-a'-\rho'\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq R2^{-s}\}} .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-covariance-double-increment-verified}
\end{equation}
In particular the covariance-block hypothesis
\eqref{eq:spde-covariance-block-double-increment-bound} follows for compact
dyadic order-four decompositions of the cutoff covariance.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
  r=\mathsf D_{2^s}(a-a'),\qquad
  u=\mathsf D_{2^s}h,\qquad
  u'=\mathsf D_{2^s}h'.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \Delta_{h,h'}C_s(a,a')
  =
  2^s\{&
  c_s(r+u-u')-c_s(r+u)\\
  &\quad -c_s(r-u')+c_s(r)\}.
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:spde-rescaled-covariance-double-difference}
\end{equation}
The uniform \(C^2\) bound gives the scale-one finite-difference estimate
\begin{equation}
  |c_s(r+u-u')-c_s(r+u)-c_s(r-u')+c_s(r)|
  \leq
  C_\theta
  \min\{1,\|u\|_{\mathfrak s}\}^{\theta}
  \min\{1,\|u'\|_{\mathfrak s}\}^{\theta}.
  \label{eq:spde-scale-one-double-difference}
\end{equation}
Indeed, if \(\|u\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq1\) and
\(\|u'\|_{\mathfrak s}\leq1\), the second-order integral form of the
increment bounds the left side by \(C\|u\|_{\mathfrak s}\|u'\|_{\mathfrak s}\),
which is stronger than \eqref{eq:spde-scale-one-double-difference} because
\(\theta\leq1\).  If only one increment is small, apply the first-order
mean-value bound to the small increment and the triangle inequality in the
other variable.  If both increments are large, the uniform \(C^0\) bound
gives the estimate.

Since
\[
  \|u\|_{\mathfrak s}=2^s\|h\|_{\mathfrak s}
  \leq R_1 2^{s-n},
  \qquad
  \|u'\|_{\mathfrak s}=2^s\|h'\|_{\mathfrak s}
  \leq R_1 2^{s-n'},
\]
we have
\[
  \min\{1,\|u\|_{\mathfrak s}\}^{\theta}
  \leq C_{R_1}2^{-\theta(n-s)_+},
  \qquad
  \min\{1,\|u'\|_{\mathfrak s}\}^{\theta}
  \leq C_{R_1}2^{-\theta(n'-s)_+}.
\]
Combining these estimates with
\eqref{eq:spde-rescaled-covariance-double-difference} gives the numerical
factor in \eqref{eq:spde-covariance-double-increment-verified}.

It remains only to record support.  Each of the four terms in
\eqref{eq:spde-rescaled-covariance-double-difference} vanishes unless the
corresponding separation \(a+\rho-a'-\rho'\), with
\(\rho\in\{0,h\}\) and \(\rho'\in\{0,h'\}\), lies in a fixed parabolic ball
of radius \(O(2^{-s})\).  If all four indicators in
\eqref{eq:spde-covariance-double-increment-verified} vanish, then all four
terms vanish.  Otherwise the indicator sum is at least \(1\), and the
previous numerical bound applies.  Enlarging the support constant gives the
displayed estimate.
\end{proof}

\section{BPHZ Renormalization of the Dynamic Equation}

For the normalization
\[
  \partial_\tau\Phi
  =
  \Delta\Phi-m^2\Phi-\lambda\Phi^3+\xi ,
\]
the parabolic dimension is \(|\mathfrak s|=5\).  A mollified white noise
\(\xi_\epsilon\) is assigned homogeneity
\[
  |\Xi|=-\frac52-\kappa ,
\]
where \(\kappa>0\) is chosen small.  The heat integration map raises
homogeneity by \(2\).  Thus the stochastic convolution symbol
\(X=\mathcal I(\Xi)\) has
\[
  |X|=-\frac12-\kappa ,
  \qquad
  |X^2|=-1-2\kappa ,
  \qquad
  |X^3|=-\frac32-3\kappa .
\]
The one-loop subtraction is already forced by \(X^3\).  The first nonlinear
response \(\mathcal I(X^3)\) has homogeneity
\[
  |\mathcal I(X^3)|=\frac12-3\kappa ,
\]
and the product \(X^2\mathcal I(X^3)\) has
\[
  |X^2\mathcal I(X^3)|=-\frac12-5\kappa .
\]
The next remark records exactly which cubic drift monomials have
negative homogeneity in the first nonlinear expansion.  This finite
drift-level bookkeeping determines the one-loop and two-loop local mass
coordinates in the equation displayed below; the full
regularity-structure construction then adds the model, reexpansion, and
analytic-coordinate estimates for these symbols.

\begin{remark}[Drift-level negative homogeneity bookkeeping]
\label{rem:spde-phi-four-three-negative-drift-bookkeeping}
Let \(0<\kappa<1/14\).  Put
\[
  \alpha=-\frac12-\kappa,\qquad
  \beta=\frac12-3\kappa .
\]
Here \(\alpha\) is the homogeneity of \(X=\mathcal I(\Xi)\) and \(\beta\) is
the homogeneity of the first nonlinear response
\(Y=\mathcal I(X^3)\).  Among the four cubic monomials
\[
  X^3,\qquad X^2Y,\qquad XY^2,\qquad Y^3 ,
\]
the monomials of negative homogeneity are exactly \(X^3\) and \(X^2Y\).
Their homogeneities are
\[
  |X^3|=-\frac32-3\kappa,\qquad
  |X^2Y|=-\frac12-5\kappa .
\]
The remaining two have positive homogeneity:
\[
  |XY^2|=\frac12-7\kappa>0,\qquad
  |Y^3|=\frac32-9\kappa>0 .
\]
Homogeneity is additive under multiplication and is raised by \(2\) under
\(\mathcal I\).  Therefore
\[
  |Y|=|\mathcal I(X^3)|=3\alpha+2=\frac12-3\kappa .
\]
The four cubic monomials in the first nonlinear expansion have homogeneities
\[
\begin{array}{c|c}
  \text{monomial} & \text{homogeneity} \\
  \hline
  X^3 & 3\alpha=-\frac32-3\kappa \\
  X^2Y & 2\alpha+\beta=-\frac12-5\kappa \\
  XY^2 & \alpha+2\beta=\frac12-7\kappa \\
  Y^3 & 3\beta=\frac32-9\kappa .
\end{array}
\]
The first two numbers are negative for every \(\kappa>0\).  The inequality
\(\kappa<1/14\) gives \(1/2-7\kappa>0\), and the weaker inequality
\(\kappa<1/6\) gives \(3/2-9\kappa>0\).  Hence the displayed list contains
all and only the negative cubic drift monomials at this stage.
\end{remark}

The coordinate attached to \(X^3\) is the one-loop Wick contraction
\(C_{1,\epsilon}\).  The coordinate attached to \(X^2\mathcal I(X^3)\) is
the two-loop local contraction \(C_{2,\epsilon}\) after the nested
one-loop subgraph has already been subtracted.

With these conventions, the renormalized cutoff equation in the BPHZ
regularity-structure convention
has the form
\begin{equation}
  \partial_\tau\Phi_\epsilon
  =
  \Delta\Phi_\epsilon-m^2\Phi_\epsilon
  -\lambda\Phi_\epsilon^3
  +
  \bigl(3\lambda C_{1,\epsilon}
        -9\lambda^2 C_{2,\epsilon}
        +c_{\rm fin}\bigr)\Phi_\epsilon
  +\xi_\epsilon .
  \label{eq:phi-four-three-renormalized-spde}
\end{equation}
Here \(C_{1,\epsilon}\) is the one-loop contraction already visible in
\(:\!\Phi^3\!:\), \(C_{2,\epsilon}\) is the two-loop local contraction
arising from the negative tree with two cubic vertices, and \(c_{\rm fin}\)
is the finite mass coordinate.  Different smooth mollifiers or subtraction
schemes change \(C_{1,\epsilon}\), \(C_{2,\epsilon}\), and \(c_{\rm fin}\)
separately, but not the statement that only the local linear drift and
vacuum-energy coordinates are needed in this superrenormalizable model.

\begin{example}[Sharp spatial cutoff one-loop coordinate]
\label{ex:spde-phi-four-three-c1-fourier-growth}
Work on \(\mathbb T^3=(\mathbb R/2\pi\mathbb Z)^3\) with Fourier basis
\[
  e_n(x)=(2\pi)^{-3/2}e^{in\cdot x},\qquad n\in\mathbb Z^3 .
\]
Let \(m>0\), and let \(X_M\) be the stationary solution of the linear
equation
\[
  \partial_\tau X_M=(\Delta-m^2)X_M+\xi_M
\]
obtained by projecting the noise to modes \(|n|_\infty\leq M\), with
normalization
\[
  \mathbb E\,\xi(\tau,x)\xi(\tau',x')
  =
  2\delta(\tau-\tau')\delta(x-x').
\]
Then the one-loop local coordinate is
\begin{equation}
  C_1(M)
  =
  \mathbb E X_M(\tau,x)^2
  =
  (2\pi)^{-3}
  \sum_{\substack{n\in\mathbb Z^3\\ |n|_\infty\leq M}}
  \frac{1}{|n|^2+m^2},
  \label{eq:spde-c1-sharp-fourier-cutoff}
\end{equation}
independent of \((\tau,x)\).  There are constants \(0<c_m<C_m<\infty\)
such that, for all \(M\geq1\),
\[
  C_1(M)\leq C_m(1+M),
\]
and, for all \(M\geq \max(1,\lceil m\rceil)\),
\[
  C_1(M)\geq c_m M .
\]
Consequently, for dyadic cutoffs \(M_N=2^N\),
\[
  0\leq C_1(M_{N+1})-C_1(M_N)\leq C_m'2^N
\]
with \(C_m'<\infty\).
\end{example}

For a fixed Fourier mode \(n\), the linear equation is the
Ornstein--Uhlenbeck equation
\[
  dX_n=-(|n|^2+m^2)X_n\,d\tau+\sqrt2\,dB_n(\tau),
\]
with the real-field constraint \(X_{-n}=\overline{X_n}\).  The stationary
variance is the ratio between the noise variance \(2\) and twice the damping
rate:
\[
  \mathbb E|X_n|^2=\frac{1}{|n|^2+m^2}.
\]
Since \(|e_n(x)|^2=(2\pi)^{-3}\), summing the retained modes gives
\eqref{eq:spde-c1-sharp-fourier-cutoff}.

Let
\[
  S_r=\{n\in\mathbb Z^3:|n|_\infty=r\}.
\]
For \(r\geq1\),
\[
  |S_r|=(2r+1)^3-(2r-1)^3=24r^2+2 .
\]
If \(n\in S_r\), then \(r^2\leq |n|^2\leq3r^2\).  Hence
\[
  \sum_{n\in S_r}\frac{1}{|n|^2+m^2}
  \leq
  \frac{24r^2+2}{r^2}
  \leq 26 .
\]
Adding the zero mode gives the upper bound \(C_1(M)\leq C_m(1+M)\).

For \(r\geq\max(1,\lceil m\rceil)\), the same shell satisfies
\[
  |n|^2+m^2\leq 3r^2+r^2=4r^2 .
\]
Therefore
\[
  \sum_{n\in S_r}\frac{1}{|n|^2+m^2}
  \geq
  \frac{24r^2}{4r^2}
  =
  6 .
\]
Summing these shell lower bounds from
\(\max(1,\lceil m\rceil)\) to \(M\) gives \(C_1(M)\geq c_mM\) after
adjusting \(c_m\) to cover the finite initial range.  The dyadic increment
bound follows from the upper shell estimate applied to
\(M_N<|n|_\infty\leq M_{N+1}\), whose shell radii are
\(M_N+1,\ldots,M_{N+1}\).

\begin{lemma}[Spatial Fourier cutoff two-loop coordinate]
\label{lem:spde-phi-four-three-c2-fourier-log-growth}
Use the notation of
Example~\ref{ex:spde-phi-four-three-c1-fourier-growth}, and put
\[
  a_n=|n|^2+m^2,\qquad n\in\mathbb Z^3 .
\]
Let
\[
  K_M(t,x)
  =
  \mathbf 1_{t>0}(2\pi)^{-3}
  \sum_{\substack{k\in\mathbb Z^3\\ |k|_\infty\leq M}}
  e^{-a_kt}e^{ik\cdot x}
\]
be the retarded heat kernel with the same spatial cutoff, and let
\[
  G_M(t,x)
  =
  (2\pi)^{-3}
  \sum_{\substack{p\in\mathbb Z^3\\ |p|_\infty\leq M}}
  \frac{e^{-a_p|t|}e^{ip\cdot x}}{a_p}
\]
be the stationary covariance.  Define
\begin{equation}
  C_2(M)
  =
  2\int_0^\infty\int_{\mathbb T^3}
  K_M(t,x)G_M(t,x)^2\,\dd x\,\dd t .
  \label{eq:spde-c2-fourier-cutoff-integral}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
  C_2(M)
  =
  2(2\pi)^{-6}
  \sum_{\substack{p,q\in\mathbb Z^3\\
                  |p|_\infty,|q|_\infty,|p+q|_\infty\leq M}}
  \frac{1}{a_pa_q(a_p+a_q+a_{p+q})}.
  \label{eq:spde-c2-fourier-cutoff-sum}
\end{equation}
There are constants \(0<c_m<C_m<\infty\), depending on \(m\) but not on
\(M\), such that
\[
  C_2(M)\leq C_m\bigl(1+\log(1+M)\bigr)
  \qquad(M\geq1),
\]
and
\[
  C_2(M)\geq c_m\log M
  \qquad(M\geq16).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Substituting the Fourier series for \(K_M\) and \(G_M\) into
\eqref{eq:spde-c2-fourier-cutoff-integral} gives
\[
\begin{aligned}
  C_2(M)
  &=
  2(2\pi)^{-9}
  \sum_{\substack{k,p,q\in\mathbb Z^3\\
                  |k|_\infty,|p|_\infty,|q|_\infty\leq M}}
  \frac{1}{a_pa_q}
  \int_0^\infty e^{-(a_k+a_p+a_q)t}\,\dd t
  \int_{\mathbb T^3}e^{i(k+p+q)\cdot x}\,\dd x .
\end{aligned}
\]
The spatial integral is \((2\pi)^3\) when \(k+p+q=0\) and is zero otherwise.
Eliminating \(k\) gives \eqref{eq:spde-c2-fourier-cutoff-sum}.

For the upper bound, discard the restriction \(|p+q|_\infty\leq M\).  Let
\[
  B_0=\{n\in\mathbb Z^3:|n|_\infty<2\},
  \qquad
  B_\ell=\{n\in\mathbb Z^3:2^\ell\leq |n|_\infty<2^{\ell+1}\}
  \quad(\ell\geq1).
\]
There is a constant \(A<\infty\) such that
\[
  |B_\ell|\leq A2^{3\ell}\qquad(\ell\geq0).
\]
For \(\ell\geq1\) this follows from
\[
  |B_\ell|\leq |\{n:|n|_\infty<2^{\ell+1}\}|
  =(2^{\ell+2}-1)^3,
\]
and \(B_0\) is finite.  There is also \(b_m>0\), for instance
\[
  b_m=\min(m^2,1),
\]
such that, for \(n\in B_\ell\),
\[
  a_n\geq b_m2^{2\ell}\qquad(\ell\geq0).
\]
If \(p\in B_\ell\) and \(q\in B_s\), then
\[
  a_p+a_q+a_{p+q}\geq a_p+a_q
  \geq b_m2^{2\max(\ell,s)} .
\]
Thus the contribution of the block \(B_\ell\times B_s\) is bounded by
\[
  C_m
  \frac{2^{3\ell}2^{3s}}
       {2^{2\ell}2^{2s}2^{2\max(\ell,s)}}
  =
  C_m2^{-|\ell-s|}.
\]
If \(|p|_\infty,|q|_\infty\leq M\), then only
\(\ell,s\leq L_M=\lceil\log_2(1+M)\rceil\) occur.  Hence
\[
  C_2(M)
  \leq
  C_m
  \sum_{\ell=0}^{L_M}\sum_{s=0}^{L_M}2^{-|\ell-s|}
  \leq
  3C_m(L_M+1),
\]
which is the stated upper bound after increasing \(C_m\).

For the lower bound, write \(N=\lfloor\log_2M\rfloor\).  For
\(2\leq \ell\leq N-2\), let
\[
  P_\ell
  =
  \{n\in\mathbb Z^3:
    2^\ell\leq n_i<2^\ell+2^{\ell-2},\ i=1,2,3\}.
\]
Then \(|P_\ell|\geq 2^{3\ell-6}\).  If \(p,q\in P_\ell\), then
\[
  |p|_\infty,\ |q|_\infty,\ |p+q|_\infty\leq 2^{\ell+2}\leq M,
\]
and
\[
  a_p,\ a_q,\ a_{p+q}\leq A_m2^{2\ell}
\]
with \(A_m<\infty\) independent of \(\ell\).  The summands in
\eqref{eq:spde-c2-fourier-cutoff-sum} are therefore bounded below by
\(A_m^{-3}2^{-6\ell}\) on \(P_\ell\times P_\ell\).  The contribution of
this block is at least
\[
  2(2\pi)^{-6}|P_\ell|^2A_m^{-3}2^{-6\ell}
  \geq c_m .
\]
Summing the disjoint lower-bound blocks for
\(\ell=2,\ldots,N-2\) gives \(C_2(M)\geq c_m(N-3)\).  Since
there is an absolute constant \(c_0>0\) with
\[
  N-3\geq c_0\log M\qquad(M\geq16),
\]
the lower bound follows after decreasing \(c_m\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Dyadic shell bound for the two-loop coordinate]
\label{prop:spde-phi-four-three-c2-dyadic-shell-bound}
Let \(C_2(M)\) be the sharp spatial Fourier-cutoff two-loop coordinate in
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-phi-four-three-c2-fourier-log-growth}, and set
\[
  M_N=2^N,\qquad N\in\mathbb N .
\]
There is a constant \(C_m^{\rm shell}<\infty\), depending on \(m\) but not
on \(N\), such that, for all \(N\geq2\),
\[
  0\leq C_2(M_{N+1})-C_2(M_N)\leq C_m^{\rm shell}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
  D_N=\{(p,q)\in\mathbb Z^3\times\mathbb Z^3:
       |p|_\infty,|q|_\infty,|p+q|_\infty\leq2^N\}.
\]
The summand in \eqref{eq:spde-c2-fourier-cutoff-sum} is non-negative, and
\(D_N\subset D_{N+1}\), so the increment is non-negative.

Use the dyadic annuli \(B_\ell\) from the proof of
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-phi-four-three-c2-fourier-log-growth}.  The same
block estimate gives a constant \(A_m<\infty\) such that, for every
\(\ell,s\geq0\), the contribution of
\[
  (B_\ell\times B_s)\cap D_{N+1}
\]
to \(C_2(M_{N+1})\) is bounded by
\[
  A_m2^{-|\ell-s|}.
\]
If \((p,q)\in D_{N+1}\setminus D_N\) and
\[
  p\in B_\ell,\qquad q\in B_s,
\]
then \(\ell,s\leq N+1\).  Moreover, \(\max(\ell,s)\geq N-1\).  Indeed, if
\(\ell,s\leq N-2\), then
\[
  |p|_\infty<2^{N-1},\qquad |q|_\infty<2^{N-1},
\]
hence \(|p+q|_\infty<2^N\), so \((p,q)\in D_N\), a contradiction.
Therefore
\[
\begin{aligned}
  C_2(M_{N+1})-C_2(M_N)
  &\leq
  A_m
  \sum_{\substack{0\leq\ell,s\leq N+1\\
                  \max(\ell,s)\geq N-1}}
  2^{-|\ell-s|}                                      \\
  &\leq
  A_m\sum_{t=N-1}^{N+1}
  \left(1+2\sum_{r=0}^{t-1}2^{-(t-r)}\right)          \\
  &\leq
  9A_m .
\end{aligned}
\]
Thus \(C_m^{\rm shell}=9A_m\) is admissible.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Finite-cutoff local counterterm calculation.}
\label{par:spde-phi-four-three-local-counterterm-calculation}
Let \(X_\epsilon\) be the smooth stationary Gaussian solution of the
linearized cutoff equation and write
\[
  G_\epsilon(z,w)
  =
  \mathbb E\bigl[X_\epsilon(z)X_\epsilon(w)\bigr].
\]
Let \(K_\epsilon\) denote the retarded heat kernel with the same ultraviolet
mollification and define the local constants
\begin{equation}
  C_{1,\epsilon}=G_\epsilon(z,z),
  \qquad
  C_{2,\epsilon}
  =
  2\int K_\epsilon(z,w)G_\epsilon(z,w)^2\,\dd w ,
  \label{eq:spde-c1-c2-local-definitions}
\end{equation}
where translation invariance on the spacetime torus makes the right-hand
sides independent of \(z\).  Consider the perturbative fixed-point expansion
\[
  \Phi_\epsilon
  =
  X_\epsilon
  -
  \lambda K_\epsilon(X_\epsilon^3)
  +O(\lambda^2),
\]
and let \(\mathcal L\) denote the projection that retains only the local
linear part produced by Wick contractions and the zeroth Taylor coefficient
of the remaining field at \(w=z\).  Then
\[
  \mathcal L\!\left[-\lambda X_\epsilon^3
  +3\lambda^2X_\epsilon^2K_\epsilon(X_\epsilon^3)\right]
  =
  \bigl(-3\lambda C_{1,\epsilon}
        +9\lambda^2C_{2,\epsilon}\bigr)X_\epsilon .
\]
Consequently the counterterm inserted in the cutoff drift is the negative of
this local singular part, namely
\[
  \bigl(3\lambda C_{1,\epsilon}
        -9\lambda^2C_{2,\epsilon}\bigr)\Phi_\epsilon ,
\]
up to the independent finite mass coordinate \(c_{\rm fin}\Phi_\epsilon\).

The one-loop term is the Wick contraction of two of the three fields in
\(X_\epsilon^3\):
\[
  X_\epsilon(z)^3
  =
  :\!X_\epsilon(z)^3\!:
  +3G_\epsilon(z,z)X_\epsilon(z).
\]
Thus
\[
  \mathcal L[-\lambda X_\epsilon^3]
  =
  -3\lambda C_{1,\epsilon}X_\epsilon .
\]

For the two-loop term, expand the nonlinearity to first order in the
nonlinear response:
\[
  -\lambda\Phi_\epsilon^3
  =
  -\lambda X_\epsilon^3
  +3\lambda^2X_\epsilon^2K_\epsilon(X_\epsilon^3)
  +O(\lambda^3).
\]
The coefficient \(3\) is the number of choices for the factor of
\(\Phi_\epsilon\) in \(\Phi_\epsilon^3\) that is replaced by
\(-\lambda K_\epsilon(X_\epsilon^3)\); the two minus signs give the positive
sign in the displayed term.  At a spacetime point \(z\),
\[
  X_\epsilon(z)^2K_\epsilon(X_\epsilon^3)(z)
  =
  \int K_\epsilon(z,w)
  X_\epsilon(z)^2X_\epsilon(w)^3\,\dd w .
\]
Its local linear part is obtained by contracting four of the five Gaussian
fields and replacing the remaining field at \(w\) by its zeroth Taylor term
at \(z\).  There are two possible forms of such contractions.

First leave one of the three \(X_\epsilon(w)\) factors uncontracted and
contract the two \(X_\epsilon(z)\) factors with the two remaining
\(X_\epsilon(w)\) factors.  This gives \(3\cdot2=6\) pairings and contributes
\[
  6
  \int K_\epsilon(z,w)G_\epsilon(z,w)^2\,\dd w\;X_\epsilon(z)
  =
  3C_{2,\epsilon}X_\epsilon(z).
\]
Second leave one of the two \(X_\epsilon(z)\) factors uncontracted, contract
the other \(X_\epsilon(z)\) with one of the three \(X_\epsilon(w)\) factors,
and contract the remaining two \(X_\epsilon(w)\) factors with each other.
This produces
\[
  6
  \int K_\epsilon(z,w)G_\epsilon(z,w)G_\epsilon(w,w)\,\dd w\;X_\epsilon(z).
\]
This is the one-loop tadpole inserted into the inner cubic vertex.  The
finite-cutoff forest subtraction used here is the following recursive local
operation: before extracting the new local part of a graph, replace every
proper divergent subgraph by its already computed local counterterm.  For the
present tree this means replacing the inner \(X_\epsilon(w)^3\) by its
one-loop Wick-ordered cubic, so the displayed nested tadpole is removed
before the two-loop coordinate is defined.  Therefore the new two-loop local
coordinate is the first contribution only, with the normalization in
\eqref{eq:spde-c1-c2-local-definitions}.  Multiplying by the outer factor
\(3\lambda^2\) gives
\[
  \mathcal L[3\lambda^2X_\epsilon^2K_\epsilon(X_\epsilon^3)]
  =
  9\lambda^2C_{2,\epsilon}X_\epsilon .
\]
Combining the one-loop and two-loop local parts proves the displayed
formula.  The finite coordinate \(c_{\rm fin}\) is not fixed by singular
subtraction; it labels the chosen renormalized mass coordinate.

\begin{theorem}[Abstract local fixed point in modelled distributions]
\label{thm:spde-abstract-modelled-fixed-point}
Let \(0<T\leq1\).  Let \(E_T\) be a Banach space of modelled distributions
on the parabolic time slab \([0,T]\times\mathbb T^3\), let \(F_T\) be a
Banach space of modelled distributional forcing terms on the same slab, and
assume the following data and estimates.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item A zero-initial-time abstract heat integration operator
  \(\mathcal K_T:F_T\to E_T\) satisfies, for constants \(A>0\) and
  \(\theta>0\),
  \begin{equation}
    \|\mathcal K_T H\|_{E_T}
    \leq
    A T^\theta \|H\|_{F_T}.
    \label{eq:spde-abstract-schauder-small-time}
  \end{equation}
  The power \(T^\theta\) encodes the positive time gain obtained after the
  singular local model has been fixed.
  \item A reconstructed stochastic convolution \(X_T\in E_T\) and an
  initial-data lift \(P_Tu_0\in E_T\) are given.  Put
  \[
    R_0=\|P_Tu_0+X_T\|_{E_T}.
  \]
  \item The cubic product is a locally Lipschitz map \(E_T\to F_T\):
  for a constant \(B>0\),
  \[
    \|U^3\|_{F_T}\leq B\|U\|_{E_T}^3,
  \]
  and
  \begin{equation}
    \|U^3-V^3\|_{F_T}
    \leq
    B(\|U\|_{E_T}^2+\|V\|_{E_T}^2)\|U-V\|_{E_T}.
    \label{eq:spde-cubic-modelled-lipschitz}
  \end{equation}
  \item The local linear term is bounded as a map \(E_T\to F_T\):
  \[
    \|U\|_{F_T}\leq D\|U\|_{E_T}
  \]
  for a constant \(D>0\).
\end{enumerate}
Fix real parameters \(\lambda\) and \(M\).  Define
\begin{equation}
  \Psi_T(U)
  =
  P_Tu_0+X_T
  +
  \mathcal K_T\bigl(-\lambda U^3+MU\bigr).
  \label{eq:spde-modelled-fixed-point-map}
\end{equation}
Let \(R=2R_0\).  If
\begin{align}
  A T^\theta\bigl(B|\lambda|R^3+D|M|R\bigr)
  &\leq \frac{R}{2},
  \label{eq:spde-fixed-point-ball-condition}\\
  A T^\theta\bigl(2B|\lambda|R^2+D|M|\bigr)
  &<1,
  \label{eq:spde-fixed-point-contraction-condition}
\end{align}
then \(\Psi_T\) has a unique fixed point in the closed ball
\[
  \mathbb B_R=\{U\in E_T:\|U\|_{E_T}\leq R\}.
\]
The fixed point depends Lipschitz-continuously on \(P_Tu_0+X_T\) as long as
the same constants and the same ball are used.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For \(U\in\mathbb B_R\), the Schauder estimate
\eqref{eq:spde-abstract-schauder-small-time}, the cubic bound, and the
linear bound give
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \|\Psi_T(U)\|_{E_T}
  &\leq
  R_0
  +
  A T^\theta
  \bigl(|\lambda|\|U^3\|_{F_T}+|M|\|U\|_{F_T}\bigr)\\
  &\leq
  \frac{R}{2}
  +
  A T^\theta
  \bigl(B|\lambda|R^3+D|M|R\bigr)
  \leq R .
\end{aligned}
\]
Thus \(\Psi_T\) maps \(\mathbb B_R\) into itself.  For
\(U,V\in\mathbb B_R\), the Lipschitz estimate
\eqref{eq:spde-cubic-modelled-lipschitz} gives
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \|\Psi_T(U)-\Psi_T(V)\|_{E_T}
  &\leq
  A T^\theta
  \left(
    |\lambda|\|U^3-V^3\|_{F_T}
    +|M|\|U-V\|_{F_T}
  \right)\\
  &\leq
  A T^\theta
  \bigl(2B|\lambda|R^2+D|M|\bigr)\|U-V\|_{E_T}.
\end{aligned}
\]
Condition~\eqref{eq:spde-fixed-point-contraction-condition} makes this
Lipschitz constant strictly smaller than one; call it \(q\).  Choose
\(U_0\in\mathbb B_R\) and set \(U_{n+1}=\Psi_T(U_n)\).  Since
\(\Psi_T(\mathbb B_R)\subset\mathbb B_R\),
\[
  \|U_{n+1}-U_n\|_{E_T}
  \leq
  q^n\|U_1-U_0\|_{E_T}.
\]
For \(m>n\),
\[
  \|U_m-U_n\|_{E_T}
  \leq
  \sum_{j=n}^{m-1}q^j\|U_1-U_0\|_{E_T}
  \leq
  \frac{q^n}{1-q}\|U_1-U_0\|_{E_T}.
\]
The space \(E_T\) is complete, so \(U_n\) converges to some
\(U_\ast\in\mathbb B_R\).  Continuity of \(\Psi_T\) gives
\(\Psi_T(U_\ast)=U_\ast\).  If \(V_\ast\) is another fixed point in
\(\mathbb B_R\), then
\[
  \|U_\ast-V_\ast\|_{E_T}
  \leq
  q\|U_\ast-V_\ast\|_{E_T},
\]
and \(q<1\) forces \(U_\ast=V_\ast\).

For dependence on the inhomogeneous term, let \(Y=P_Tu_0+X_T\) and
\(\widetilde Y=\widetilde P_T\widetilde u_0+\widetilde X_T\), and suppose
the two corresponding fixed points \(U,\widetilde U\) lie in the same ball
\(\mathbb B_R\).  The same estimate gives
\[
  \|U-\widetilde U\|_{E_T}
  \leq
  \|Y-\widetilde Y\|_{E_T}
  +
  q\|U-\widetilde U\|_{E_T},
  \qquad
  q=A T^\theta(2B|\lambda|R^2+D|M|)<1.
\]
Therefore
\[
  \|U-\widetilde U\|_{E_T}
  \leq
  \frac{1}{1-q}\|Y-\widetilde Y\|_{E_T}.
\]
\end{proof}

In the dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\) application, \(E_T\) is a weighted
modelled-distribution space whose lowest components encode the stochastic
convolution and whose positive components encode the unknown remainder.
The space \(F_T\) is the corresponding forcing space after subtracting the
singular local parts of the cubic.  The operator \(\mathcal K_T\) is the
abstract heat integration map, and
\[
  M=3\lambda C_{1,\epsilon}-9\lambda^2C_{2,\epsilon}+c_{\rm fin}
\]
in the finite-cutoff equation before passing to the renormalized model.  The
theorem proves the fixed-point step once the model bounds, product bounds,
and Schauder bound have been established.  It does not prove convergence of
the BPHZ-renormalized models; that remains a separate stochastic estimate.

\begin{quotedtheorem}[Renormalized dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\) theorem package]
\label{thm:renormalized-phi-four-three-spde-datum}
Let the spatial manifold be a finite three-dimensional torus, let
\(\xi_\epsilon=\rho_\epsilon\ast\xi\) be a smooth space-time mollification
of white noise, and fix the normalization of
\eqref{eq:phi-four-three-renormalized-spde}.  In the BPHZ
regularity-structure chart there are local constants
\(C_{1,\epsilon}\), \(C_{2,\epsilon}\), and a finite mass coordinate
\(c_{\rm fin}\), such that the following statements hold.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item For each fixed \(\epsilon>0\) and smooth initial field, the cutoff
  equation \eqref{eq:phi-four-three-renormalized-spde} has a unique smooth
  local solution.  The solution map is Markovian and depends continuously on
  the initial field and on the smooth noise.
  \item After enhancing the mollified noise by its BPHZ-renormalized negative
  trees, the cutoff solutions converge in probability, on compact
  stochastic-time intervals before explosion and in negative spatial Holder
  or Besov topologies, to a limit independent of the mollifier up to finite
  local coordinate changes.
  \item The positive quartic drift, together with the renormalized mass
  coordinate, gives global solutions and invariant probability measures for
  the limiting Markov process in the massive phase.  Starting the cutoff
  equation in its finite-cutoff Gibbs law gives stationary solutions, and
  every limiting stationary law is invariant for the limiting Markov
  semigroup.
  \item In a common finite-volume regulator and renormalization chart, this
  invariant law has the same Schwinger moments as the constructive
  \(\Phi^4_3\) Euclidean measure with the same renormalized mass coordinate.
  Equivalently, after the field and mass normalizations are matched, the
  SPDE stationary construction and the constructive Euclidean construction
  determine the same OS input hierarchy.
\end{enumerate}
\end{quotedtheorem}

This renormalized \(\Phi^4_3\) SPDE theorem is a quoted theorem-boundary for
the regularity-structures construction, not a proof completed here.  The
quoted source lineage is Hairer's regularity-structures construction and the
Hairer--Mourrat--Weber treatments of dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\) renormalization.
The four clauses are logically distinct.  Local cutoff well-posedness is an
ordinary smooth parabolic theorem.  Renormalized convergence is the singular
SPDE theorem: one first builds the canonical model from the mollified noise;
its negative tree components diverge as \(\epsilon\downarrow0\); the BPHZ
character subtracts the expectations of all divergent negative subtrees,
producing a renormalized model satisfying uniform analytic bounds; compactness
and Kolmogorov estimates then give convergence of the model.

After the renormalized model has been constructed, the local fixed-point
step has the form proved in
Theorem~\ref{thm:spde-abstract-modelled-fixed-point}.  The missing analytic
input is the verification, for the actual BPHZ model, of the Schauder,
product, and small-time estimates used in that theorem.  Reconstructing the
fixed point then gives the distribution-valued solution by
Theorem~\ref{thm:spde-compact-reconstruction}.  The explicit local term in
\eqref{eq:phi-four-three-renormalized-spde} is the image, in the concrete
equation, of the BPHZ action on the negative trees.  Invariant measures are
identified by finite-cutoff stationarity, tightness, and convergence of
stationary solutions.  Identification with the constructive Euclidean
\(\Phi^4_3\) measure is still another step: both constructions must be placed
in the same finite-volume cutoff chart, the mass and field coordinates must be
matched, and equality of the limiting Schwinger moments must be proved.  Each
sentence in this paragraph names a theorem-level estimate; none is to be
treated as proved merely by being quoted.

The proof boundary has narrowed.
For the \(\Phi^4_2\) equation, the construction of the stochastic
convolution and its Wick powers, the path-space enhanced-noise convergence,
the Sobolev and Besov local DPD maps, the smooth energy estimate, the
compactness and closedness steps for smooth approximants, the regulator
comparison criteria, and the abstract SPDE-to-OS reconstruction criterion
have been proved above.  The remaining two-dimensional work is not a generic
appeal to the Da Prato--Debussche theorem.  It consists of specific
constructive estimates: the local rough-forcing estimate in
\eqref{eq:spde-local-rough-forcing-estimate}, Nelson stability for the
chosen Wick quartic cutoff family, and the moment-continuity, positive-time
semigroup regularity, and corrected OS-II growth estimates needed by
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-invariant-law-os-reconstruction-criterion}.

For dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\), the self-contained proof boundary is still larger.
The finite negative sector, its homogeneity bookkeeping, its reexpansion
coordinates, and the scale-summed criterion that would imply convergence of
that sector have been proved in
Lemma~\ref{lem:spde-phi-four-three-negative-sector-coordinate-chart}
and
the negative-sector coordinate-control consequence.
What remains is to prove, for the actual BPHZ-renormalized model, the
coordinate estimates required by that scale-summed criterion for
\[
  \Xi,\quad X,\quad X^2,\quad X^3,\quad XY,\quad X^2Y,
  \quad\text{and}\quad c_n(z,z'),
\]
including both uniform model-seminorm moments and dyadic cutoff-increment
moments with enough scale and parameter slack.  One must then extend the
negative-sector convergence to the full modelled-distribution space used by
the fixed point, prove the Schauder and multiplication estimates for the
concrete model, identify the BPHZ counterterms with the local constants in
\eqref{eq:phi-four-three-renormalized-spde}, and compare the stationary SPDE
law with the Euclidean constructive measure.
\footnote{See G.~Da Prato and A.~Debussche, ``Strong solutions to the
stochastic quantization equations,'' \emph{Ann. Probab.} 31 (2003);
M.~Hairer, ``A theory of regularity structures,'' \emph{Invent. Math.} 198
(2014); and the Hairer--Mourrat--Weber regularity-structures treatment of
\(\Phi^4_3\) renormalization.  For recent singular-SPDE work in gauge
contexts, see A.~Chandra, I.~Chevyrev, M.~Hairer, and H.~Shen, ``Stochastic
quantisation of Yang--Mills,'' Invent. Math. \textbf{230} (2022)
1025--1096.}
The cited works identify deeper analytic machinery that remains to be
reconstructed in this monograph; citation supplies orientation, while the
proof obligations remain the estimates just listed.

\begin{openproblem}[Remaining self-contained singular-SPDE proof stack]
\label{op:self-contained-singular-spde-proof-stack}
Complete the proof stack left open by the preceding analysis.  The
two-dimensional part requires: a proof of the rough-forcing estimate
\eqref{eq:spde-local-rough-forcing-estimate} for the Wick-enhanced
\(\Phi^4_2\) stochastic convolution; a direct Nelson stability theorem, or a
fully controlled comparison with a regulator for which Nelson stability has
been proved, for the cutoff family used in the stochastic assembly; and the
OS reconstruction inputs listed in
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-invariant-law-os-reconstruction-criterion}.

The three-dimensional part requires: construction of the BPHZ-renormalized
dynamic \(\Phi^4_3\) model; proof of the coordinate moment and cutoff-Cauchy
estimates in
the negative-sector coordinate-control consequence;
extension of those estimates from the strict negative sector to the full
sector used in the fixed-point problem; verification that the concrete BPHZ
model satisfies the Schauder and product estimates required by
Theorem~\ref{thm:spde-abstract-modelled-fixed-point}; derivation of the
local counterterms \(C_{1,\epsilon}\), \(C_{2,\epsilon}\), and
\(c_{\rm fin}\) from the BPHZ character in the convention of
\eqref{eq:phi-four-three-renormalized-spde}; invariant-law construction and
comparison with the constructive Euclidean \(\Phi^4_3\) measure; and the
SPDE-to-OS reconstruction inputs for the resulting Schwinger hierarchy.
Until these arguments are supplied, the remaining quoted theorem boundary is
a documented proof boundary rather than an authority claim.
\end{openproblem}

\section{Paracontrolled and RG Routes}

Regularity structures are not the only analytic language for singular SPDE.
Paracontrolled distributions decompose products using Bony's paraproduct
\[
  fg=f\prec g+f\circ g+f\succ g,
\]
and control the resonant product \(f\circ g\) by enhancing the noise with the
few ill-defined resonant objects needed by the equation.  For \(\Phi^4_3\),
this route uses the same local counterterm content as
\eqref{eq:phi-four-three-renormalized-spde}, expressed in Fourier/Besov
language rather than in a tree Hopf algebra.

Kupiainen-style RG treats the stochastic convolution and nonlinear response
by scale integration.  It is closer in form to the constructive RG of
Chapter~\ref{ch:constructive-rigorous-renormalization-group}.  The common
structure is that no finite truncation of diagrams is being trusted by
itself: the theorem estimates the infinite irrelevant tail in a norm and
shows convergence of the renormalized limit.

\section{Invariant Measure and OS Data}

If the renormalized Markov process exists and is ergodic with invariant
measure \(\mu\), the Euclidean Schwinger functions are
\begin{equation}
  S_n(f_1,\ldots,f_n)
  =
  \int \Phi(f_1)\cdots\Phi(f_n)\,\dd\mu(\Phi).
  \label{eq:spde-invariant-measure-schwinger}
\end{equation}
A complete QFT construction must verify:
\[
\begin{gathered}
  \text{Euclidean covariance},\qquad
  \text{reflection positivity},\\
  \text{regularity and OS growth bounds},\qquad
  \text{clustering or phase decomposition}.
\end{gathered}
\]
Stochastic quantization is especially powerful because it gives a dynamic
construction of the measure and a precise algebraic account of stochastic
counterterms.  Reflection positivity, however, is a property of the
Euclidean field measure under physical time reflection; it is not automatic
from Markov positivity in the auxiliary stochastic time.

\begin{remark}[SPDE invariant law as an OS reconstruction input]
\label{rem:spde-invariant-law-os-reconstruction-criterion}
Let \(E=\mathcal S'(\R^d)\) be the real tempered-distribution space,
equipped with its Borel \(\sigma\)-algebra, and let \(\mu\) be a probability
measure on \(E\).  For \(f\in\mathcal S(\R^d)\) write
\(\Phi(f)(\varphi)=\varphi(f)\).  Suppose that the following conditions
hold.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item For every \(n\geq0\), the multilinear functional initially defined on
  finite tensor sums by
  \[
    S_n\!\left(\sum_a c_a f_{a,1}\otimes\cdots\otimes f_{a,n}\right)
    =
    \sum_a c_a
    \int_E
      \Phi(f_{a,1})\cdots\Phi(f_{a,n})\,\dd\mu(\Phi)
  \]
  is well-defined and obeys a Schwartz-seminorm estimate
  \begin{equation}
    |S_n(F)|\leq C_n\,q_{n,N_n}(F),
    \qquad F\in \mathcal S((\R^d)^n),
    \label{eq:spde-os-moment-continuity}
  \end{equation}
  after extending from finite tensor sums.  Here \(q_{n,N}\) is any fixed
  increasing defining family of Schwartz seminorms on
  \(\mathcal S((\R^d)^n)\).  Equivalently, \(\mu\) has enough polynomial
  cylinder moments, with enough seminorm continuity, to make each \(S_n\) a
  tempered Euclidean distribution.
  \item The hierarchy \(\{S_n\}\) is normalized, Euclidean covariant,
  permutation symmetric, and Hermitian in the sense of
  Definition~\ref{def:os-admissible-euclidean-data}.  In a scalar real
  theory these conditions follow from \(S_0=1\), invariance of \(\mu\) under
  the Euclidean group action on \(E\), and reality of the field coordinates;
  for labelled or graded fields the label reflection and Koszul signs must
  be part of the declared field presentation.
  \item Let \(\Theta\) denote physical Euclidean time reflection.  For every
  polynomial cylinder observable
  \[
    F(\Phi)=
    \sum_a c_a\,\Phi(f_{a,1})\cdots\Phi(f_{a,r_a})
  \]
  whose test functions are supported in the positive-time half-space,
  \begin{equation}
    \int_E \overline{F(\Theta\Phi)}\,F(\Phi)\,\dd\mu(\Phi)\geq0 .
    \label{eq:spde-os-cylinder-positivity}
  \end{equation}
  If this inequality is first proved only for bounded cylinder functions,
  then the passage to polynomial cylinders must be justified by the uniform
  integrability or truncation estimates appropriate to the cutoff limit.
  \item The positive-time translation operators on the OS quotient satisfy
  the semigroup law, symmetry, and strong-continuity hypotheses
  \eqref{eq:os-time-semigroup-law}--\eqref{eq:os-time-strong-continuity}.
  \item The translation-reduced hierarchy satisfies the corrected OS-II
  linear-growth estimate \eqref{eq:os-linear-growth-condition};
  explicitly, for some \(A,B,\gamma>0\) and integers \(N_0,C_{\rm OS}\),
  \[
    |S_n^{\rm red}(F)|
    \leq
    A\,B^n\,(n!)^\gamma\,
    q_{n,N_0+C_{\rm OS}n}(F)
  \]
  on the zero-diagonal reduced Schwartz test space of
  Chapter~\ref{ch:os-reconstruction}.
\end{enumerate}
Then the Schwinger hierarchy obtained from \(\mu\) satisfies the hypotheses
of Theorem~\ref{thm:os-reconstruction}.  Consequently it reconstructs
Lorentzian Wightman field data whose Euclidean time-ordered boundary values
recover the Schwinger functions at noncoincident Euclidean configurations.
If the hierarchy is clustering in the sense of
Corollary~\ref{cor:os-reconstruction-vacuum-sector}, the reconstructed vacuum is
unique; without clustering one obtains the corresponding phase-decomposed
Wightman presentation.
Condition (i) is the distributional regularity step.  Finite tensor sums are
dense in the Schwartz tensor product, and the estimate
\eqref{eq:spde-os-moment-continuity} makes the cylinder moment functional
continuous for the Schwartz topology.  Thus each \(S_n\) extends uniquely to
a tempered distribution on \((\R^d)^n\).

Condition (ii) gives normalization, Euclidean covariance, permutation
symmetry, and Hermiticity.  Condition (iii) is exactly OS reflection
positivity on the positive-time polynomial cylinder algebra; the warning in
the second sentence records the point used repeatedly above, namely that
polynomial OS positivity cannot be read off from bounded-cylinder positivity
without a tail estimate.  Conditions (iv) and (v) are the corrected analytic
inputs emphasized in Chapter~\ref{ch:os-reconstruction}: reflection
positivity constructs the Hilbert space and positive Hamiltonian, while the
OS-II semigroup and linear-growth package supplies the many-variable
Fourier--Laplace continuation with tempered Lorentzian boundary values.

All hypotheses of Theorem~\ref{thm:os-reconstruction} are therefore present.
Applying that theorem gives
\[
  (\Hilb_{\rm OS},\vac_{\rm OS},U,\mathcal D_{\rm OS},
  \{\widehat\Phi_\alpha\})
\]
and the Wightman distributions obtained as boundary values of the analytic
continuations of the \(S_n\).  The clustering statement is precisely
Corollary~\ref{cor:os-reconstruction-vacuum-sector}.
\end{remark}

In stochastic quantization the preceding remark is a checklist, not an automatic
corollary of stationarity.  The Markov invariant law supplies a candidate
\(\mu\).  The constructive proof must still establish moment continuity,
physical-time reflection positivity, the OS-II positive-time semigroup
regularity, and the corrected linear-growth estimate.  For \(\Phi^4_2\) and
\(\Phi^4_3\), these conditions should ultimately be verified by comparing
the SPDE invariant law with the corresponding constructive Euclidean measure
in a common renormalization chart, because the constructive measure is where
reflection positivity and OS growth are naturally controlled.

\begin{construction}[Common Schwinger-hierarchy comparison]
\label{con:spde-common-schwinger-hierarchy-comparison}
Let
\[
  E=\mathcal S'(\R^d)
\]
with its cylinder \(\sigma\)-algebra.  Let \(\mu_{\rm spde}\) be a candidate
stationary law produced by a renormalized stochastic quantization construction,
and let \(\mu_{\rm cons}\) be a constructive Euclidean measure in the same
finite-volume, field-normalization, mass-coordinate, and local-counterterm
chart.  For \(f\in\mathcal S(\R^d)\), write
\[
  \Phi(f)(\varphi)=\varphi(f).
\]
The comparison datum needed for OS reconstruction is the equality of
Schwinger hierarchies, not equality of auxiliary stochastic processes.  A
precise sufficient datum is the following.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item For each \(n\), both moment functionals
  \[
    S_n^{\rm spde}(f_1,\ldots,f_n)
    =
    \int_E\prod_{j=1}^n\Phi(f_j)\,\dd\mu_{\rm spde}(\Phi),
    \qquad
    S_n^{\rm cons}(f_1,\ldots,f_n)
    =
    \int_E\prod_{j=1}^n\Phi(f_j)\,\dd\mu_{\rm cons}(\Phi)
  \]
  extend continuously to \(\mathcal S((\R^d)^n)\), with declared Schwartz
  seminorm bounds
  \[
    |S_n^\bullet(F)|\leq C_n^\bullet q_{n,N_n^\bullet}(F),
    \qquad \bullet\in\{{\rm spde},{\rm cons}\}.
  \]
  \item There is a dense linear subspace \(\mathcal D\subset\mathcal S(\R^d)\)
  such that
  \[
    S_n^{\rm spde}(f_1,\ldots,f_n)
    =
    S_n^{\rm cons}(f_1,\ldots,f_n),
    \qquad f_j\in\mathcal D,
  \]
  for every \(n\).  In applications \(\mathcal D\) is often generated by the
  test functions used by the two regulator families, after matching the field
  and mass coordinates.
  \item The constructive hierarchy \(S_\bullet^{\rm cons}\) satisfies the OS
  normalization, Euclidean covariance, symmetry, Hermiticity, polynomial
  reflection positivity, positive-time semigroup regularity, corrected OS-II
  linear growth, and any declared clustering or phase-decomposition
  hypothesis.
\end{enumerate}
Then the SPDE hierarchy and the constructive hierarchy coincide as tempered
Schwinger distributions.  Indeed, finite sums of tensors
\(f_1\otimes\cdots\otimes f_n\) with \(f_j\in\mathcal D\) are dense in
\(\mathcal S((\R^d)^n)\).  The difference
\[
  S_n^{\rm spde}-S_n^{\rm cons}
\]
is continuous by (i) and vanishes on that dense tensor subspace by (ii), hence
vanishes on all of \(\mathcal S((\R^d)^n)\).  Every OS quadratic form is a
finite linear combination of these distributions evaluated on reflected
positive-time tensor products.  Reflection positivity, covariance, symmetry,
Hermiticity, the semigroup regularity inputs, the corrected OS-II growth bound,
and clustering therefore transfer from \(S_\bullet^{\rm cons}\) to
\(S_\bullet^{\rm spde}\) with the same constants after replacing the seminorm
family by a common dominating family.

Consequently the OS reconstruction of the SPDE hierarchy is canonically
identified with the OS reconstruction of the constructive hierarchy: the
positive-time polynomial pre-Hilbert inner products are identical, the null
spaces are identical, and the completed Hilbert spaces and reconstructed
Wightman distributions agree under the induced unitary identification.  If
the comparison is first proved only for bounded cylinder functions, the
bounded-to-polynomial passage must use the uniform-integrability and
truncation criteria proved above; bounded-cylinder equality by itself supplies
only the bounded part of the comparison datum.  Equality of probability laws
is a stronger route to the same conclusion when a moment-determinacy theorem is
available, but OS reconstruction uses the Schwinger hierarchy itself as its
input.
\end{construction}

\begin{remark}[Gauge theories and BV compatibility]
\label{rem:spde-gauge-bv-compatibility}
For gauge theories, stochastic quantization must be reconciled with gauge
symmetry, gauge fixing, and the BV master equation.  A stochastic evolution
for gauge potentials before quotienting is not by itself a construction of a
gauge-invariant local QFT.  The constructive target is a measure or
observable theory for gauge-invariant fields, or a gauge-fixed/BV
construction whose quantum master equation and positivity replacement are
controlled.  Two- and three-dimensional Yang--Mills SPDE programs provide
important laboratories; four-dimensional Yang--Mills remains a separate open
problem.
\end{remark}

\begin{openproblem}[SPDE-to-Wightman construction]
\label{op:spde-to-wightman-construction}
Starting from a renormalized singular SPDE construction of an interacting
Euclidean field, prove the inputs of
Remark~\ref{rem:spde-invariant-law-os-reconstruction-criterion},
identify the resulting Wightman distributions, and compare the stochastic
counterterms with Wilsonian local coordinates in a common renormalization
chart.
\end{openproblem}
